Minority (Ṣighr) as an Impediment to Legal Capacity
Commentary on rulings of ṣighr in legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that minority lifts responsibility for harmful acts but not for beneficial acts, and distinguish between the initial and discerning stages of minority.

Core Idea
Minority lifts obligation for harmful acts; beneficial acts remain valid.

In Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh, legal capacity (ahliyya) is affected by certain impediments (awārid). One of the most important is minority (ṣighr). This lesson explains how minority impacts a person's capacity to be bound by obligations and the validity of his actions, based on the commentary from the source text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two stages of minority
The passage distinguishes between the initial state (pre-discernment) where the minor lacks all discrimination and the discerning state (mumayyiz) where he acquires deficient capacity (ahliyya qāṣira).
The initial state is compared to insanity, but even more deficient.
2
Understand the effect on obligations
All obligations that can be dropped (like prayer, fasting, hudud) are lifted from the minor due to the excuse of minority. Actions that cannot be dropped (like faith) remain valid if performed.
The hadith on mercy supports this leniency.
3
Distinguish beneficial vs harmful acts
Acts that are harmless (e.g., accepting gifts, charity) are valid whether done by the minor or his guardian. Harms acts (e.g., divorce, manumission) are not binding on the minor.
This is based on the principle that minority is a cause of mercy.
4
Apply the rule to inheritance
If a minor kills his ancestor, he is not deprived of inheritance because the offence can be pardoned. But a minor who is a slave or apostate is deprived not as punishment but due to lack of capacity or cause.
Slavery negates ownership capacity; apostasy negates guardianship.
5
Note the exception for damages
Liability for destroying others' property remains on the minor because it is compensation for violating inviolable property, not a penal act.
This is distinguished from acts that are purely punitive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تھے، لہذا نبی آدم میں جوان ہونا اصل ہوا اور صغر کو عوارض میں شمار کیا، بہر حال صغرا اپنی ابتدائی حالت میں یعنی عاقل ہونے سے پہلے جنون کے مثل ہے، جنون کی طرح صفر میں بھی عقل معدوم ہوتی ہے ، اور اچھے برے کی تمیز نہیں ہوتی، بلکہ صغر جنون سے بھی ناقص تر ہے، کیونکہ مجنون تو کبھی کبھارا اچھے برے میں امتیاز کر بھی لیتا ہے مگر صغیر کو اس کی قدرت بالکل نہیں ہوتی۔
لیکن جب بچہ سمجھدار ہو جائے تو اس میں ایک قسم کی اہلیت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے یعنی اہلیت قاصرہ ، نہ کہ اہلیت کا ملہ یعنی ادا کی اہلیت اس میں پیدا ہو جاتی ہے مگر چونکہ صغرا بھی باقی ہے، لہذا اس صغر کے عذر کی وجہ سے وہ تمام احکام بچہ سے ساقط ہو جا ئینگے جو اعزار کی وجہ سے بالغ سے ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں، جیسے نماز، روزہ اور عبادات وغیرہ اور حدود دو کفارات ، البتہ جو احکام سقوط کا احتمال نہیں رکھتے وہ ساقط نہ ہوں گے جیسے ایمان لانا ، لہذا عاقل بچہ اگر ایمان لایا تو اس کا ایمان معتبر ہوگا ، الغرض صغر کے سلسلہ میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ صغیر سے ذمہ داری اٹھالی گئی ہے، لہذا غیر ذمہ داری اور غیر ضر ر والے کام صغیر خود کرے گا تو بھی درست ہے یا اس کی طرف سے اس کا ولی کرے گا تو بھی درست ہے، جیسے ہدیہ قبول کرنا ،صدقہ قبول کرنا وغیرہ ، تو ہدیہ اور صدقہ قبول کرنا اس میں بچہ کا کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے، لہذا یہ بچہ کے لیے درست ہے، بچہ خود قبول کرے، یا اس کی طرف سے اس کا ولی قبول کرے، کیونکہ بچپنا اسباب رحمت میں سے ہے ، طبعاً بھی یعنی طبعی طور پر بچہ کو دیکھ کر رحم آتا ہے، اور شرعاً بھی یعنی شریعت نے بھی بچہ پر ورحم کا حکم دیا ہے ،من لم يرحم صغيرنا ولم يؤقر كبيرنا فليس منا ، لہذا صغر اور بھینے کو عذر سمجھا گیا ہر اس ذمہ داری سے جس میں عفو اور معاف ہونے کا احتمال ہوتا ہے، لہذا بچہ نے اگر اپنے مورث کو قتل کر دیا تو یہ میراث سے محروم نہ ہوگا ، کیونکہ موجب قتل یعنی قصاص معاف کرنے سے ساقط ہو سکتا ہے لہذا بچہ سے بھی عذر صفر کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گا ، اور یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ مورث اپنی موت مرا ہے۔ ولايلزم عليه حرمانه: - ایک سوال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ جب صغر اسباب رحمت میں سے ہے اور بچہ مورث کو قتل کرنے سے بھی میراث سے محروم نہیں ہوتا ہے تو پھر بچہ رقیت اور کفر کی وجہ سے بھی میراث سے محروم نہ ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ کفر وارتداد کی صورت میں اور غلامی کی صورت میں بچہ میراث سے محروم ہوتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ رقیت میراث کی اہلیت کے منافی ہے، یعنی غلام میراث کا اہل نہیں ہے، کیونکہ میراث کا اہل ہونے کا مطلب ہے میراث کا مالک بنا ، اور غلام کسی چیز کا مالک نہیں بن سکتا ہے ، بلکہ جو چیز اس کی ملک میں آئے گی اس کا مالک اس کا مولی ہے، اسی طرح کفر بھی میراث کی اہلیت کے منافی ہے، اس لئے کہ کفر اہلیت ولایت کے منافی ہے یعنی کا فر کو مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں ہے، اور میراث کا مدار ولایت پر ہے، لہذا کا فروارث نہ ہوگا، رقیت میں حق میراث کی اہلیت کا سبب یعنی آزاد ہونا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے غلام محروم ہوگا اور کفر کی صورت میں حق میراث کا سبب یعنی ولایت نہیں پائی گئی اس لیے کا فر بچہ وارث نہ ہوگا ، تو اگر سبب اور اہلیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حق میراث معدوم ہوا تو اس کو سزا اور عقوبت نہ کہینگے کہ جس سے یہ بات لازم آئے کہ بچہ پر رحمت کے تقاضے کے خلاف کیا جارہا ہے، اور اس کو حرمانِ ارث کی سزاد بیجارہی ہے، بلکہ اس کا حرمان تو عدم سبب وعدم اہلیت کی وجہ سے ہے اس کو سز ا اور عقوبت نہیں کہیں گے۔ واما العته بعد البلوغ :- تیسرا عارض عنہ ہے ، عنہ کہتے ہیں عقل میں ایسا خلل ہو کہ معتوہ کی باتیں کبھی تو سمجھ داروں جیسی ہوں اور کبھی دیوانوں جیسی، پس بالغ معتوہ کا حکم صبی عاقل جیسا ہے، بچہ کی ابتدائی حالت تو جنون کے مشابہ تھی البتہ انتہائی حالت میں بچہ کی عقل ہوتی ہے مگر ناقص تو معتوہ میں بھی عقل میں خلل ہوتا ہے ، لہذا معتوہ بالغ صبی عاقل کے مانند ہے، پس عئہ قول و فعل کی صحت کو نہیں روکتا ہے، یعنی جیسے عاقل بچے کے اقوال وافعال صحیح ہیں ، ایسے ہی متوہ کے بھی صحیح ہیں جیسے اسلام قبول کرنا، ہدیہ قبول کرنا، وکیل بنا وغیرہ ،البتہ حئہ ذمہ داری کو روکتا ہے، یعنی ایسی چیز اس پر لازم نہ ہوگی جس میں اس کا ضرر ہو، لہذا معتوہ کا اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دینا درست نہ ہوگا ، نہ اپنے غلام کو آزاد کر نا صحیح ہوگا، نہ ولی کی اجازت سے نہ بغیر اجازت کے، اسی طرح معتوہ اگر بیع کا وکیل بنا تو اس سے تسلیم مبیع کا مطالبہ نہیں کیا جائے گا ، اور عیب ظاہر ہونے کی صورت میں معتوہ کو مبیع واپس لینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا،غرض نقصان اور ضر روالے کام کی ذمہ داری اس پر نہ ہوگی جیسے جیسی عاقل پر نہیں ہوتی۔
واماضمان مايستھلک :- ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ جب معتوہ اور صبی عاقل پر ضرر والی چیزیں لازم نہیں کیجاتی تو ان پر تلف کردہ مال کا ضمان بھی نہ آنا چاہیے، کیونکہ اس میں بھی ان کا ضرر ہے، حالانکہ ان پر ضمان واجب ہے، اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ضمان ذمہ داری کی بنا پر نہیں ہے جو معتوہ سے مشتکی ہے بلکہ مال معصوم کو ضائع کرنے کی تلافی میں ضمان مشروع ہوا ہے، اور ضائع کرنے والے کا معتوہ یا صبئ معذور ہونا عصمت محل کے منافی نہیں ہے یعنی مال ضائع کرنے والا اگر چہ صبی یا معتوہ ہے مگر اس کی وجہ سے کسی کے مال کی عصمت ختم نہیں ہو جاتی ، لہذا اس کی تلافی میں ضمان واجب ہوگا، یعنی یہ ضمان عصمت محل کا ہے فعل کی جزا نہیں ہے فعل کی جزا معتوہ پر نہیں آتی لہذا اگر اس نے اللہ کے حقوق ضائع کئے تو اس پر جو ضمان آئے گا وہ فعل کی جزا ہے، وہ معتوہ اور صبی عاقل پر نہیں آئے گی ، معتوہ سے اسی طرح خطاب اٹھا لیا گیا ہے جیسے صبی سے اٹھالیا گیا ہے، اور صبی کی طرح معتوہ پر بھی دوسروں کی ولایت ثابت ہوگی ان کے قصور عقل کی وجہ سے، البتہ معتوہ دوسرے کا ولی نہیں بن سکتا ہے، کیونکہ خود اپنے پر ولایت نہیں تو دوسروں پر کیسے ہوگی، پھر ایک ہے جنون اور ایک ہے عئہ ، جنون بچہ کی ابتدائی حالت کے
They were, so in the sons of Adam, adulthood is the original state, and minority is counted among the impediments. In any case, minority in its initial state, i.e., before becoming rational, is like insanity. Like insanity, in minority, intellect is absent, and there is no discrimination between good and bad. Rather, minority is even more deficient than insanity, because an insane person sometimes distinguishes between good and bad, but a minor has absolutely no such ability. But when a child becomes discerning, a kind of capacity arises in him, i.e., deficient capacity (ahliyya qāṣira), not complete capacity; that is, capacity of execution (ahliyya adā') arises in him, but because minority still remains, due to the excuse of minority, all those rulings fall from the child which fall from an adult due to excuses, such as prayer, fasting, and worship, and prescribed punishments and expiations. However, rulings that do not admit of being dropped are not dropped, such as faith. Therefore, if a discerning minor believes, his faith is valid. In short, the general principle regarding minority is that responsibility is lifted from the minor. Therefore, actions that are harmless and non-detrimental are valid whether the minor does them himself or his guardian does them on his behalf, such as accepting a gift, accepting charity, etc. So accepting a gift and charity involves no harm for the child, hence it is valid for the child, whether he accepts it himself or his guardian accepts it on his behalf, because childhood is among the causes of mercy, naturally, i.e., one naturally feels mercy upon seeing a child, and also legally, i.e., the Law has commanded mercy upon children. "He who does not show mercy to our young and honor our elders is not of us." Therefore, minority and idiocy are considered excuses from every responsibility that admits of pardon and forgiveness. Hence, if a child kills his ancestor, he will not be deprived of inheritance, because the cause of murder (qiṣāṣ) can be dropped by forgiving, so it is dropped from the child due to the excuse of minority, and it will be considered that the ancestor died his own death. "And he is not deprived of it." - They are answering a question: When minority is among the causes of mercy, and a child is not deprived of inheritance even if he kills his ancestor, then a child should not be deprived of inheritance due to slavery and disbelief either, whereas in the case of disbelief and apostasy and slavery, a child is deprived of inheritance. They are answering that slavery conflicts with the capacity for inheritance; that is, a slave is not eligible for inheritance, because being eligible for inheritance means being an owner of the inheritance, and a slave cannot own anything; rather, whatever comes into his possession, his master is its owner. Similarly, disbelief conflicts with the capacity for inheritance, because disbelief conflicts with the capacity for guardianship; that is, an infidel has no guardianship over a Muslim, and inheritance is based on guardianship. Therefore, an infidel will not inherit. In slavery, the cause of the right of inheritance, i.e., freedom, is not found, so a slave is deprived. In the case of disbelief, the cause of the right of inheritance, i.e., guardianship, is not found, so a child who is an infidel will not inherit. So if the right of inheritance is absent due to the absence of cause and capacity, we will not call it a punishment such that it would imply that something against the requirement of mercy is being done to the child, and that he is being punished with deprivation of inheritance. Rather, his deprivation is due to the absence of cause and capacity; we will not call it a punishment. "And regarding 'atah after puberty": The third impediment is 'atah. They say that 'atah is such a defect in intellect that the utterances of the ma'tūh (imbecile) are sometimes like those of sensible people and sometimes like those of mad people. So the ruling of a post-pubescent ma'tūh is like that of a discerning minor. The initial state of a child was similar to insanity, but in the final state, the child has intellect, though deficient. Similarly, in the ma'tūh, there is a defect in intellect. So a post-pubescent ma'tūh is like a discerning minor. Thus, 'atah does not prevent the validity of speech and action; i.e., just as the utterances and actions of a discerning minor are valid, so are those of the ma'tūh, such as accepting Islam, accepting a gift, appointing an agent, etc. However, 'atah does prevent responsibility; i.e., no matter involving harm will be binding upon him. Therefore, the ma'tūh's divorcing his wife is not valid, nor is his manumitting his slave valid, whether with the guardian's permission or without. Similarly, if the ma'tūh is appointed as an agent for sale, he cannot be demanded to deliver the sold item, and in case of a defect appearing, the ma'tūh cannot be compelled to take back the sold item. In short, responsibility for harmful and detrimental actions will not be on him, just as it is not on the discerning minor. "And the liability for what is destroyed": This is an answer to an objection. It is that when harmful things are not made binding on the ma'tūh and discerning minor, then liability for destroyed property should also not be imposed on them, because it involves harm to them, whereas liability is obligatory on them. The answer is that liability is not based on responsibility, which is doubted for the ma'tūh. Rather, liability is prescribed as compensation for destroying protected property. The fact that the destroyer is a ma'tūh or a minor with an excuse does not negate the inviolability of the place; i.e., even if the destroyer is a minor or a ma'tūh, the inviolability of someone's property is not nullified. Therefore, liability is obligatory as compensation. That is, this liability is for the inviolability of the place, not part of the penalty for the act. The penalty for the act does not apply to the ma'tūh. So if he destroys the rights of Allah, the liability that comes on him is part of the penalty for the act; that will not be on the ma'tūh and discerning minor. Address (taklīf) is lifted from the ma'tūh just as it is lifted from the minor. And like the minor, guardianship of others will be established over the ma'tūh due to their deficiency of intellect. However, the ma'tūh cannot be a guardian of another, because if he has no guardianship over himself, how can he have it over others? Then, insanity is one thing and 'atah is another. Insanity is like the initial state of a child...
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Usul al-Fiqh rules regarding the impediments (awārid) of minority (ṣighr) and imbecility ('atah) affecting legal capacity (ahliyya). The author explains that a minor in his initial state (before becoming discerning) is like an insane person, lacking rational discrimination. When the child becomes discerning (mumayyiz), he acquires a deficient capacity (ahliyya qāṣira) – capable of valid actions that bring benefit or are neutral, but not burdened with obligations or punishments that harm him. The general principle is that responsibility (taklīf) is lifted from the minor; thus obligatory acts like prayer and fasting are waived, and penal consequences (ḥudūd, kaffārāt) are dropped. However, actions that cannot be dropped, like faith (īmān), remain valid if performed. A child who kills his ancestor is not deprived of inheritance because the offense (qiṣāṣ) can be pardoned, and minority is a valid excuse to drop liability. The author then addresses an objection: why then is a minor slave or a minor apostate deprived of inheritance? The response is that slavery negates the very capacity to own property (since a slave cannot own), and apostasy negates the guardianship (wilāya) required for inheritance. This deprivation is not a punishment but merely the absence of required capacity or cause. Next, the passage discusses the impediment of 'atah (imbecility) after puberty – a mental weakness where the person sometimes speaks rationally and sometimes not. The ruling for such an adult is identical to that of a discerning minor: their speech and actions are valid if beneficial (e.g., accepting gifts, becoming Muslim) but not binding if detrimental (e.g., divorce, manumission). However, they remain liable for damages (ḍamān) for destroying others' property, because liability is compensation for violating inviolable property, not a punitive act that would have been lifted. The passage concludes that just as authority over a minor rests with a guardian, so too a ma'tūh is under guardianship, but he himself cannot be a guardian of others.

Key Terms
صغر (ṣighr): Minority, an impediment that lifts responsibility from a child due to lack of complete rationality.
اہلیت قاصرہ (ahliyya qāṣira): Deficient legal capacity that a discerning minor possesses – capable of valid beneficial actions but not bound by obligations.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for compensation, obligatory even on a minor or imbecile for destroying others' property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule on minority, which of the following acts of a discerning minor is NOT valid?
A) Accepting a gift of a book
B) Manumitting his slave
C) Becoming Muslim (accepting faith)
D) Receiving charity on behalf of his family

Key Takeaway
Minority lifts responsibility for penal and harmful obligations but does not invalidate beneficial acts, nor does it remove liability for compensating damages.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
6 min
Imbecility (ʿAṭah) as an Impediment to Legal Capacity
Commentary on rulings of ʿatah in legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that imbecility (ʿatah) is treated like the discerning stage of minority, and determine the validity of actions and responsibility of a ma'tūh.

Core Idea
A post-pubescent imbecile has the same rulings as a discerning minor.

In addition to minority, Hanafi usul recognizes imbecility (ʿatah) as an impediment to full legal capacity. This lesson explains the definition and rulings of ʿatah, showing that it is analogous to the discerning stage of minority, with similar effects on validity of actions and responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Define ʿatah and distinguish it from insanity
ʿAṭah is a mental weakness where the person sometimes speaks rationally and sometimes irrationally. Unlike insanity (junūn), which is complete loss of reason, ʿatah is intermittent.
The source compares it to the discerning minor's intellect—deficient but present.
2
Recognize that ʿatah does not prevent validity of beneficial acts
Like a discerning minor, the ma'tūh's utterances and actions that are beneficial (e.g., accepting gifts, becoming Muslim) are valid.
This is because the capacity for beneficial acts remains.
3
Understand that ʿatah prevents responsibility for harmful acts
Detrimental actions like divorce or manumission are not valid, even with guardian permission. The ma'tūh is not bound by obligations that harm him.
The same principle of mercy applies.
4
Apply the liability for damages
The ma'tūh remains liable for destroying others' property, just as the discerning minor is, because liability is compensation, not punishment.
This maintains the inviolability of others' property.
5
Note the guardianship implications
The ma'tūh is under guardianship of others, just as a minor is. However, he himself cannot be a guardian of others because he lacks full control over himself.
This follows from his deficient capacity.

تھے، لہذا نبی آدم میں جوان ہونا اصل ہوا اور صغر کو عوارض میں شمار کیا، بہر حال صغرا اپنی ابتدائی حالت میں یعنی عاقل ہونے سے پہلے جنون کے مثل ہے، جنون کی طرح صفر میں بھی عقل معدوم ہوتی ہے ، اور اچھے برے کی تمیز نہیں ہوتی، بلکہ صغر جنون سے بھی ناقص تر ہے، کیونکہ مجنون تو کبھی کبھارا اچھے برے میں امتیاز کر بھی لیتا ہے مگر صغیر کو اس کی قدرت بالکل نہیں ہوتی۔
لیکن جب بچہ سمجھدار ہو جائے تو اس میں ایک قسم کی اہلیت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے یعنی اہلیت قاصرہ ، نہ کہ اہلیت کا ملہ یعنی ادا کی اہلیت اس میں پیدا ہو جاتی ہے مگر چونکہ صغرا بھی باقی ہے، لہذا اس صغر کے عذر کی وجہ سے وہ تمام احکام بچہ سے ساقط ہو جا ئینگے جو اعزار کی وجہ سے بالغ سے ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں، جیسے نماز، روزہ اور عبادات وغیرہ اور حدود دو کفارات ، البتہ جو احکام سقوط کا احتمال نہیں رکھتے وہ ساقط نہ ہوں گے جیسے ایمان لانا ، لہذا عاقل بچہ اگر ایمان لایا تو اس کا ایمان معتبر ہوگا ، الغرض صغر کے سلسلہ میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ صغیر سے ذمہ داری اٹھالی گئی ہے، لہذا غیر ذمہ داری اور غیر ضر ر والے کام صغیر خود کرے گا تو بھی درست ہے یا اس کی طرف سے اس کا ولی کرے گا تو بھی درست ہے، جیسے ہدیہ قبول کرنا ،صدقہ قبول کرنا وغیرہ ، تو ہدیہ اور صدقہ قبول کرنا اس میں بچہ کا کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے، لہذا یہ بچہ کے لیے درست ہے، بچہ خود قبول کرے، یا اس کی طرف سے اس کا ولی قبول کرے، کیونکہ بچپنا اسباب رحمت میں سے ہے ، طبعاً بھی یعنی طبعی طور پر بچہ کو دیکھ کر رحم آتا ہے، اور شرعاً بھی یعنی شریعت نے بھی بچہ پر ورحم کا حکم دیا ہے ،من لم يرحم صغيرنا ولم يؤقر كبيرنا فليس منا ، لہذا صغر اور بھینے کو عذر سمجھا گیا ہر اس ذمہ داری سے جس میں عفو اور معاف ہونے کا احتمال ہوتا ہے، لہذا بچہ نے اگر اپنے مورث کو قتل کر دیا تو یہ میراث سے محروم نہ ہوگا ، کیونکہ موجب قتل یعنی قصاص معاف کرنے سے ساقط ہو سکتا ہے لہذا بچہ سے بھی عذر صفر کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گا ، اور یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ مورث اپنی موت مرا ہے۔ ولايلزم عليه حرمانه: - ایک سوال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ جب صغر اسباب رحمت میں سے ہے اور بچہ مورث کو قتل کرنے سے بھی میراث سے محروم نہیں ہوتا ہے تو پھر بچہ رقیت اور کفر کی وجہ سے بھی میراث سے محروم نہ ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ کفر وارتداد کی صورت میں اور غلامی کی صورت میں بچہ میراث سے محروم ہوتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ رقیت میراث کی اہلیت کے منافی ہے، یعنی غلام میراث کا اہل نہیں ہے، کیونکہ میراث کا اہل ہونے کا مطلب ہے میراث کا مالک بنا ، اور غلام کسی چیز کا مالک نہیں بن سکتا ہے ، بلکہ جو چیز اس کی ملک میں آئے گی اس کا مالک اس کا مولی ہے، اسی طرح کفر بھی میراث کی اہلیت کے منافی ہے، اس لئے کہ کفر اہلیت ولایت کے منافی ہے یعنی کا فر کو مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں ہے، اور میراث کا مدار ولایت پر ہے، لہذا کا فروارث نہ ہوگا، رقیت میں حق میراث کی اہلیت کا سبب یعنی آزاد ہونا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے غلام محروم ہوگا اور کفر کی صورت میں حق میراث کا سبب یعنی ولایت نہیں پائی گئی اس لیے کا فر بچہ وارث نہ ہوگا ، تو اگر سبب اور اہلیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حق میراث معدوم ہوا تو اس کو سزا اور عقوبت نہ کہینگے کہ جس سے یہ بات لازم آئے کہ بچہ پر رحمت کے تقاضے کے خلاف کیا جارہا ہے، اور اس کو حرمانِ ارث کی سزاد بیجارہی ہے، بلکہ اس کا حرمان تو عدم سبب وعدم اہلیت کی وجہ سے ہے اس کو سز ا اور عقوبت نہیں کہیں گے۔ واما العته بعد البلوغ :- تیسرا عارض عنہ ہے ، عنہ کہتے ہیں عقل میں ایسا خلل ہو کہ معتوہ کی باتیں کبھی تو سمجھ داروں جیسی ہوں اور کبھی دیوانوں جیسی، پس بالغ معتوہ کا حکم صبی عاقل جیسا ہے، بچہ کی ابتدائی حالت تو جنون کے مشابہ تھی البتہ انتہائی حالت میں بچہ کی عقل ہوتی ہے مگر ناقص تو معتوہ میں بھی عقل میں خلل ہوتا ہے ، لہذا معتوہ بالغ صبی عاقل کے مانند ہے، پس عئہ قول و فعل کی صحت کو نہیں روکتا ہے، یعنی جیسے عاقل بچے کے اقوال وافعال صحیح ہیں ، ایسے ہی متوہ کے بھی صحیح ہیں جیسے اسلام قبول کرنا، ہدیہ قبول کرنا، وکیل بنا وغیرہ ،البتہ حئہ ذمہ داری کو روکتا ہے، یعنی ایسی چیز اس پر لازم نہ ہوگی جس میں اس کا ضرر ہو، لہذا معتوہ کا اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دینا درست نہ ہوگا ، نہ اپنے غلام کو آزاد کر نا صحیح ہوگا، نہ ولی کی اجازت سے نہ بغیر اجازت کے، اسی طرح معتوہ اگر بیع کا وکیل بنا تو اس سے تسلیم مبیع کا مطالبہ نہیں کیا جائے گا ، اور عیب ظاہر ہونے کی صورت میں معتوہ کو مبیع واپس لینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا،غرض نقصان اور ضر روالے کام کی ذمہ داری اس پر نہ ہوگی جیسے جیسی عاقل پر نہیں ہوتی۔
واماضمان مايستھلک :- ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ جب معتوہ اور صبی عاقل پر ضرر والی چیزیں لازم نہیں کیجاتی تو ان پر تلف کردہ مال کا ضمان بھی نہ آنا چاہیے، کیونکہ اس میں بھی ان کا ضرر ہے، حالانکہ ان پر ضمان واجب ہے، اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ضمان ذمہ داری کی بنا پر نہیں ہے جو معتوہ سے مشتکی ہے بلکہ مال معصوم کو ضائع کرنے کی تلافی میں ضمان مشروع ہوا ہے، اور ضائع کرنے والے کا معتوہ یا صبئ معذور ہونا عصمت محل کے منافی نہیں ہے یعنی مال ضائع کرنے والا اگر چہ صبی یا معتوہ ہے مگر اس کی وجہ سے کسی کے مال کی عصمت ختم نہیں ہو جاتی ، لہذا اس کی تلافی میں ضمان واجب ہوگا، یعنی یہ ضمان عصمت محل کا ہے فعل کی جزا نہیں ہے فعل کی جزا معتوہ پر نہیں آتی لہذا اگر اس نے اللہ کے حقوق ضائع کئے تو اس پر جو ضمان آئے گا وہ فعل کی جزا ہے، وہ معتوہ اور صبی عاقل پر نہیں آئے گی ، معتوہ سے اسی طرح خطاب اٹھا لیا گیا ہے جیسے صبی سے اٹھالیا گیا ہے، اور صبی کی طرح معتوہ پر بھی دوسروں کی ولایت ثابت ہوگی ان کے قصور عقل کی وجہ سے، البتہ معتوہ دوسرے کا ولی نہیں بن سکتا ہے، کیونکہ خود اپنے پر ولایت نہیں تو دوسروں پر کیسے ہوگی، پھر ایک ہے جنون اور ایک ہے عئہ ، جنون بچہ کی ابتدائی حالت کے
They were, so in the sons of Adam, adulthood is the original state, and minority is counted among the impediments. In any case, minority in its initial state, i.e., before becoming rational, is like insanity. Like insanity, in minority, intellect is absent, and there is no discrimination between good and bad. Rather, minority is even more deficient than insanity, because an insane person sometimes distinguishes between good and bad, but a minor has absolutely no such ability. But when a child becomes discerning, a kind of capacity arises in him, i.e., deficient capacity (ahliyya qāṣira), not complete capacity; that is, capacity of execution (ahliyya adā') arises in him, but because minority still remains, due to the excuse of minority, all those rulings fall from the child which fall from an adult due to excuses, such as prayer, fasting, and worship, and prescribed punishments and expiations. However, rulings that do not admit of being dropped are not dropped, such as faith. Therefore, if a discerning minor believes, his faith is valid. In short, the general principle regarding minority is that responsibility is lifted from the minor. Therefore, actions that are harmless and non-detrimental are valid whether the minor does them himself or his guardian does them on his behalf, such as accepting a gift, accepting charity, etc. So accepting a gift and charity involves no harm for the child, hence it is valid for the child, whether he accepts it himself or his guardian accepts it on his behalf, because childhood is among the causes of mercy, naturally, i.e., one naturally feels mercy upon seeing a child, and also legally, i.e., the Law has commanded mercy upon children. "He who does not show mercy to our young and honor our elders is not of us." Therefore, minority and idiocy are considered excuses from every responsibility that admits of pardon and forgiveness. Hence, if a child kills his ancestor, he will not be deprived of inheritance, because the cause of murder (qiṣāṣ) can be dropped by forgiving, so it is dropped from the child due to the excuse of minority, and it will be considered that the ancestor died his own death. "And he is not deprived of it." - They are answering a question: When minority is among the causes of mercy, and a child is not deprived of inheritance even if he kills his ancestor, then a child should not be deprived of inheritance due to slavery and disbelief either, whereas in the case of disbelief and apostasy and slavery, a child is deprived of inheritance. They are answering that slavery conflicts with the capacity for inheritance; that is, a slave is not eligible for inheritance, because being eligible for inheritance means being an owner of the inheritance, and a slave cannot own anything; rather, whatever comes into his possession, his master is its owner. Similarly, disbelief conflicts with the capacity for inheritance, because disbelief conflicts with the capacity for guardianship; that is, an infidel has no guardianship over a Muslim, and inheritance is based on guardianship. Therefore, an infidel will not inherit. In slavery, the cause of the right of inheritance, i.e., freedom, is not found, so a slave is deprived. In the case of disbelief, the cause of the right of inheritance, i.e., guardianship, is not found, so a child who is an infidel will not inherit. So if the right of inheritance is absent due to the absence of cause and capacity, we will not call it a punishment such that it would imply that something against the requirement of mercy is being done to the child, and that he is being punished with deprivation of inheritance. Rather, his deprivation is due to the absence of cause and capacity; we will not call it a punishment. "And regarding 'atah after puberty": The third impediment is 'atah. They say that 'atah is such a defect in intellect that the utterances of the ma'tūh (imbecile) are sometimes like those of sensible people and sometimes like those of mad people. So the ruling of a post-pubescent ma'tūh is like that of a discerning minor. The initial state of a child was similar to insanity, but in the final state, the child has intellect, though deficient. Similarly, in the ma'tūh, there is a defect in intellect. So a post-pubescent ma'tūh is like a discerning minor. Thus, 'atah does not prevent the validity of speech and action; i.e., just as the utterances and actions of a discerning minor are valid, so are those of the ma'tūh, such as accepting Islam, accepting a gift, appointing an agent, etc. However, 'atah does prevent responsibility; i.e., no matter involving harm will be binding upon him. Therefore, the ma'tūh's divorcing his wife is not valid, nor is his manumitting his slave valid, whether with the guardian's permission or without. Similarly, if the ma'tūh is appointed as an agent for sale, he cannot be demanded to deliver the sold item, and in case of a defect appearing, the ma'tūh cannot be compelled to take back the sold item. In short, responsibility for harmful and detrimental actions will not be on him, just as it is not on the discerning minor. "And the liability for what is destroyed": This is an answer to an objection. It is that when harmful things are not made binding on the ma'tūh and discerning minor, then liability for destroyed property should also not be imposed on them, because it involves harm to them, whereas liability is obligatory on them. The answer is that liability is not based on responsibility, which is doubted for the ma'tūh. Rather, liability is prescribed as compensation for destroying protected property. The fact that the destroyer is a ma'tūh or a minor with an excuse does not negate the inviolability of the place; i.e., even if the destroyer is a minor or a ma'tūh, the inviolability of someone's property is not nullified. Therefore, liability is obligatory as compensation. That is, this liability is for the inviolability of the place, not part of the penalty for the act. The penalty for the act does not apply to the ma'tūh. So if he destroys the rights of Allah, the liability that comes on him is part of the penalty for the act; that will not be on the ma'tūh and discerning minor. Address (taklīf) is lifted from the ma'tūh just as it is lifted from the minor. And like the minor, guardianship of others will be established over the ma'tūh due to their deficiency of intellect. However, the ma'tūh cannot be a guardian of another, because if he has no guardianship over himself, how can he have it over others? Then, insanity is one thing and 'atah is another. Insanity is like the initial state of a child...
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Usul al-Fiqh rules regarding the impediments (awārid) of minority (ṣighr) and imbecility ('atah) affecting legal capacity (ahliyya). The author explains that a minor in his initial state (before becoming discerning) is like an insane person, lacking rational discrimination. When the child becomes discerning (mumayyiz), he acquires a deficient capacity (ahliyya qāṣira) – capable of valid actions that bring benefit or are neutral, but not burdened with obligations or punishments that harm him. The general principle is that responsibility (taklīf) is lifted from the minor; thus obligatory acts like prayer and fasting are waived, and penal consequences (ḥudūd, kaffārāt) are dropped. However, actions that cannot be dropped, like faith (īmān), remain valid if performed. A child who kills his ancestor is not deprived of inheritance because the offense (qiṣāṣ) can be pardoned, and minority is a valid excuse to drop liability. The author then addresses an objection: why then is a minor slave or a minor apostate deprived of inheritance? The response is that slavery negates the very capacity to own property (since a slave cannot own), and apostasy negates the guardianship (wilāya) required for inheritance. This deprivation is not a punishment but merely the absence of required capacity or cause. Next, the passage discusses the impediment of 'atah (imbecility) after puberty – a mental weakness where the person sometimes speaks rationally and sometimes not. The ruling for such an adult is identical to that of a discerning minor: their speech and actions are valid if beneficial (e.g., accepting gifts, becoming Muslim) but not binding if detrimental (e.g., divorce, manumission). However, they remain liable for damages (ḍamān) for destroying others' property, because liability is compensation for violating inviolable property, not a punitive act that would have been lifted. The passage concludes that just as authority over a minor rests with a guardian, so too a ma'tūh is under guardianship, but he himself cannot be a guardian of others.

Key Terms
عته (ʿatah): Imbecility or mental weakness in an adult where the person sometimes acts rationally and sometimes irrationally.
معتوہ (ma'tūh): A person afflicted with ʿatah, i.e., an imbecile with intermittent rationality.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for compensation, obligatory even on a ma'tūh or minor for destroying others' property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule on ʿatah, which of the following actions of a ma'tūh is valid?
A) Divorcing his wife
B) Manumitting his slave
C) Appointing an agent (wakīl) for a sale
D) Making a binding contract of sale

Key Takeaway
A ma'tūh (imbecile) is treated like a discerning minor: his beneficial acts are valid, harmful acts are not binding, but he remains liable for compensatory damages.

Habitual Forgetfulness and Its Effect on Legal Obligations
Explains the effect of habitual forgetfulness on obligations in rights of Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on habitual forgetfulness (nisyān ghalib) to distinguish between rights of Allah and rights of humans, and state the effect on obligations.

Core Idea
Habitual forgetfulness pardons in Allah's rights but not in human rights; the obligation itself remains.

In this passage, we explore a key Hanafi usul principle: forgetfulness does not remove an obligation, but if habitual, it can be a cause of pardon in matters of worship. This distinction between haqq Allah and haqq al-'ibad has practical implications for rulings on prayer and other acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key distinction
Recognize that the rule distinguishes between rights of Allah and rights of human beings. Forgetfulness affects these two categories differently.
This is a foundational division in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand that forgetfulness does not negate wujub
Forgetfulness (nisyān) does not remove the original obligation (wujub) in the rights of Allah. The obligation still stands, but pardon may apply.
Contrast with the idea that forgetfulness might negate the obligation entirely.
3
Recognize the condition of habitual forgetfulness
The text specifies that the forgetfulness must be 'ghalib' (habitual or predominant), meaning it accompanies acts of obedience. Rare forgetfulness does not receive the same pardon.
The Arabic phrase 'kāna ghāliban yulāzimu al-ṭā‘ah' is key.
4
Apply to the given examples
Examine the examples: forgetfulness in fasting (eating/drinking by mistake) and forgetting the tasmiya in slaughter. Both are pardoned because the person is engaged in worship.
Also consider the example of forgetful salām in prayer.
5
Contrast with speech in prayer
The text contrasts forgetful salām with forgetful speech. The posture (hay'ah) of the praying person reminds him, so speech during prayer is not habitual, thus it breaks the prayer.
This shows the practical application of the habitual condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَا النِّسْيَانَ فَلَايْنَا فَي الْوُجُوْبَ فِي حَقَّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لَكِنَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ غَالِبًا يُلاَزِمُ الطَّاعَةَ مِثْلُ النِّيْسَانِ فِي الصَّوْمِ وَالتَّسْمِيَةِ فِي النَّبِيْحَةِ جُعِلَ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ الْعَفْوِلِأَنَّهُ مِنْ جِهَةِ صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ اعْتَرَضَ بِخِلَافِ حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا اِنَّ سَلَامَ النَّاسِى لَمَّا كَانَ غَالِبًا لَمْ يَقْطَع الصَّلوةَ بِخِلَافِ الْكَلَام لِاَنَّ هَيَاهَ الْمُصْلَى مُذَكِرَةٌ لَهُ فَلَا يَغْلِبُ الْكَلَامُ نَاسِيَا
As for forgetfulness, it does not negate [or: does not affect?] obligation in the rights of Allah the Exalted; but if it is habitual and accompanies obedience, such as forgetfulness in fasting and the takbīr [tasmiya?] in slaughtering, it is made a cause of pardon, because it is from the side of the rights holder (Allah). This is contrary to the rights of human beings. On this basis, we say that the salām of a forgetful person, since it is habitual, does not break the prayer, unlike speech, because the posture of the praying person reminds him, so speech does not occur habitually by a forgetful person.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of forgetfulness (nisyān) on legal obligations. The author states that forgetfulness does not remove the obligation itself in matters pertaining to Allah's rights; however, if forgetfulness is a common occurrence that accompanies acts of obedience (like forgetting to eat during fasting or forgetting the tasmiya in slaughter), it becomes a cause of pardon because the right belongs to Allah and He may grant leniency. This is in contrast to the rights of human beings, where forgetfulness does not pardon. An example given: if a praying person forgetfully says salām (which is not part of the prayer) during prayer, it does not invalidate the prayer because it is habitual forgetfulness and the posture of the prayer reminds the person; however, if he speaks words, that is not habitual and would break the prayer.

Key Terms
نسيان (nisyān): Forgetfulness; the state of not remembering an obligation or action.
عفو ('afw): Pardon; the removal of liability or sin due to forgetfulness.
حقالله (haqq allah): Rights of Allah; obligations that primarily concern divine commands.
غالب (ghālib): Habitual; predominant; occurring frequently or as a common trait.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a person habitually forgetfully says 'Salām' during prayer?
A) The prayer is invalidated because it is not part of the prayer.
B) The prayer remains valid because habitual forgetfulness is pardoned in Allah's rights.
C) The prayer is valid only if the person performs sajdah sahw.
D) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Habitual forgetfulness in acts of worship is pardoned in Hanafi usul, but the obligation itself remains and the concept does not extend to human rights.

Distinguishing Madness and Childhood in Presenting Islam: A Usul Ruling
Explains difference between junun and sughr regarding Islam presentation to spouse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal distinction between junun and sughr regarding the presentation of Islam to a spouse and apply the underlying principle to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Madness has no fixed end, so no waiting; childhood has a definite limit, so waiting is required.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text examines a key principle: how the temporal nature of an impediment to legal capacity affects the ruling. The case involves a spouse embracing Islam. The author distinguishes between the madman (unlimited impediment) and the child (limited impediment), and also clarifies the status of the ma'tuh (mentally deficient but not insane). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rulings to other situations where legal capacity is suspended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage discusses three types of persons: the madman (majnun), the child (sabi), and the mentally deficient person (ma'tuh). Note the key attribute of each.
2
Note the key attribute of each impediment
Madness (junun) is unlimited – no fixed time for its removal. Childhood (sughr) is limited – it ends with maturity. Ma'tuh is similar to an intelligent child; his Islam is valid without guardian.
3
Apply to the scenario of a spouse embracing Islam
If the wife of a madman becomes Muslim, present Islam to his parents immediately. If the wife of a child becomes Muslim, wait until the child matures, then present Islam. If the wife of a ma'tuh becomes Muslim, present Islam immediately to him.
4
Derive the usul principle
The ruling depends on whether the impediment is temporary with a known end or indefinite. If indefinite, immediate action is taken; if limited, one waits until the impediment is removed.
5
Apply to other impediments
Consider other situations: unconsciousness (similar to madness – no fixed end) vs. a fixed-term illness (similar to childhood – limited period).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشابہ ہے اور عتہ بچہ کی انتہائی حالت کے مشابہ ہے، تو مصنف بچہ اور مجنون میں اور بچہ اور معتوہ میں فرق بتلار ہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ جنون اور صفر کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ جنون غیر محدود ہے، اس کے زوال کا کوئی وقت متعین نہیں ہے، اور صغر محدود ہے ایک مدت ختم ہونے پر صغر ختم ہو جائے گا، تو اس پر تفریح کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر مجنون کی بیوی مسلمان ہوگئی تو مجنون کے والدین پر اسلام پیش کیا جائے گا، اور مجنون والدین کے تابع سمجھا جائے گا، اگر والدین نے قبول کر لیا تو نکاح برقرار رہے گا ورنہ عورت مجنون سے بائنہ ہو جائے گی، یہاں مجنون پر اسلام پیش کرنے میں تاخیر سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ پتہ نہیں جنون کب زائل ہو، لیکن اگر صبی کی بیوی مسلمان ہوگئی تو بچہ کے والدین پر اسلام پیش نہیں کیا جائے گا، بلکہ بچہ کے عاقل ہونے تک انتظار کیا جائے گا، عاقل ہونے کے بعد اسلام پیش کیا جائے گا، اس نے قبول کر لیا تو نکاح برقرار رہے گا اور نہ تفریق ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ جنون غیر محدود ہے تو انتظار سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں، اور صغر محدود ہے، لہذا بچہ کے عاقل ہونے تک انتظار کیا جائے گا، یہ تو فرق ہوا مجنون اور صیبی میں، اور معتوہ عاقل اور صبی عاقل میں مصنف لیے فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے، لہذا اگر معتوہ کی بیوی مسلمان ہوگئی تو بلاتا خیر معتوہ پر اسلام پیش کیا جائے گا جیسے صبی عاقل پر بلا تاخیر اسلام پیش کیا جاتا ہے، اگر معتوہ نے اسلام قبول کیا تو نکاح برقرار رہے گا اور نہ تفریق ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ معتوہ اور صئی عاقل دونوں کا اسلام معتبر ہے، لہذا اسلام پیش کرنے میں تاخیر تا خیر نہیں کی جائے گی، مصنف اس نے معتوہ کے ساتھ عاقل کی قید اس لیے لگائی کہ معتوہ کا اطلاق بعض دفعہ مجنون پر بھی ہوتا ہے اور یہاں مجنون مراد نہیں ہے۔
It is similar, and atah is similar to the extreme state of a child. So the author is distinguishing between a child and a madman, and between a child and a ma'tuh. He says: The difference between madness (junun) and childhood (sughr) is that madness is unlimited – there is no fixed time for its removal – while childhood is limited; upon completion of a period, childhood ends. Then he elaborates: If the wife of a madman becomes Muslim, Islam will be presented to the madman's parents, and the madman is considered subordinate to his parents. If the parents accept, the marriage remains; otherwise the woman becomes bain from the madman. Here, delaying the presentation of Islam to the madman is of no benefit because it is unknown when the madness will end. But if the wife of a child becomes Muslim, Islam will not be presented to the child's parents; rather, one waits until the child reaches maturity. After maturity, Islam will be presented. If he accepts, the marriage remains; otherwise it is annulled. This is because madness is unlimited, so waiting is of no benefit, while childhood is limited, so one waits until the child becomes mature. That is the distinction between a madman and a child. Regarding ma'tuh and an intelligent child, the author says there is no difference between them. So if the wife of a ma'tuh becomes Muslim, Islam will be presented to the ma'tuh immediately, just as it is presented immediately to an intelligent child. If the ma'tuh accepts Islam, the marriage remains and is not annulled, because the Islam of both the ma'tuh and the intelligent child is valid. Therefore, there is no delay in presenting Islam. The author added the condition of 'intelligent' for ma'tuh because ma'tuh is sometimes applied to a madman, and here madman is not intended.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a comparative legal ruling distinguishing between the cases of a madman (majnun), a child (sabi), and a mentally deficient person (ma'tuh) when their spouses embrace Islam. The key principle is that madness has no fixed duration, so waiting for recovery is futile; thus Islam is presented immediately to the madman's parents. Childhood, on the other hand, has a natural end, so one waits until the child reaches maturity. Ma'tuh is treated like an intelligent child because his Islam is valid. The passage follows the Hanafi view that guardianship (wilaya) over a madman rests with his parents, and that the validity of marriage depends on the acceptance of Islam by the party or their guardian. This is a standard Hanafi ruling from the chapter on apostasy and marriage.

Key Terms
جنون (junun): Madness, a state of insanity with no fixed end.
صغر (sughr): Childhood, a limited period ending with maturity (bulugh).
معتوہ (ma'tuh): Mentally deficient person who is not insane but lacks full intelligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Islam presented immediately to the madman's parents rather than waiting for the madman to recover?
A) Because the madman is incapable of understanding Islam entirely
B) Because madness has no fixed limit, so waiting is futile
C) Because the parents have authority over the madman's marriage
D) Because the madman's Islam is not valid without his parents

Key Takeaway
The nature of an impediment (limited vs. unlimited) determines whether one must act immediately or wait for its removal.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

8 min
Forgetfulness: When It Excuses and When It Doesn't
Analyzing nisyan as an impediment in Hanafi usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that prevalent forgetfulness is a cause of pardon in huquq Allah but not in huquq al-ibad, and identify the legal consequences in specific cases.

Core Idea
Prevailing forgetfulness pardons in Allah's rights but not in servants' rights.

Forgetfulness (nisyan) is a natural human condition that often arises during acts of worship. This lesson explores how the Hanafi school treats forgetfulness as an impediment (arid al-ahliyya) that affects liability. The key distinction is between rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of servants (huquq al-ibad). In the former, if forgetfulness is prevalent and unavoidable, it is pardoned; in the latter, liability remains. Understanding this principle helps resolve many fiqh cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify nisyan as an arid al-ahliyya
Recognize that forgetfulness is one of the impediments that partially affects a person's capacity (ahliyya ada). It does not remove obligation but may excuse the sin or invalidation.
Nisyan is distinct from ignorance or negligence.
2
Apply the rule that nisyan does not negate obligation
The text explicitly states: 'nisyan does not contradict obligation in the right of Allah.' Thus, missed acts must be made up (qada) even if forgotten.
Obligation remains, but the forgetful person is excused from sin.
3
Distinguish huquq Allah from huquq al-ibad
In huquq Allah, forgetfulness is pardoned if it is prevalent and unavoidable (ghalib), because it arises 'from the side of the Owner of the right' (i.e., Allah created the distraction). In huquq al-ibad, forgetfulness does not pardon; compensation (daman) is required.
The source text gives examples: fasting and tasmiyah in dhabihah are huquq Allah; destroying property is huquq al-ibad.
4
Analyze the example of forgetful salaam in prayer
The text uses the case of someone forgetfully saying salaam during prayer. If such forgetfulness is prevalent, it does not break the prayer, unlike intentional speech. The reason is that the state of prayer normally reminds the person not to speak, so forgetful speech is rare and thus pardoned.
This illustrates the principle applied to a specific ruling.
5
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Using the same distinction, evaluate cases like forgetfully missing a rukn or wajib in prayer, or forgetting to pay zakat on time. The outcome depends on whether the act falls under huquq Allah or involves others' rights.
The Hanafi rule is consistent across ibadat and muamalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَا النِّسْيَانَ فَلَا يُنَافِي الْوُجُوبَ فِي حَقِّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لَكِنَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ غَالِبًا يُلاَزِمُ الطَّاعَةَ مِثْلُ النِّيْسَانِ فِي الصَّوْمِ وَالتَّسْمِيَةِ فِي الذَّبِيْحَةِ جُعِلَ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ الْعَفْوِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ جِهَةِ صَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ اعْتَرَضَ بِخِلَافِ حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا اِنَّ سَلَامَ النَّاسِى لَمَّا كَانَ غَالِبًا لَمْ يَقْطَع الصَّلوةَ بِخِلَافِ الْكَلَام لِاَنَّ هَيْئَةَ الْمُصْلَى مُذَكِّرَةٌ لَهُ فَلَا يَغْلِبُ الْكَلَامُ نَاسِيًا - ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال نیسان پس وہ اللہ کے حق میں وجوب کے منافی نہیں ہے لیکن جب نسیان ایسا غالب ہو جو طاعت کے ساتھ لازم رہے جیسے روزہ میں نسیان اور ذبیحہ میں تسمیہ کا نسیان تو اس کو اسباب عفو میں سے قرار دیا گیا ہے، اس لئے کہ یہ نسیان صاحب حق کی طرف سے عارض ہوا ہے، بر خلاف حقوق العباد کے، اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا کہ ناسی کا سلام جب غالب ہو تو وہ نماز کو قطع نہیں کرے گا، برخلاف کلام کے اس لئے کہ نماز کی ہیئت نماز کو یاد دلانے والی ہے، تو بھول کر کلام غالب نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح : چوتھا عارض نسیان ہے، نسیان یہ ہے کہ بغیر کسی آفت و بیماری کے بعض چیزوں سے جاہل اور بے خبر ہو جانا، حالانکہ بہت سی چیزوں کا علم رکھتا ہے، بھول حقوق اللہ کے وجوب کو نہیں روکتی، لہذا نماز، روزہ وغیرہ عبادتیں بھول جانے سے ساقط نہ ہوں گی، بلکہ ان کی قضا لازم ہوگی لیکن جن عبادتوں میں نسیان کا غلبہ ہو ان میں نسیان اسباب عفو میں سے ہے یعنی معاف ہے، کیونکہ یہ نسیان صاحب حق یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف سے پیش آیا ہے، بندہ کا اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے، لہذا خود اللہ کے حقوق میں نسیان معاف ہوگا جیسے روزہ میں نسیان، انسان بسا اوقات بھول کر کھا پی لیتا ہے، تو یہ معاف ہے، اس سے روزہ فاسد نہ ہوگا، اسی طرح ذبح کے وقت عام طور پر انسان پر ایسی ہیبت طاری ہوتی ہے کہ وہ بسم اللہ بھول جاتا ہے، لہذا احناف کے نزدیک ذبح کے وقت تسمیہ کا نسیان معاف ہے، لیکن حقوق العباد میں نسیان معاف نہیں ہے لہذا بھول کر اگر کسی کا مال ہلاک کر دیا تو منمان لازم آئے گا۔ چونکہ نسیان غالب عذر ہے اور معاف ہے اس لئے اگر کسی نے قعدہ اولی میں بھول کر، اس کو قعدہ اخیر سمجھ کر
As for forgetfulness, it does not contradict obligation in the right of Allah the Exalted, but when it is prevalent and accompanies obedience, like forgetfulness in fasting and forgetfulness of the tasmiyah in sacrifice, it is made one of the causes of pardon, because this forgetfulness arises from the side of the owner of the right, unlike the rights of servants. And upon this we said: The greeting of a forgetful person, when it is prevalent, does not break the prayer, unlike speech, because the state of the one praying is a reminder for him, so speech does not become prevalent forgetfully. Translation: As for forgetfulness, it does not contradict obligation in the right of Allah, but when forgetfulness is such that it is prevalent and accompanies obedience, such as forgetfulness in fasting and forgetfulness of tasmiyah in sacrifice, then it is considered from the causes of pardon, because this forgetfulness occurs from the side of the Owner of the right, unlike the rights of servants. And on this basis we said: When the greeting of a forgetful person is prevalent, it will not cut the prayer, unlike speech, because the state of prayer reminds him, so forgetful speech does not become prevalent. Explanation: The fourth impediment is forgetfulness. Forgetfulness is to become ignorant and unaware of some things without any affliction or illness, while knowing many other things. Forgetfulness does not prevent the obligation in the rights of Allah. Therefore, prayers, fasting, etc. do not lapse due to forgetfulness; rather, their qada is necessary. But in those acts of worship where forgetfulness is prevalent, forgetfulness is from the causes of pardon, i.e., it is forgiven, because this forgetfulness occurs from the Owner of the right, i.e., Allah, and the servant has no role in it. So in the rights of Allah themselves, forgetfulness is forgiven, such as forgetfulness in fasting – a person sometimes eats and drinks forgetfully, so it is forgiven, and the fast is not invalidated. Similarly, at the time of slaughter, usually a person is overcome by such awe that he forgets to say Bismillah, so according to the Hanafis, forgetfulness of tasmiyah at the time of slaughter is forgiven. But in the rights of servants, forgetfulness is not forgiven; so if someone destroys another's property forgetfully, compensation is necessary. Since forgetfulness is a prevalent excuse and is forgiven, if someone in the first sitting forgetfully thinks it is the last sitting...
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage discusses the impediment (arid) of forgetfulness (nisyan) and its effect on legal obligations. The key principle: forgetfulness does not negate the obligation itself in the rights of Allah; one remains obliged to perform the missed act. However, forgetfulness can be a cause of forgiveness for the sin or invalidation in certain contexts. The text distinguishes between rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of servants (huquq al-ibad). In huquq Allah, if forgetfulness is prevalent and unavoidable, it is pardoned – e.g., forgetting to eat while fasting, or forgetting tasmiyah when slaughtering. But in huquq al-ibad, forgetfulness does not excuse; liability remains. The author also applies this to the case of a forgetful person giving salaam during prayer: if it's a common occurrence due to forgetfulness, it does not invalidate the prayer, unlike intentional speech. The passage is from a Hanafi usul work, and the rulings cited (e.g., forgetfulness in fasting, tasmiyah in dhabihah) are standard Hanafi positions. The reasoning is based on the idea that such forgetfulness arises from the side of Allah (i.e., He created the distraction) and thus is excused. The text ends mid-sentence, likely continuing with an example of the first sitting (qada'ah ula).

Key Terms
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness – being unaware of something due to natural oversight, not illness.
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Rights of Allah – obligations purely for His worship.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-ibad): Rights of servants – obligations involving other people's rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is forgetfulness in fasting considered a cause of pardon according to the passage?
A) Because fasting is not an obligation
B) Because the forgetfulness arises from the side of Allah, the Owner of the right
C) Because eating forgetfully is not really eating
D) Because the fast was already complete

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, prevalent forgetfulness in huquq Allah is a cause of pardon, but in huquq al-ibad, liability remains.

Sleep and Coma as Impediments to Legal Capacity
Explains impediments to legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish sleep from coma in terms of their effects on legal capacity and apply the Hanafi rulings regarding utterances and prayer.

Core Idea
Sleep suspends choice; coma destroys it — thus sleep voids certain utterances while coma always invalidates wudu and prevents building prayer.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, certain states of unconsciousness affect a person's legal capacity (ahliyyah). This lesson examines the rulings for sleep (al-nawm) and coma (al-ighma) as presented in Al-Husami. You will learn how each state negates the ability to use power and how that impacts utterances of divorce, manumission, and conversion, as well as the validity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Define sleep and coma as legal impediments
Identify the two states from the passage: sleep is a natural rest (fatrah asliyyah) causing inability to use power; coma is an accidental state (arid) that fundamentally contradicts strength.
Both negate choice (ikhtiyar) but differ in nature.
2
Compare their effects on legal capacity
Sleep temporarily suspends capacity for utterances; coma permanently (during the state) destroys capacity more severely. Sleep is not a hadath; coma is always a hadath.
Coma prevents building prayer (bina), sleep does not.
3
Derive rulings for utterances
Both states render utterances of divorce, manumission, conversion to Islam, and apostasy void because they require conscious choice.
The ruling is based on the absence of volition.
4
Derive rulings for prayer
In sleep, recitation and speech in prayer have no ruling (do not invalidate); loud laughter in sleep also does not invalidate. In coma, the duration is considered for makeup prayers, and building is not allowed.
Coma requires renewing wudu and restarting prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَامَّا النَّوْمُ فَعَجْزٌ عَنْ اسْتَعْمَالِ الْقُدْرَةِ يُنَافِى الْإخْتِيَارَ فَاَوْجَبَ تَاخِيْرَ الْخِطَابِ لِلْآدَاءِ وَبَطَلَتْ عِبَارَاتُهُ اَصْلًا فِي الطَّلَاقِ وَالْعَتَاقِ وَالْإسْلَام وَالرِّدَّةِ وَلَمْ يَتَعَلَّقَ بِقِرَاء تِهِ وَكَلامِهِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ حُكْمٌ وَكَذَا إِذَا قَهْقَهَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ وَالْأَغْمَاء مِثْلُ النَّوْمِ فِي فَوْتِ الْاِخْتِيَارِ وَفَوْتِ اسْتَعْمَالِ الْقَدْرَةِ حَتَّى مَنَعَ صِحَّةَ الْعِبَارَاتِ وَهُوَ أَشَدُّ مِنْهُ لِاَنَّ النَّوْمَ فَتْرَةٌ أَصْلِيَّةٌ وَهَذَا عَارِضٌ يُنَافِي الْقُوَّةَ أَصْلًا وَلِهَذَا كَانَ حَدَثًا فِي كُلِّ الْأَحْوَالِ وَمَنَعَ الْبِنَاءَ وَاعْتَبَرَ امْتِدَادَهُ فِي حَقِّ الصَّلَاةِ خَاصَّةً - ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال نیند پس وہ قدرت کے استعمال سے ایسی عاجزی ہے جو اختیار کے منافی ہے، تو نیند ادا کے خطاب کی تاخیر کو واجب کرے گی، اور نائم کی عبارات طلاق، عتاق اور اسلام اور ردت میں بالکل باطل ہو جائیں گی اور نماز میں اس کی قرآت اور اس کے کلام سے کوئی حکم متعلق نہ ہوگا، اور اسی طرح جب اس نے اپنی نماز میں قہقہہ لگایا، یہی صحیح ہے۔ اور اغماء نیند کی طرح ہے اختیار کے فوت ہونے میں اور قدرت کے استعمال کے فوت ہونے میں، یہانتک کہ انماء عبارات کی صحت سے مانع ہے، اور اغماء نیند سے بڑھ کر ہے، اس لئے نیند ایک طبعی سستی ہے اور اغماء ایسا عارض ہے جو قوت کے بالکل منافی ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے اغماء تمام احوال میں حدث ہے اور اغماء بناء کے لئے مانع ہے، اور اغماء کا امتداد خاص کر نماز کے حق میں معتبر ہے۔
As for sleep, it is an inability to use power that conflicts with choice, so it necessitates delaying the address for performance, and his utterances are completely void in divorce, manumission, acceptance of Islam, and apostasy, and no ruling attaches to his recitation and speech in prayer. Similarly, if he laughs loudly in his prayer, that is the correct view. And coma is like sleep in the loss of choice and loss of the use of power, so that it prevents the validity of utterances, and it is more severe than it, because sleep is an original rest, and this is an accidental impediment that fundamentally contradicts strength, and therefore it is an event (hadath) in all states and prevents building upon previous prayer, and its duration is considered specifically in the right of prayer. Translation: As for sleep, it is such an inability to use power that it is contrary to choice, so necessary delayed performance, and the utterances of the sleeper are absolutely void in divorce, manumission, acceptance of Islam, and apostasy, and no ruling attaches to his recitation and speech in prayer. Similarly, if he laughed loudly in his prayer, this is the correct view. And coma is like sleep in the loss of choice and loss of the use of power, so much so that it prevents the validity of utterances, and it is more severe than sleep, because sleep is a natural rest, while coma is an accidental impediment that fundamentally contradicts power, and for this reason coma is a hadath in all states and prevents building upon previous prayer, and its duration is considered specifically in the right of prayer.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage discusses sleep (nawm) and coma (ighma) as impediments that affect legal capacity. The author states that sleep is a state of inability to exercise power, conflicting with choice. Therefore, a sleeping person's utterances are void when it comes to divorce, manumission, conversion to Islam, or apostasy. In prayer, his recitation and speech produce no ruling – i.e., they do not invalidate the prayer if done in sleep. Similarly, laughter in sleep does not break prayer (the correct view). Coma (ighma) is similar to sleep but more severe: it is an accidental state that contradicts strength, unlike sleep which is a natural rest. Coma always invalidates wudu (hadath) and prevents building upon previous prayer (i.e., if one regains consciousness, they must start anew). However, the duration of coma is considered only in relation to making up missed prayers. This is a standard Hanafi usul discussion on the impediments (awarid) of legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Key Terms
النوم (al-nawm): Sleep – a natural rest state that negates choice and power.
الإغماء (al-ighma): Coma – an accidental loss of consciousness that completely contradicts strength.
العبارات (al-ibarat): Utterances – specifically those of divorce, manumission, Islam, apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between sleep and coma regarding the validity of building upon previous prayer?
A) Sleep prevents building; coma does not
B) Coma prevents building; sleep does not
C) Both prevent building
D) Neither prevents building

Key Takeaway
Sleep and coma both void utterances of divorce, manumission, Islam, and apostasy, but only coma always invalidates wudu and prevents building prayer.

The Principle of Prevalence (Ghalabah) in Excusing Mistakes in Prayer
Ruling on unintentional salam during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify prevalence (ghalabah) as a cause for legal relaxation and apply it to distinguish between excused and unexcused acts in prayer.

Core Idea
Prevalence of a mistake excuses it; rarity makes it invalidating.

In Hanafi usul, the prevalence of an occurrence can lead to leniency in rulings. This lesson examines the case of accidentally saying salam during prayer, which is excused because such a mistake is common. We will see how the principle of ghalabah operates to lift the normal prohibition of speech in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being considered (salam) and what is the ruling? (excused, does not break prayer)
The act is salam said forgetfully during prayer.
2
Identify the effective cause (illa)
Why is salam excused? Because its occurrence is prevalent (ghalib) due to confusion between the first and last sitting.
Prevalence is the key factor.
3
Contrast with speech
Why is speech not excused? Because it is not prevalent; the prayer form reminds the person.
Rarity makes it invalidating.
4
Formulate the usul principle
Prevalence (ghalabah) leads to legal relaxation (takhfif) in the Hanafi school.
This is an application of istihsan based on 'urf.
5
Apply the principle broadly
Other similar prevalent mistakes in prayer may also be excused.
e.g., constant motion of a finger during tasbih may be excused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سلام پھیر دیا، تو یہ سلام معاف ہے، اس سے نماز نہیں ٹوٹے گی جب تک کوئی دوسرا منافئی نماز عمل کلام وغیرہ نہ کرے، البتہ تیسری رکعت کے قیام میں تاخیر کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا لیکن اگر نماز میں بھول کر کلام کر لیا تو یہ معاف نہیں ہے اس سے نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی، کیونکہ کلام غالب نہیں ہے یعنی عام طور نماز میں نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ نماز کی ہیئت یاد دلا دیتی ہے کہ نماز میں ہے ، اور سلام کا وقوع غالب ہے، کیونکہ قعدہ اولی اور اخیرہ میں اشتباہ ہو جاتا ہے،اس لئے اس کا وقوع کثرت سے ہے۔
If one (accidentally) turns around and gives greetings (salam), then this salam is forgiven; it does not break the prayer, unless another act contrary to prayer (like speech etc.) is committed. However, due to the delay in standing for the third rak'ah, prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah sahw) becomes obligatory. But if one speaks forgetfully during prayer, that is not forgiven; it breaks the prayer, because speech is not prevalent (i.e., it does not commonly occur in prayer, since the form of prayer reminds one that one is in prayer). The occurrence of salam is prevalent, because confusion occurs between the first and last sitting (qada'ah), hence its occurrence is frequent.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific exception to the general rule that any act of speech or action contrary to prayer invalidates it. The Hanafi ruling here is that accidentally saying salam during prayer due to confusion between the first and last tashahhud is excused and does not nullify the prayer, because such a mistake is common and the person does not intend to exit prayer. However, if one speaks words other than salam, even forgetfully, the prayer breaks because speech is not a common mistake. The rationale ('illa) is the prevalence (ghalabah) of the occurrence of salam in such situations. This is an example of how the law takes into account human nature and lifts hardship. The later requirement of sajdah sahw is due to the delay in standing, not the salam itself.

Key Terms
سلام (salām): The Islamic greeting of peace, also the concluding act of prayer.
معاف (ma‘āf): Forgiven, excused; the action is overlooked by the law.
غالب (ghālib): Prevalent, common occurrence; a cause for legal relaxation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is unintentional salam in prayer excused according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because salam is not a valid action
B) Because it is prevalent due to confusion
C) Because the prayer ends with salam
D) Because it is said silently

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the prevalence of a mistake (ghalabah) serves as an effective cause to excuse it, distinguishing it from rare errors that invalidate the act.

Sleep as an Excusing Factor in Hanafi Usul
Definition of sleep as an excusing factor and its legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sleep as a legal excusing factor and apply its effects on obligations and voluntary acts.

Core Idea
Sleep removes choice but does not drop obligations — it only delays them.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, certain natural conditions temporarily suspend the normal legal consequences of actions. Sleep is one such excusing factor. In this lesson, we examine the definition of sleep and its legal effects on acts like divorce, apostasy, and prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal nature of sleep
Recognize that sleep is categorized as a 'arid (excusing factor) that removes choice (ikhtiyar). The text describes it as a natural languor that arises involuntarily.
2
Understand the effect on obligations
Obligations (wajib) are not dropped but delayed; the address (khitab) is postponed until after waking. The sleeper remains liable.
3
List the acts invalidated by lack of choice
Acts requiring intention (niyyah) or choice are void: divorce, emancipation, apostasy, and recitation in prayer are invalid. Even involuntary speech does not break prayer.
The prayer is invalid if it depends on recitation that did not occur validly.
4
Distinguish involuntary speech and laughter
Involuntary speech during sleep is not considered real speech, so it does not invalidate prayer. For laughter (qahqaha), the mufta bihi view is that it breaks prayer, though some earlier views differed.
The text notes that another opinion holds laughter does not break prayer, but the relied-upon view is that it does.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Test the definition: if a sleeping person makes a contract of sale, is it valid? Apply the principle that choice is required for binding contracts; the sale is void.
This follows the same logic as divorce and emancipation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما النوم :- پانچواں عارض نوم ہے، نیند وہ طبعی کسل اور ستی ہے جو تھکن کی وجہ سے غیر اختیاری طور پر پیدا ہوتی ہے، اور انسان کے اختیار کو ختم کر دیتی ہے، لہذا نیند کی وجہ سے خطاب ادا مؤخر ہو جائے گا لیکن واجب ساقط نہ ہوگا اور چونکہ نائم کا اختیار ختم ہو جاتا ہے تو وہ عبارتیں جو اختیار پر مبنی ہیں باطل و غیر معتبر ہوں گی ، لہذا نائم نے اگر بیوی کو طلاق دی یا غلام کو آزاد کیا، یا اسلام قبول کیا یا مرتد ہو گیا، تو ان میں سے کسی کا بھی اعتبار نہ ہوگا، لہذا نائم کی نہ طلاق پڑے گی ، نہ آزادی واقع ہوگی ، اور نہ اسلام وارتداد کا اعتبار ہوگا، اور اگر اس نے نماز میں نیند کی حالت میں قرآت کی یارکوع ، سجدہ کیا تو غیر معتبر ہے، جب قرآت صحیح نہیں تو نماز صحیح نہ ہوگی، اسی طرح نیند کی حالت میں کلام کیا تو کلام کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا، لہذا اس سے نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ بے اختیار صادر ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ حقیقی کلام نہیں ہے ،اسی طرح اگر نماز میں نیند کی حالت میں قہقہہ لگایا تو اس سے بھی حکم متعلق نہ ہوگا یعنی نہ وضو ٹوٹے گا نہ نماز ٹوٹے گی لیکن مفتی بہ قول کے مطابق قہقہہ سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
As for sleep: The fifth excusing factor is sleep. Sleep is the natural languor and numbness that arises involuntarily due to fatigue, and it eliminates a person's choice. Therefore, due to sleep, the address (of obligation) is delayed, but the obligation does not fall. Since the sleeper's choice is eliminated, those expressions that are based on choice are void and invalid. Thus, if a sleeping person divorces his wife, frees a slave, accepts Islam or apostatizes, none of these are valid. So his divorce does not occur, emancipation does not take effect, and neither Islam nor apostasy is considered. And if he recites Quran, bows, or prostrates while sleeping in prayer, it is invalid; since recitation is not correct, the prayer is not valid. Similarly, if he speaks while sleeping, the speech is not considered, so the prayer does not become invalid, because it is real speech due to being involuntary. Also, if he laughs loudly (qahqaha) while sleeping in prayer, then no ruling attaches—neither wudu breaks nor prayer breaks, but according to the mufta bih (relied upon) view, laughing loudly invalidates prayer.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage defines sleep (nawm) as the fifth 'arid (excusing factor). It explains that sleep removes the faculty of choice (ikhtiyar), so any acts that require choice are null and void. The obligations (wajib) are not dropped but delayed until after waking. Specific rulings are given: divorce, emancipation, apostasy are invalid. In prayer, recitation and movements are invalid, and the prayer is not valid if it relies on them. However, involuntary speech does not break prayer. As for laughter, the majority view (mufta bih) is that it breaks prayer even in sleep. This shows the Hanafi principle that actions dependent on intention are invalid without it.

Key Terms
نوم (nawm): Sleep as a natural excusing factor that removes choice.
عارض (‘āriḍ): A legal excusing factor that temporarily suspends normal obligations or effects.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): Free choice or volition, required for many legal acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sleeping person divorces his wife, does the divorce take effect in Hanafi law?
A) Yes, because divorce is a verbal act.
B) No, because sleep removes choice.
C) Yes, if he has a history of divorce threats.
D) Only if he repeats it when awake.

Key Takeaway
Sleep is an excusing factor that eliminates choice, delaying obligations but not dropping them, and rendering all volitional acts void.

Definition of Ighma and Its Legal Rulings
Definition and comparison of ighma with sleep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ighma, distinguish it from sleep and insanity, and apply its rulings regarding wudu, prayer continuation (bina'), and the effect of prolongation (imtidad).

Core Idea
Ighma removes choice but not intellect; it is more severe than sleep but less than insanity in legal effect.

In this passage, the author introduces ighma (unconsciousness) as the sixth excusing factor. It is defined as an illness that weakens the senses but does not remove intellect, unlike insanity. Although similar to sleep in removing choice, ighma is more disruptive, affecting rulings on wudu, prayer continuation, and the dropping of prayers when prolonged. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi difference regarding how to calculate the dropping of prayers due to prolonged unconsciousness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the 'arid and its definition
Read the first part of the passage to identify the 'arid (excusing factor) being defined: ighma. Note its description as an illness that weakens faculties but does not remove intellect.
The author contrasts ighma with junun (insanity) where intellect is lost.
2
Compare ighma with sleep and insanity
Analyze the comparison: ighma is like sleep in removing choice, but ighma is more severe because it is unnatural and suspends all faculties. Understand why ighma always breaks wudu while sleep only does so in certain positions.
The difference arises from the nature of ighma as a complete suspension of power.
3
Derive rulings on wudu and prayer continuation
From the comparison, extract the ruling: ighma always breaks wudu, and if it occurs during prayer, bina' (continuing) is not allowed, unlike sleep.
This is a direct application of the definition and severity.
4
Analyze the condition of prolongation (imtidad)
Examine the condition: normally ighma is brief; if prolonged (more than a day and night), it takes the ruling of insanity and prayers are dropped. Note the two opinions (Shaykhayn vs. Imam Muhammad) on how to measure the prolongation.
The dispute focuses on whether to count by hours or by missed prayers.
5
Note the limitation of the ruling
Observe that this dropping of prayers applies only to prayer, not to fasting or zakat, where qada' is always required.
This shows the specificity of the ruling based on the nature of the act of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاغماء مثل النوم : - چھٹا عارض انماء ہے، یعنی غشی اور بیہوشی یہ ایک طرح کا مرض ہے جس سے انسانی قوی کمزور اور بے حس ہو جاتے ہیں، لیکن عقل زائل نہیں ہوتی ، بر خلاف جنون کے کہ اس میں عقل زائل ہو جاتی ہے، اور یہ بیہوشی نیند کی طرح ہے، نیند کی طرح بیہوشی میں بھی اختیار اور استعمال قدرت فوت ہو جاتا ہے، اور بیہوشی کی حالت کے سب کلام باطل ہیں، بلکہ بیہوشی اختیار زائل ہونے میں نیند سے بھی بڑھ کر ہے، اس لئے کہ نیند ایک طبعی سستی ہیں ، اور بیہوشی ایک غیر طبعی چیز ہے جو قوت کے بالکل منافی ہے، یعنی اغماء سے قومی بالکل معطل ہو جاتے ہیں، اسی لئے اعماء اور بیہوشی تمام احوال میں ناقض وضو ہے خواہ کروٹ پر لیٹا ہو یا ٹیک لگا کر یا کھٹر ا ہو، بیٹھا ہو یا رکوع ، سجدہ میں ہو، اور نیند صرف لیٹنے اور ٹیک لگانے کی صورت میں ناقض وضو ہے، باقی حالتوں میں ناقض وضو نہیں ہے، اور اگر اغماء نماز میں پیش آجائے تو بنا کو مانع ہے برخلاف نوم کے، اگر نماز میں پیش آجائے تو بیدار ہونے کے بعد بنا درست ہے۔ البتہ بیہوشی کبھی دیر تک ممتد ہو جاتی ہے، حالانکہ عام طور پر امتداد نہیں ہوتا ، اگر بیہوشی میں امتداد نہ ہو تو یہ نیند کے حکم میں ہے اور اگر امتداد ہو تو جنون کے حکم میں ہے، لہذا اگر بیہوشی ایک دن رات سے زیادہ ہو جائے تو نماز ساقط ہو جائے گی شیخین کے نزدیک گھنٹوں کے حساب سے ایک دن رات سے زیادہ ہو جائے تو نماز ساقط ہو جائے گی ، امام محمد کے نزدیک نمازوں کے حساب سے ہے، یعنی اگر چھٹی نماز کا وقت بھی آگیا تو نمازیں معاف ہیں ، اور اگر امتداد چھٹی نماز کا وقت آنے سے پہلے ختم ہو گیا تو نمازوں کی قضا لازم ہوگی لیکن روزے میں مہینہ بھر کا امتداد شاذ و نادر ہے، لہذا اگر مہینہ بھر بیہوشی کا امتداد ہو بھی گیا تو روزے ساقط نہ ہوں گے ، قضا لازم ہوگی ، اسی طرح زکوۃ بھی امتداد سے ساقط نہ ہوگی ، الغرض بیہوشی کے امتداد کا صرف نماز کے حق میں اعتبار ہے۔
And unconsciousness (ighma) is like sleep: The sixth excusing factor is ighma, i.e., fainting and unconsciousness. It is a kind of illness that weakens the human faculties and makes them senseless, but the mind is not lost, unlike insanity where the mind is lost. This unconsciousness is similar to sleep: just as in sleep, choice and ability to use power are lost. All speech during unconsciousness is void. Rather, unconsciousness is even stronger than sleep in removing choice, because sleep is a natural laziness, while unconsciousness is an unnatural thing that is totally contrary to power; i.e., from ighma the powers are completely suspended. For this reason, ighma and unconsciousness break wudu in all states whether one is lying on side, leaning, whether standing, sitting, bowing or prostrating. Sleep breaks wudu only when lying down or leaning, not in other states. And if ighma occurs during prayer, it prevents building upon (bina'), unlike sleep: if sleep occurs in prayer, one can continue after waking. However, sometimes unconsciousness becomes prolonged, though normally it is not. If unconsciousness is not prolonged, it has the same ruling as sleep; if prolonged, it has the ruling of insanity. Thus, if unconsciousness lasts more than a day and a night, prayer becomes dropped. According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in terms of hours: if it exceeds a day and a night, prayers are dropped. According to Imam Muhammad, it is by the number of prayers: if the time of the sixth prayer also arrives, then the prayers are excused; if the prolongation ends before the time of the sixth prayer, qada' (make-up) is obligatory. But for fasting, a month's prolonged unconsciousness is rare; even if a month of unconsciousness occurs, fasting is not dropped; qada' is obligatory. Similarly, zakat is not dropped by prolongation. In short, the consideration of prolongation of unconsciousness is only for prayer.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage discusses unconsciousness (ighma) as the sixth 'arid. It clarifies that while similar to sleep in removing choice, ighma is more severe because it is unnatural and completely suspends faculties. This has practical differences: ighma always breaks wudu, while sleep only does so in certain positions. In prayer, if ighma occurs, one cannot continue (bina' is prevented) because it is more disruptive. The extension (imtidad) of ighma has specific rulings: if it lasts more than a day and night, prayers are dropped for the duration, with a difference of opinion between the Shaykhayn (by hours) and Imam Muhammad (by number of prayers). This applies only to prayer, not to fasting or zakat, where qada' is always required. This shows that the law considers the severity and duration of the excusing factor.

Key Terms
اغماء (ighmā’): Unconsciousness or fainting, an excusing factor that removes choice but not intellect.
نوم (nawm): Sleep, a natural state that removes choice partially.
جنون (junūn): Insanity, which removes intellect.
بنا (binā’): Building upon or continuing a prayer after an interruption.
امتداد (imtidād): Prolongation or duration of unconsciousness affecting rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of ighma (unconsciousness) on wudu?
A) It breaks wudu only if the person was lying down.
B) It never breaks wudu.
C) It always breaks wudu regardless of posture.
D) It breaks wudu only if prolonged.

Key Takeaway
Ighma is defined as a removal of choice without loss of intellect, which leads to stricter rulings than sleep but milder than insanity, and its prolongation affects only prayer.
