Riqq as an Indivisible Legal Incapacity
Definition of riqq and its legal implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define riqq as a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi) and explain why it is indivisible, and identify the Hanafi dispute regarding partial emancipation.

Core Idea
Slavery is an indivisible legal status: a person is either fully a slave or fully free.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text defines slavery (riqq) as a legal incapacity initially legislated as punishment. The key point is that riqq is indivisible—a person cannot be partially a slave. This leads to a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, on whether emancipation can be partial. Understanding the definition and the dispute helps us grasp how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from legal concepts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of riqq
The passage defines riqq as 'ajz hukmi'—a legal incapacity. It originally was a punishment but now is a legal status that puts a person under ownership and exchange. Note that it is a description (wasf) that does not admit of division (tajazzi).
2
Examine the example from Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad gives a case: a person of unknown lineage acknowledges that half of him is a slave. The ruling is that he is considered fully a slave in all his affairs. This illustrates that partial slavery is not recognized; riqq applies in total.
This is from al-Jami' al-Kabir.
3
Understand the dispute on emancipation (itq)
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that emancipation is removal of ownership that is non-divisible; if only part of the ownership is removed, emancipation does not take effect until the whole is removed. Abu Hanifa, however, holds that ownership can be removed partially, so partial emancipation frees that part. The dispute hinges on whether the ruling of emancipation is indivisible.
4
Analyze the evidence (qiyas) used by Sahibayn
Sahibayn compare emancipation to washing limbs for wudu (each limb must be washed for prayer to be valid) and to number of divorces (each divorce counts separately but prohibition only after three). This analogy supports the indivisibility of emancipation.
The qiyas is based on the necessity of completion.
5
Identify the consequences of riqq on legal capacity
Because of riqq, the slave cannot own property (as a full owner) and cannot perform Hajj, as he lacks bodily self-possession. His bodily benefits belong to the master, except for physical acts of worship like prayer and fasting.
This shows the practical effect of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الرِّقُ فَهُوَ عَجْزٌ حُكْمِيٌّ شُرِعَ جَزَاءً فِي الْأَصْلِ لَكِنَّهُ فِي حَالَةِ الْبَقَاءِ صَارَ مِنَ الْأمُورِ الْحُكْمِيَّةِ بِهِ يَصِيْرًا الْمَرْءُ عَرْضَةً لِلتَّمَلُّكِ وَالْإِبْتِدَالِ وَهُوَ وَصْفْ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّجْزِى فَقَدْ قَالَ مُحَمَّدْ فِى الْجَامِعِ فِى مَجْهُولِ النَّسَبِ إِذَا قَرَآنَ نِصْفَهُ عَبْدُ فَلَانٍ إِنَّهُ يُجْعَلْ عَبْدًا فِي شَهَادَاتِهِ وَفِي جَمِيعِ أَحْكَامِه وَكَذَلِكَ الْعِتْقُ الَّذِى هُوَ ضِدُّهُ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُف وَمُحَمَّدٌ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى الْإِعْتَاقُ إِزَالَةٌ لِمِلْكِ مُتَجَرِّيَّ تَعَلَّقَ بِسْقُوطِ كَلَّه عَنِ الْمَحَلَّ حُكْمْ لَا يَتَجَزَأْ وَهُوَ الْعِتْقُ فَإِذَا سَقَطَ بَعْضُهُ فَقَدْ وَجِدَ شَطْرُ العِلةِ فَيَتَوَقَفَ الْعِتْقُ إِلَى تَكْمِيْلِهَا وَصَارَذْلِكَ كَغَسْلِ أَعْضَاءِ الْوُضُوءِ لِإِبَاحَةِ آدَاءِ الصَّلٰوةِ وَكَاَعْدَ ادِ الطَّلَاقِ لِلتَّحْرِيم وَهَذَا الزِقُ يُنَافِى مَالِكِيَّةَ الْمَالِ لِقِيَامِ الْمَمْلُوكِيَةِ مَالًا حَتَّى لَا يَمْلِكَ الْعَبْدُ وَالْمُكَاتَبُ الشَّسَرِئَ وَلَا تَصِحُ مِنْهُمَا حَجَةُ الْإِسْلَامِ لِعَدَمِ أَصْلِ الْقُدْرَةِ وَهِيَ الْمَنَافِعُ الْبَدَنِيَّةُ لِاَنَّهَا لِلْمَوْلَى إِلَّا فِيْمَا اسْتُثْنِيَ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الْقُرَبِ الْبَدَنِيَّةِ - ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال رقیت تو وہ ایسا عجز حکمی ہے جو اصل میں بطور سزا کے مشروع ہوا ہے لیکن رقیت حالت بقاء میں حکمی امور میں سے ہو گئی ، جس کی وجہ سے آدمی تملک اور ذلت کا نشانہ بن جاتا ہے ، اور رقیت ایسا وصف ہے جو تجزی کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے ، پس امام محمد نے جامع کبیر میں مجہول النسب کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ جب اس نے اقرار کیا کہ اس کا نصف فلاں کا غلام ہے، تو اس کو شہادت اور جملہ أحکام میں غلام شمار کیا جائے گا، اور ایسے ہی وہ عشق جو رقیت کی ضد ہے ، اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اعتاق غیر متجری ہے ، اس وجہ سے کہ اس کا اثر اور وہ عشق ہے غیر متجری ہے، اور امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ اعتاق ایسی ملک کو زائل کرنے کا نام ہے ، جو تجربی کو قبول کرتا ہے ، حالانکہ محل ( مملوک ) سے پورے ملک کے سقوط کے ساتھ ایسا حکم متعلق ہے جو غیر متجری ہے اور وہ عشق ہے ، پس جب ملک کا
As for slavery (riqq), it is a legal incapacity initially legislated as a punishment, but in its ongoing state it has become part of the legal matters, whereby a person becomes subject to being owned and exchanged. It is a description that does not admit of division. So Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' regarding a person of unknown lineage: if he acknowledges that half of him is the slave of so-and-so, he is considered a slave in his testimonies and all his rulings, and similarly for emancipation which is its opposite. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: Emancipation is the removal of non-divisible ownership; it is attached to the total removal of ownership from the subject, a ruling that does not admit of division, and that is emancipation. So if part of it falls, then half of the cause has been found, so emancipation stops until its completion. This is like washing the limbs of ablution to permit prayer, and like the number of divorces for prohibition. And this slavery (riqq) opposes ownership of property because the status of being owned stands as property, so that the slave and the mukatab do not own the [shar'i] property, and from them the Hajj of Islam is not valid due to lack of original ability (qudra), which is bodily benefits because they belong to the master, except for those bodily acts of worship that are exempted.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage defines riqq (slavery) as a legal disability (ajz hukmi) originally legislated as punishment but now a legal status. It is indivisible: a person is either fully a slave or free; part-slave status is not recognized. Imam Muhammad's example: if a person of unknown lineage admits that half of him is a slave, he is considered fully a slave in all rulings. Similarly, emancipation (itq) is indivisible: it removes ownership entirely. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) view it as a non-divisible ruling; if part of ownership is removed, it does not proceed until all is removed. This is contrasted with Abu Hanifa's view that ownership can be removed partially. The passage uses analogies: like washing limbs for wudu (each limb is part of the condition) and number of divorces (each divorce is a count). Finally, riqq prevents the slave from possessing property (as a full owner) and from performing Hajj because he lacks bodily self-possession; his bodily benefits belong to his master, except for physical acts of worship like prayer and fasting which are exempted.

Key Terms
رق (riqq): Slavery as a legal status of incapacity.
عتق (itq): Emancipation, freeing a slave.
تجزى (tajazzī): Divisibility; the quality of being divisible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on partial emancipation?
A) The slave is freed completely in both views
B) According to Abu Hanifa, the slave becomes half-free; according to Sahibayn, no emancipation occurs
C) The master can reclaim the freed half
D) The slave must be completely freed in both views

Key Takeaway
Riqq is an indivisible legal incapacity; this indivisibility governs rulings on emancipation and the slave's legal capacity.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Legal Definition and Indivisibility of Raqiyya (Slavery)
Defines raqiyya and discusses its indivisibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define raqiyya as a legal disability, explain its indivisibility using the example from al-Jami', and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the divisibility of 'itq.

Core Idea
Slavery is an indivisible legal disability; manumission's effect is also indivisible even if its cause (ownership removal) is divisible.

This passage from the Sharh al-Husami defines raqiyya (slavery) as a legal disability that is indivisible. It then examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person frees half of their slave, does the slave become half-free? The school's founding imams differ on whether the act of manumission ('itq) is divisible. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi usul classifies legal causes and effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of raqiyya
Note that raqiyya is described as a 'legal disability' (ajz hukmi) and a 'description that does not admit of division.' Identify its original purpose (punishment for kufr) and its continued legal effect.
The definition has two parts: origin and continuance.
2
Analyze the proof of indivisibility from al-Jami'
Examine the example: a man of unknown lineage confesses that half of him is a slave. The ruling is that he is considered a full slave in all legal matters, even though the confession only covered half. Why? Because the description of slavery (raqiyya) cannot be split.
The example shows that ownership can be partial but the status of slavery is entire.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'itq
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that manumission is indivisible because its effect (freedom) is indivisible. Abu Hanifa holds that the act of manumission is the removal of divisible ownership, so if half the ownership is removed, half the cause exists, but the actual freedom is suspended until the remaining half is also freed. Understand the causal reasoning (talil) behind each position.
Note the analogy to wudu and divorce given in the text.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamar al-khilaf)
Apply the two positions to the case of freeing half a slave. Under Abu Hanifa, the slave becomes half-free; under the Sahibayn, he remains completely enslaved until the other half is freed. This is the practical consequence of the theoretical dispute.
The text does not clearly declare one view as mufta bihi; both are recorded.
5
Summarize the legal effects of raqiyya
Note the final part of the passage: raqiyya prevents a slave from owning property (e.g., a female slave for marriage) and invalidates obligatory Hajj because the slave lacks fundamental capability (bodily benefits belong to the master).
This shows how the indivisible status affects multiple fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الرِّقُ فَهُوَ عَجْزٌ حُكْمِيٌّ شُرِعَ جَزَاءً فِي الْأَصْلِ لَكِنَّهُ فِي حَالَةِ الْبَقَاءِ صَارَ مِنَ الْأُمُورِ الْحُكْمِيَّةِ بِهِ يَصِيرُ الْمَرْءُ عُرْضَةً لِلتَّمَلُّكِ وَالْإِبْتِدَالِ وَهُوَ وَصْفٌ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّجْزِيَ فَقَدْ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي الْجَامِعِ فِي مَجْهُولِ النَّسَبِ إِذَا قَرَّ أَنَّ نِصْفَهُ عَبْدُ فُلَانٍ إِنَّهُ يُجْعَلُ عَبْدًا فِي شَهَادَاتِهِ وَفِي جَمِيعِ أَحْكَامِهِ وَكَذَلِكَ الْعِتْقُ الَّذِي هُوَ ضِدُّهُ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى الْإِعْتَاقُ إِزَالَةٌ لِمِلْكٍ مُتَجَزِّئٍ تَعَلَّقَ بِسُقُوطِ كُلِّهِ عَنِ الْمَحَلِّ حُكْمٌ لَا يَتَجَزَّأُ وَهُوَ الْعِتْقُ فَإِذَا سَقَطَ بَعْضُهُ فَقَدْ وُجِدَ شَطْرُ الْعِلَّةِ فَيَتَوَقَّفُ الْعِتْقُ إِلَى تَكْمِيلِهَا وَصَارَ ذَلِكَ كَغَسْلِ أَعْضَاءِ الْوُضُوءِ لِإِبَاحَةِ آدَاءِ الصَّلَاةِ وَكَعَدَدِ الطَّلَاقِ لِلتَّحْرِيمِ وَهَذَا الرِّقُ يُنَافِي مَالِكِيَّةَ الْمَالِ لِقِيَامِ الْمَمْلُوكِيَّةِ مَالًا حَتَّى لَا يَمْلِكَ الْعَبْدُ وَالْمُكَاتَبُ السَّرِيَّ وَلَا تَصِحُّ مِنْهُمَا حَجَّةُ الْإِسْلَامِ لِعَدَمِ أَصْلِ الْقُدْرَةِ وَهِيَ الْمَنَافِعُ الْبَدَنِيَّةُ لِأَنَّهَا لِلْمَوْلَى إِلَّا فِيمَا اسْتُثْنِيَ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الْقُرَبِ الْبَدَنِيَّةِ - ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال رقیت تو وہ ایسا عجز حکمی ہے جو اصل میں بطور سزا کے مشروع ہوا ہے لیکن رقیت حالت بقاء میں حکمی امور میں سے ہو گئی ، جس کی وجہ سے آدمی تملک اور ذلت کا نشانہ بن جاتا ہے ، اور رقیت ایسا وصف ہے جو تجزی کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے ، پس امام محمد نے جامع کبیر میں مجہول النسب کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ جب اس نے اقرار کیا کہ اس کا نصف فلاں کا غلام ہے، تو اس کو شہادت اور جملہ احکام میں غلام شمار کیا جائے گا، اور ایسے ہی وہ عتق جو رقیت کی ضد ہے ، اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اعتاق غیر متجزی ہے ، اس وجہ سے کہ اس کا اثر اور وہ عتق ہے غیر متجزی ہے، اور امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ اعتاق ایسی ملک کو زائل کرنے کا نام ہے ، جو تجزی کو قبول کرتا ہے ، حالانکہ محل ( مملوک ) سے پورے ملک کے سقوط کے ساتھ ایسا حکم متعلق ہے جو غیر متجزی ہے اور وہ عتق ہے ، پس جب ملک کا بعض حصہ ساقط ہو گیا تو علت کا نصف حصہ پایا گیا، پس عتق علت کی تکمیل تک موقوف رہے گا اور یہ ( اسقاط ملک) ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اعضاء کا غسل ( علت ہے ) نماز کی ادائیگی کی اباحت کے لئے، اور جیسے طلاق کے اعداد (علت ہیں ) تحریم کے لئے ، اور یہ رقیت مال کی مالکیت کے منافی ہے مال ہونے کی حیثیت سے مملوکیت کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے ، یہاں تک کہ غلام اور مکاتب ( جماع کے لئے ) تستری (باندی رکھنے ) کے مالک نہ ہوں گے، اور ان دونوں کی جانب سے اسلام کا فریضہ حج صحیح نہ ہوگا اصل قدرت کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے، اور قدرت وہ منافع بدنیہ ہیں، اس لئے کہ منافع آقا کے لئے ہیں، مگر ان بدنی عبادات میں جن کا استثنا کر دیا گیا۔
And as for slavery (raqiyya), it is a legal disability, originally legislated as a punishment, but in the state of continuance it became one of the legal matters; through it a person becomes a target of ownership and humiliation, and it is a description that does not admit of division. So indeed Muhammad said in al-Jami' regarding a person of unknown lineage: if he confesses that half of him is the slave of so-and-so, he is considered a slave in his testimonies and in all his rulings. And likewise manumission ('itq) which is its opposite. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: Manumission is the removal of divisible ownership, but it is connected to the fall of the entire ownership from the locus, a ruling that is indivisible, and that is manumission. So if part of it falls, half of the cause has occurred, so manumission is suspended until its completion. And that is like washing the limbs of ablution for the permissibility of performing prayer, and like the number of divorces for prohibition. And this slavery contradicts ownership of property because of the establishment of being owned as property, so that a slave and a mukatab do not own a female slave (for marriage), and the Hajj of Islam is not valid from them due to the absence of fundamental capability, and capability is bodily benefits, because they belong to the master except what is exempted from bodily acts of worship.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
یہ عبارت رقیت (غلامی) کے تعریف اور اس کے احکام پر مشتمل ہے۔ مصنف اسے عارض ساتویں کے طور پر پیش کرتے ہیں۔ رقیت کو عجز حکمی قرار دیا گیا ہے، یعنی شرعاً یہ ایک مجبوری ہے جو اصل میں کفر کی سزا کے طور پر مشروع ہوئی، لیکن حالت بقاء میں یہ محض ایک حکم شرعی بن گیا۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگرچہ ابتداء میں یہ صرف کافروں پر ثابت ہوتا تھا، لیکن اب اگر کوئی غلام مسلمان ہو جائے تو وہ غلامی کی حالت میں ہی رہے گا۔ رقیت ایک ایسا وصف ہے جو تجزی (تقسیم) کو قبول نہیں کرتا، یعنی انسان آدھا غلام اور آدھا آزاد نہیں ہو سکتا، کیونکہ یہ کفر کی سزا اور حق اللہ ہے، اور یہ دونوں غیر قابل تقسیم ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل امام محمد کی جامع کبیر کی روایت ہے کہ اگر کوئی مجہول النسب شخص اقرار کرے کہ اس کا نصف فلاں کا غلام ہے، تو اس اقرار کی وجہ سے نصف میں ملکیت تو ثابت ہوتی ہے، لیکن رقیت کے غیر متجزی ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ شخص تمام احکام (شہادت، وغیرہ) میں کامل غلام شمار ہوگا۔ اسی طرح عتق (آزادی) بھی رقیت کی ضد ہے اور اس میں بھی تجزی نہیں ہوتا۔ صاحبین (ابو یوسف اور محمد) کے نزدیک عتق بھی غیر متجزی ہے کیونکہ اس کا اثر (آزادی) غیر متجزی ہے۔ جبکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک عقت دراصل ملک کو زائل کرنے کا نام ہے، اور ملک تو متجزی ہے (آدھے حصے میں بھی ملک ہو سکتا ہے)، لیکن اس کا حکم (عتق) غیر متجزی ہے۔ اس لیے جب ملک کا کچھ حصہ ساقط ہوتا ہے تو عتق کے لیے پوری علت نہیں پائی گئی، اس لیے عتق مکمل ہونے تک موقوف رہے گا۔ یہ اس طرح ہے جیسے وضو میں اعضاء کا دھونا نماز کی اباحت کے لیے علت ہے، یا طلاق کی عدد تحریم کے لیے علت ہے۔ آخر میں بتایا گیا کہ رقیت مال کی ملکیت سے منافی ہے، اس لیے غلام اور مکاتب (وہ غلام جس سے کتابت ہوئی ہو) باندی (سری) کے مالک نہیں ہو سکتے، اور ان کا حج اسلام (فرض حج) صحیح نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ ان کے پاس اصل قدرت (بدنی منافع) نہیں ہوتی، کیونکہ بدنی منافع آقا کے ہوتے ہیں سوائے ان عبادات کے جن کا استثنا کیا گیا ہے جیسے نماز اور روزہ۔

Key Terms
الرق (al-riqq): Legal disability that is indivisible; originally a punishment for disbelief, now a purely legal status.
العتق (al-'itq): Manumission; removal of ownership. Its divisibility is disputed: Abu Hanifa says it is divisible, the Sahibayn say it is not.
التجزي (al-tajazzī): Divisibility. Raqiyya does not admit of tajazzi; ownership does.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person confesses that half of himself is a slave of someone, what is his legal status?
A) He is half-slave and half-free.
B) He is a full slave in all rulings.
C) He is fully free because the confession is invalid.
D) He is a slave only in matters of testimony.

Key Takeaway
Raqiyya is an indivisible legal disability; manumission's divisibility is disputed within the Hanafi school, with practical consequences for partial freeing.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Slavery and Property Ownership: The Principle of Incompatibility
Explains how slavery conflicts with property ownership and its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that slavery conflicts with property ownership and apply it to determine that a slave cannot own concubines or be obligated to perform Hajj.

Core Idea
A slave cannot simultaneously be property and own property — the legal status of riqq blocks full ownership.

In this lesson, we explore a foundational principle of Hanafi usul: the legal state of slavery (riqq) fundamentally conflicts with the capacity to own property. The author of Al-Husami explains that because a slave himself is owned, he cannot be a full owner of assets, leading to specific rulings on concubinage and the obligation of Hajj. We will unpack the logical reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
The text states that slavery conflicts with ownership of property. Determine what exactly is meant by 'conflict' (munafi) here.
2
Understand the rationale
The reasoning given is that being owned (mamluk) and being an owner (malik) cannot coexist because one implies power (qudra) and the other incapability (ajz).
3
Apply to concubinage
Since the slave cannot be an owner, he cannot possess a female slave for intercourse (tasarrari), even with the master's permission.
This is because full ownership (milk al-raqaba) is required.
4
Apply to Hajj
Hajj is not obligatory for a slave because the condition of istita'ah (capacity) is lacking; the master owns his physical benefits except for prayer and fasting.
The slave is considered free in matters of prayer and fasting only.
5
Note the exception
Prayer and fasting are unaffected because they require only the slave's own bodily acts, which are not owned by the master.
This is based on the principle that slavery does not negate religious obligations that are purely bodily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الرق ينافى : مصنف سے رقیت کا حکم بیان کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ رقیت مالکیت مال کے منافی ہے، یعنی غلام بحیثیت مال ہونے کے نہ کہ بحیثیت انسان ہونے کے اپنے آقا کا مملوک ہے، لہذا وہ مالک بننے کی اہلیت نہیں رکھے گا کیونکہ بیک وقت مالک بھی ہو اور مملوک بھی ہو ایسا نہیں ہوسکتا، کیونکہ مالک ہونا قدرت کی نشانی ہے اور مملوک ہونا عجز و بے اختیاری کی علامت ہے، پس جب رقیت مالکیت کے منافی ہے تو غلام اور مکاتب تسری کے مالک نہ ہوں گے یعنی وطی اور جماع کے لئے اپنے پاس باندی نہیں رکھ سکتے ،اگر چہ مولی اجازت دے اور نہ ان کی طرف سے حج کی ادائیگی درست ہے، اگر وہ حج ادا کریں گے تو نفل ہو گا چاہے مولی کی اجازت سے ہو، کیونکہ نماز ، اور روزہ کی ادائیگی کے علاوہ ان کے ہر طرح کے بدنی منافع کا مالک مولی ہوتا ہے، لہذا ان کو قدرت و استطاعت حاصل نہیں ہے جو وجوب حج کی شرائط میں ہے صرف نماز اور روزے میں جن بدنی منافع کی ضرورت پڑتی ہیں ان کے مالک خود ہیں، اور نماز روزہ کے حق میں یہ غلام نہیں ہوتے بلکہ آزاد ہوتے ہیں۔ وَالرَّقُ لَا يَنَا فِي مَالِكِيَّةَ غَيْرِ الْمَالِ وَهُوَ النِّكَاحُ وَالدَّمُ وَالْحَيوةُ وَيْنَا فِي كَمَالَ الْحَالِ فِي أَهْلِيَةِ الْكَرَامَاتِ الْمَوْضُوعَةِ لِلْبَشَر في الدُّنْيَا مِثْلُ الذَّمَّةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَالْحِلَّ حَتَّى اَنَّ ذِمَتَهُ ضَعْفَتْ بِرقِهِ فَلَمْ تَحْتَمِلِ الذَّيْنَ بِنَفْسِهَا وَضُمَّتْ إِلَيْهَا مَا لِيَةُ الرَّقَبَةِ وَالْكَسْبُ وَكَذَلِكَ الْحِلُ يَتَنَصَّفُ بِالزِقَ حَتَّى أَنَّهُ يَنْكِحُ الْعَبْدُ امْرَأَتَيْن وَتُطَلِّقُ الْآمَةُ ثِنَتَيْنِ وَتُنَصَفُ الْعِدَّةُ وَالْقَسَم وَالْحَدق انْتَقَصَتْ قِمْيَةُ نَفْسِهِ لِاَنَّهُ اَهْلْ لِلتَّصَرُّفِ فِى الْمَالِ وَاسِتِحْقَاقِ الْيَدِ عَلَيْهِ دُونَ مِلْكِهِ فَوَجَبَ نُقْصَانُ بَدَلِ دَمِهِ عَنِ الذِيَةِ لِنَقْصَانِ فِي أَحَدِ ضَرْبِيَ الْمَالِكِيَّةِ كَمَا تُنَصَّفُ الذِيَةُ بِالْأُنُوثَةِ لِعَدْمِ أَحَدِهِمَا وَهَذَا عِنْدَنَا أَنَّ الْمَادُونَ يَتَصَرَفْ لِنَفْسِهِ وَيَجِبْ لَهُ الْحُكْمُ الْاَصْلِى لِلتَّصَرُّفِ وَهُوَ الْيَدُ وَالْمَوْلٰى يَخْلُفُهُ فِيْمَاهُوَ مِنَ الزَّوَائِدِ وَهُوَ الْمِلْكُ الْمَشْرُوعُ لِلتَّوَضُلِ إِلَى الْيَدِ وَلِهَذَا جَعَلْنَا الْعَبْدَ فِي حُكْمِ الْمِلْكِ وَفِي حُكْمِ بَقَاءِ الْإِذْنِ كَالْوَكِيْلِ فِي مَسَائِلِ مَرَضِ الْمَوْلٰى وَفِي عَامَةِ مَسَائِلِ الْمَادُوْنِ
This slavery conflicts: The author, while explaining the ruling of slavery, says that slavery conflicts with ownership of property, meaning the slave, as property and not as a human, is owned by his master. Therefore he does not have the capacity to become an owner, because it is impossible to be both owner and owned simultaneously, since being an owner is a sign of power and being owned is a sign of incapacity. So when slavery conflicts with ownership, a slave and a mukatib cannot be owners of concubines, i.e., they cannot keep a female slave for intercourse, even if the master permits; nor is the performance of Hajj valid on their behalf. If they perform Hajj, it will be supererogatory, even with the master's permission, because the master owns all their physical benefits except prayer and fasting. Therefore they do not possess the capability and capacity that are conditions for the obligation of Hajj; they themselves own the physical benefits needed for prayer and fasting, and in respect of prayer and fasting, they are not slaves but free. And slavery does not conflict with ownership other than property, such as marriage, blood-money, and life. Rather, it conflicts with the perfection of capacity in the matters of honors placed for humans in this world, such as dhimma, guardianship, and sexual permission. So much so that his dhimma is weakened by his slavery, so it cannot bear debt by itself; rather, the property of the slave's neck and his earnings are attached to it. Similarly, sexual permission is halved by slavery, so that a male slave may marry two women, a female slave is divorced with two divorces, and the waiting period and division of nights are halved. The blood-money (diyah) for a slave is reduced to his market value, because he is eligible to handle property and have a hand over it, but not to own it. So the compensation for his blood must be less than full diyah, due to deficiency in one of the two types of ownership, just as diyah is halved for a woman due to the absence of one of them. And according to us, the slave (ma'dun) transacts for himself, and the basic ruling of transaction (which is possession of the hand) is established for him. The master takes his place in what are extras, which is the ownership legislated as a means to the hand. For this reason, we consider the slave in the ruling of ownership and in the ruling of continuation of permission like the agent in matters of the master's illness and in all matters of the ma'dun.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the legal consequences of slavery (riqq) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by stating that slavery conflicts with the ownership of property (malikiyyat al-mal), meaning a slave cannot be a full owner because he himself is owned. This principle leads to several rulings: a slave cannot own a concubine for intercourse (tasarrari) because that requires full ownership which the slave lacks. Similarly, Hajj is not obligatory for a slave because he lacks full capacity (istita'ah) – his physical benefits belong to the master except for prayer and fasting which are purely spiritual. The author then discusses the Arabic statement that slavery does not conflict with ownership in things other than property, such as marriage, blood-money, and life. Rather, it diminishes the perfection of capacity in matters like dhimma (legal capacity for debt), wilaya (guardianship), and hilla (permissibility for marriage). For example, a slave's dhimma is weak, so he cannot incur debt alone; the master's property is attached. Marriage permissions are halved: a male slave can marry two wives (free man can marry four), a female slave is divorced with two pronouncements (free woman with three), and waiting period and division of nights are halved. The blood-money for a slave is not the full diyah of a free person but is equal to his market value. This is because a slave has the capacity to transact (tasarruf) and possess a hand (yad) over property but not full ownership (milk). The deficiency in ownership type leads to reduction in diyah, analogous to the halving of diyah for a woman due to her gender. Finally, the author explains that when a slave is permitted to trade (ma'dhun), he acts for himself in acquiring things but the master ultimately owns the property. The slave is treated like an agent (wakil) for the master in certain financial matters. The passage systematically lists the effects of slavery on legal capacity, using analogical reasoning (qiyas) with the case of women's diyah.

Key Terms
رق (riqq): The legal state of slavery, which makes the person owned by another.
مالکیت (malikiyya): The right of ownership or dominion over property.
ذمة (dhimma): Legal capacity to incur obligations, particularly debts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed in this lesson, a slave cannot perform which of the following acts even with the master's permission?
A) Prayer
B) Fasting
C) Hajj as an obligatory act
D) Engaging in trade

Key Takeaway
A slave cannot own property because he himself is owned; this leads to specific rulings on concubinage and Hajj.

Slavery and Legal Capacity: Dhimma, Marriage, and Blood-Money
Explains the effects of slavery on dhimma, marriage, and diyah, including a qiyas with women's diyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how slavery weakens dhimma, halves marriage permissions, and reduces blood-money to market value, and apply the qiyas with women's diyah.

Core Idea
Slavery diminishes legal capacity in honorific matters but does not negate it entirely, leading to halved marital rights and reduced blood-money.

This lesson examines the second part of the passage, where the author explains that slavery does not conflict with ownership in non-property matters like marriage and blood-money, but rather weakens the perfection of capacity. We will study the effects on dhimma, marriage rights, and blood-money, culminating in a qiyas (analogy) with the halving of women's diyah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scope of the principle
The text states that slavery does not conflict with ownership of non-property (marriage, blood, life) but instead conflicts with the perfection of capacity in human honors like dhimma, guardianship, and sexual permission.
2
Examine the weakening of dhimma
A slave's dhimma is weakened by slavery; it cannot bear debt by itself, so the slave's property and earnings are attached to cover any debts.
This means the master's property is ultimately liable.
3
Examine the halving of marriage rights
A male slave can marry only two women (free man can marry four). A female slave receives only two divorces (free woman three). The waiting period and division of nights are also halved.
The Arabic phrase 'hatta innahu yankihu al-'abdu imra'atayn' explicitly states two.
4
Examine the reduction of diyah
The blood-money for a slave is his market value, not full diyah, because he has capacity for transaction (tasarruf) and possession (yad) but not full ownership (milk).
5
Study the qiyas with women's diyah
The slave's reduced diyah is analogous to the woman's halved diyah; both are due to deficiency in one of the two types of ownership (malikiyya). In women, it is due to gender; in slaves, due to servitude.
6
Understand the ma'dun (permitted slave)
When a slave is permitted to trade (ma'dhun), he transacts for himself, but the basic ruling of transaction (the hand) is for him, while the master takes the extras (ownership). The slave is treated like an agent (wakil).

وَيْنَا فِي كَمَالَ الْحَالِ فِي أَهْلِيَةِ الْكَرَامَاتِ الْمَوْضُوعَةِ لِلْبَشَر في الدُّنْيَا مِثْلُ الذَّمَّةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَالْحِلَّ حَتَّى اَنَّ ذِمَتَهُ ضَعْفَتْ بِرقِهِ فَلَمْ تَحْتَمِلِ Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Effects of Slavery on Legal Capacity in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the legal effects of slavery on ownership and dignities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi view on how slavery affects legal capacity (ahliyyah al-ada) in terms of ownership, marriage, dhimma, and hilla, and apply the distinction between mal and ghayr al-mal.

Core Idea
Slavery in Hanafi law does not negate legal capacity entirely; it restricts property ownership but preserves non-property rights and halves honorific capacities.

This passage from a commentary on a usul text explores how slavery (riqq) impacts the legal capacity of a human being. It draws a sharp distinction between ownership of property (mal) and ownership of non-property (ghayr al-mal) such as marriage, blood, and life. The slave retains capacity for non-property but suffers reductions in dhimma, hilla, and diya. Understanding these effects is essential for grasping the Hanafi framework of ahliyyah and the concept of partial legal personality.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish ownership types
Identify the two categories: mal (property) and ghayr al-mal (non-property). Slavery opposes ownership of mal but not of ghayr al-mal (marriage, blood, life).
Non-property items are those that cannot be fully replaced or are inherently personal.
2
Analyze the effect on dhimma
Slavery weakens dhimma; the slave’s dhimma alone cannot bear debt. Instead, the value of his person (raqaba) and his earnings are attached to it.
This is a form of limited capacity to incur obligations.
3
Apply the halving of hilla
Hilla (lawful capacity for marriage and divorce) is halved: male slave marries two, female slave receives two divorces. idda, nights division, and hadd are also halved.
The halving reflects the slave’s incomplete status as a legal subject.
4
Examine diya reduction
Blood money for a slave is less than that of a free person because the slave lacks full ownership over himself—only possession (yad) without full property (milk).
The reduction is analogous to diya being halved for a woman.
5
Note the agent-like treatment
The authorized slave (ma'dhun) is treated as an agent: he has possession (yad) but the master holds the ownership (milk). This affects rulings on master’s terminal illness and permission.
This illustrates that the slave’s capacity is functional but not absolute.

Source Text

ان کے نزدیک اعتاق میں تجری نہیں ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتاق در حقیقت ازالہ ملک کا نام ہے، اور اثبات عشق ضمناً ہورہا ہے، اس لئے امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتاق میں تجزی ہے۔
وهذا الرق ينافى :- مصنف سے رقیت کا حکم بیان کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ رقیت مالکیت مال کے منافی ہے، یعنی غلام بحیثیت مال ہونے کے نہ کہ بحیثیت انسان ہونے کے اپنے آقا کا مملوک ہے، لہذا وہ مالک بننے کی اہلیت نہیں رکھے گا کیونکہ بیک وقت مالک بھی ہو اور مملوک بھی ہو ایسا نہیں ہوسکتا، کیونکہ مالک ہونا قدرت کی نشانی ہے اور مملوک ہونا عجز و بے اختیاری کی علامت ہے، پس جب رقیت مالکیت کے منافی ہے تو غلام اور مکاتب تسری کے مالک نہ ہوں گے یعنی وطی اور جماع کے لئے اپنے پاس باندی نہیں رکھ سکتے ،اگر چہ مولی اجازت دے اور نہ ان کی طرف سے حج کی ادائیگی درست ہے، اگر وہ حج ادا کریں گے تو نفل ہو گا چاہے مولی کی اجازت سے ہو، کیونکہ نماز ، اور روزہ کی ادائیگی کے علاوہ ان کے ہر طرح کے بدنی منافع کا مالک مولی ہوتا ہے، لہذا ان کو قدرت و استطاعت حاصل نہیں ہے جو وجوب حج کی شرائط میں ہے صرف نماز اور روزے میں جن بدنی منافع کی ضرورت پڑتی ہیں ان کے مالک خود ہیں، اور نماز روزہ کے حق میں یہ غلام نہیں ہوتے بلکہ آزاد ہوتے ہیں۔
وَالرَّقُ لَا يَنَا فِي مَالِكِيَّةَ غَيْرِ الْمَالِ وَهُوَ النِّكَاحُ وَالدَّمُ وَالْحَيوةُ وَيْنَا فِي كَمَالَ الْحَالِ فِي أَهْلِيَةِ الْكَرَامَاتِ الْمَوْضُوعَةِ لِلْبَشَر في الدُّنْيَا مِثْلُ الذَّمَّةِ وَالْوِلَايَةِ وَالْحِلَّ حَتَّى اَنَّ ذِمَتَهُ ضَعْفَتْ بِرقِهِ فَلَمْ تَحْتَمِلِ الذَّيْنَ بِنَفْسِهَا وَضُمَّتْ إِلَيْهَا مَا لِيَةُ الرَّقَبَةِ وَالْكَسْبُ وَكَذَلِكَ الْحِلُ يَتَنَصَّفُ بِالزِقَ حَتَّى أَنَّهُ يَنْكِحُ الْعَبْدُ امْرَأَتَيْن وَتُطَلِّقُ الْآمَةُ ثِنَتَيْنِ وَتُنَصَفُ الْعِدَّةُ وَالْقَسَم وَالْحَدق انْتَقَصَتْ قِمْيَةُ نَفْسِهِ لِاَنَّهُ اَهْلْ لِلتَّصَرُّفِ فِى الْمَالِ وَاسِتِحْقَاقِ الْيَدِ عَلَيْهِ دُونَ مِلْكِهِ فَوَجَبَ نُقْصَانُ بَدَلِ دَمِهِ عَنِ الذِيَةِ لِنَقْصَانِ فِي أَحَدِ ضَرْبِيَ الْمَالِكِيَّةِ كَمَا تُنَصَّفُ الذِيَةُ بِالْأُنُوثَةِ لِعَدْمِ أَحَدِهِمَا وَهَذَا عِنْدَنَا أَنَّ الْمَادُونَ يَتَصَرَفْ لِنَفْسِهِ وَيَجِبْ لَهُ الْحُكْمُ الْاَصْلِى لِلتَّصَرُّفِ وَهُوَ الْيَدُ وَالْمَوْلٰى يَخْلُفُهُ فِيْمَاهُوَ مِنَ الزَّوَائِدِ وَهُوَ الْمِلْكُ الْمَشْرُوعُ لِلتَّوَضُلِ إِلَى الْيَدِ وَلِهَذَا جَعَلْنَا الْعَبْدَ فِي حُكْمِ الْمِلْكِ وَفِي حُكْمِ بَقَاءِ الْإِذْنِ كَالْوَكِيْلِ فِي مَسَائِلِ مَرَضِ الْمَوْلٰى وَفِي عَامَةِ مَسَائِلِ الْمَادُوْنِ

الفيضُ الحجازي ۳۶۴ شرح اردو المنجم الحسامي
ترجمہ :۔ اور رقیت غیر مال کی مالکیت کے منافی نہیں ہے، اور غیر مال نکاح ، دم ، اور حیات ہے، اور رقیت کمالِ حالت کے منافی ہے ان کرامتوں کے اہل ہونے میں جو دنیا میں انسان کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہیں ، جیسے ذمہ، ولایت اور حلت، یہانتک کہ رقیق کا ذمہ ضعیف ہے اس کے رقیق ہونے کی وجہ سے ، پس وہ ذمہ بذات خود دین کا متحمل نہیں ہوگا، اور ملا دیا جائے گا اس ذمہ کی طرف مالیت رقبہ اور کسب کو ، اور اسی طرح حلت آدھی ہو جاتی ہے رقیت کی وجہ سے، یہاں تک کہ غلام دوعورتوں سے نکاح کرے گا ، اور باندی کو دو طلاقیں دی جائیں گی ، اور آدھی ہو جائے گی عدت ، باری اور حد ، اور غلام کے نفس کی قیمت گھٹ جائے گی ، اس لئے کہ غلام اہل ہے مال میں تصرف کا ، اور مال پر قبضہ کے استحقاق کا نہ کہ مال کے مالک ہونے کا، پس اس کے خون کے بدل کا آزاد کی دیت سے کم ہونا واجب ہوگا ، مالکیت کی دو قسموں میں سے ایک میں نقصان کی وجہ سے، جیسا کہ دیت آدھی ہو جاتی ہے، انوقت کی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے، اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک ہے، اس لئے کہ ماذون تصرف کرتا ہے اپنے لیے ، اور تصرف کا حکم اصلی اور وہ قبضہ ہے۔ غلام ہی کے لئے ثابت ہوتا ہے، اور مولی اس کا نائب ہے اس چیز کے حکم میں جوز وائد میں سے ہے، اور وہ ملک ہے، جو مشروع ہے قبضہ تک رسائی کے لئے ،اور اسی لئے ہم نے غلام کو ملک کے حکم میں اور بقائے اذان کے حکم میں مثل وکیل کے قرار دیا آقا کے مرض الموت کے مسائل میں اور ماذون کے اکثر مسائل میں ۔
تشریح :- رقیت کا دوسرا حکم یہ ہے کہ رقیت غیر مال کی مالکیت کے منافی نہیں ہے یعنی غلام مال کے علاوہ دیگر چیزوں کا مالک ہوگا، جیسے نکاح غیر مال ہے، لہذا غلام نکاح کر سکتا ہے، کیونکہ فطری خواہش پوری کرنا شرعاً فرض ہے اور غلام کو باندی رکھنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے، لہذا نکاح کی صورت اس کے لئے متعین ہوگئی ، البتہ نکاح کا نفاذ مولی کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگا، کیونکہ نکاح سے اس پر عورت کا مہر واجب ہوگا جو غلام کے رقبہ سے متعلق ہوگا، یعنی مہر کی ادائیگی کے لئے غلام کو بیچنے کی بھی ضرورت پڑ سکتی ہے جس میں مولی کا ضرر ہے، اس لئے نکاح کا نفاذ مولی کی اجازت پر ہوگا، اسی طرح غلام اپنے خون کا مالک خود ہے کیونکہ انسان ہونے کی حیثیت سے وہ بھی زندہ رہنے کا مستحق ہے، اور خون کے تحفظ کے بغیر زندہ رہنا ممکن نہیں ہے، اسی لئے اس کا آقا بھی اس کی جان تلف کرنے کا حق نہیں رکھتا ہے، اور اگر غلام کسی کے قتل کا اقرار کرے تو اس پر قصاص آئے گا کیونکہ خون کے معاملہ میں غلام آزاد کے مشابہ ہے۔ البتہ رقیت ان کمالات کے حاصل ہونے کے منافی ہے، جن کو شرف و اعزار کی اہلیت میں دخل ہے، یعنی وہ اعزاز وشرف جو دنیا میں انسان کو حاصل ہوتا ہے ، وہ کامل شرف غلام کو نہیں ملتا اور وہ تین چیزیں ہیں (۱) ذمہ (۲) ولایت (۳) حلت ہر انسان کو ذمہ عطا کیا گیا ہے جس سے وہ اس کا اہل ہے کہ وہ دوسروں پر کوئی چیز واجب کرے اور
According to them, there is no partiality in emancipation, but according to Imam Sahib, emancipation is essentially the removal of ownership, and the affirmation of servitude is incidental, so according to Imam Sahib, there is partiality in emancipation. And this (concept of) slavery contradicts: the author states the ruling of slavery: that slavery is contrary to ownership of property, i.e., the slave, by virtue of being property, not by virtue of being a human, is owned by his master, therefore he is not eligible to own, because it is impossible to be both owner and owned simultaneously, because being an owner is a sign of power, and being owned is a sign of incapacity and helplessness. So when slavery is contrary to ownership, then the slave and the mukatab will not be owners of concubinage, i.e., they cannot keep a slave girl for intercourse, even if the master permits, and neither is their performance of Hajj valid; if they perform Hajj, it will be supererogatory even with the master's permission, because apart from prayer and fasting, the master owns all their bodily benefits, so they do not have the capability and capacity which is among the conditions for the obligation of Hajj. Only in prayer and fasting, where bodily benefits are needed, they are owners of themselves, and in regard to prayer and fasting, they are not slaves but free. And slavery does not oppose ownership of non-property, which is marriage, blood, and life, and it opposes perfection of state in eligibility for the honors placed for humans in the world, such as dhimma, guardianship, and hilla. So much so that the slave's dhimma is weak due to his slavery, so it does not bear debt by itself, and the property value of his person and his earnings are attached to it. Similarly, hilla is halved by slavery, so that the slave marries two women, and the slave girl is divorced twice, and the waiting period, division of nights, and hadd punishment are halved. The value of his person is reduced because he is eligible for disposition of property and entitlement to possession over it without ownership of it. Therefore, the compensation for his blood is necessarily less than the blood money of a free person, due to a deficiency in one of the two types of ownership, just as blood money is halved for femininity due to the absence of one of them. And this is according to us, because the authorized slave (ma'dhun) disposes for himself, and the original ruling for disposition, which is possession, is established for him, and the master is his successor in that which is among the additions, which is ownership, which is legislated as a means to possession. For this reason, we have made the slave with regard to the ruling of ownership and the ruling of continuation of permission like an agent in the issues of the master's terminal illness and in most issues of the authorized slave. Translation: And slavery is not contrary to ownership of non-property, and non-property is marriage, blood, and life. And slavery is contrary to perfection of state in being eligible for honors that are placed for humans in the world, such as dhimma, guardianship, and hilla. So much so that the slave's dhimma is weak due to his slavery, so that dhimma itself does not bear debt, and the property value of the person and earnings are attached to that dhimma. Similarly, hilla becomes half due to slavery, so much so that the slave marries two women, and the slave girl is given two divorces, and the waiting period, division, and hadd become half. And the value of his person is reduced, because he is eligible for disposition of property and entitlement to possession over it without his ownership, so it is necessary that the compensation for his blood is less than the blood money of a free person, due to a deficiency in one of the two types of ownership, just as blood money is halved for femininity due to the absence of one of them. And this is according to us, because the authorized slave (ma'dhun) disposes for himself, and the original ruling of disposition, which is possession, is established for him, and the master is his successor in that which is from the additions, which is ownership legislated as a means to possession. For this reason, we have made the slave in the ruling of ownership and in the ruling of continuation of permission like an agent in the issues of the master's terminal illness and in most issues of the authorized slave. Elucidation: The second ruling of slavery is that slavery is not contrary to ownership of non-property, i.e., the slave will be the owner of other things besides property, such as marriage is non-property, therefore the slave can marry, because fulfilling natural desire is legally obligatory, and the slave is not permitted to keep a slave girl, so marriage becomes the designated means for him. However, the validity of the marriage is contingent upon the master's permission, because marriage imposes the obligation of dower on him, which is related to the slave's person (raqaba), i.e., it may even necessitate selling the slave to pay the dower, which harms the master. Therefore, the marriage depends on the master's permission. Similarly, the slave himself is the owner of his blood because by virtue of being human, he is entitled to life, and without protection of blood, living is impossible. Hence, his master also does not have the right to take his life. And if the slave confesses to killing someone, then qisas (retaliation) will be due on him, because in matters of blood, the slave is similar to a free person. However, slavery is contrary to the attainment of those perfections that are involved in the eligibility for honor and dignity, i.e., the complete honor that a human obtains in the world is not attained by the slave. Those are three things: (1) dhimma, (2) guardianship, (3) hilla. Every human is granted a dhimma by which he is eligible to obligate something on others.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the legal effects of slavery (riqq) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by distinguishing the views on emancipation (itaq): according to Abu Hanifa, emancipation is essentially removal of ownership, with servitude being incidental, thus it allows partial manumission. The author then explains that slavery contradicts ownership of property: a slave, being himself property, cannot own other property because ownership and being owned are mutually exclusive. Consequently, a slave cannot own a concubine for sexual relations, even with the master's permission, and his Hajj is not valid as obligatory; if performed, it counts as supererogatory because he lacks full capability—the master owns his bodily benefits except for prayer and fasting, where the slave is considered free in that respect. The text then states a key principle: slavery does not oppose ownership of non-property (ghayr al-mal)—such as marriage, blood, and life. So a slave can marry, though it requires the master's permission due to financial implications, and he owns his blood, meaning his master cannot kill him, and he is subject to qisas for murder. Conversely, slavery opposes perfection in the eligibility for worldly honors (karamat) placed for humans: namely, dhimma (legal capacity to incur obligations), wilayah (guardianship), and hilla (lawful capacity, especially regarding marriage). The slave's dhimma is weak: it cannot bear debt by itself; instead, the value of his person (raqaba) and his earnings are attached to cover debts. His hilla is halved: a male slave can marry only two women (instead of four), a female slave receives only two divorces instead of three, and idda, division of nights, and hadd punishments are halved. The blood money (diya) for a slave is less than that of a free person because the slave lacks full ownership over himself (one of the two aspects of ownership—possession versus full property). The reasoning is that the authorized slave (ma'dhun) can transact for himself—the original right of possession (yad) is his—but the master substitutes him in ownership, which is a means to possession. Hence, in many rulings, the slave is treated like an agent (wakil) of the master, especially concerning the master's terminal illness and permission.

Key Terms
الرق (al-riqq): Slavery, a legal status that makes a human being the property of another, but with residual human rights.
الذمة (al-dhimma): A legal capacity to incur obligations (e.g., debt). For a slave, it is weak and cannot bear debt by itself; instead, the slave's property value and earnings are attached to it.
الحلة (al-hilla): Lawful capacity, particularly regarding marriage limits and divorce. For a slave, it is halved: male slave marries two, female slave receives two divorces.
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): An authorized slave, i.e., a slave given permission by his master to engage in trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of slavery on the slave's dhimma (legal capacity to bear debt)?
A) The dhimma is fully intact and can bear debt without any additions.
B) The dhimma is completely nullified; the slave cannot owe any debt.
C) The dhimma is weak and cannot bear debt by itself; the value of the slave's person (raqaba) and his earnings are attached.
D) The dhimma is halved, so it can only bear half the amount a free person can.

Key Takeaway
Slavery in Hanafi law partially restricts legal capacity: it prohibits ownership of property but preserves ownership of non-property (marriage, blood, life) and reduces honorific capacities like dhimma, hilla, and diya.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Second Ruling of Riqq: Ownership of Non-Property and Diminished Honors
Explaining that riqq does not negate ownership of non-property but conflicts with complete honors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two effects of riqq on legal capacity: that it does not negate ownership of non-property (marriage, life, blood) and that it diminishes three worldly honors (dhimma, wilayah, hill), and apply this distinction to derive specific fiqh rulings.

Core Idea
Riqq reduces a slave's worldly honors but does not strip ownership over marriage, life, and blood.

The second ruling on riqq is more nuanced: while slavery limits a slave's legal capacity in terms of honors and rights, it does not completely negate the slave's ability to own things that are not property. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi view of partial legal capacity (ahliyyah naqisa). This passage from Al-Fayd al-Hijazi unpacks this principle with specific examples, including the weakening of dhimma, halving of hill, and reduction of diya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main effects of riqq
The passage first states that riqq does not negate ownership of non-property (ghayr mal), then says it conflicts with perfect worldly honors (kamaal). Outline these two effects before diving into details.
Non-property includes marriage, blood, and life.
2
Recognize the three diminished honors
List the three honors that are diminished: dhimma (legal capacity), wilayah (guardianship), and hill (lawfulness, especially regarding marriage). These are the 'perfections' that a slave lacks due to riqq.
The passage emphasizes that these are worldly honors; in the afterlife, slaves and free are equal.
3
Understand the weakening of dhimma
The slave's dhimma is inherently present (as a human) but weak. Therefore, a slave cannot independently bear debt unless the master permits, effectively attaching the slave's monetary value and earnings to the dhimma.
This explains why a non-permitted slave (ghayr ma'dhun) is not liable for debts until freed or authorized.
4
Analyze the halving of hill and related consequences
Hill is halved: a male slave marries only two women (instead of four), a female slave's iddah is two periods (rather than three), the turn (nights) with a husband is halved, and the hadd punishment is half that of a free person.
The author links these to the deficiency in the slave's ownership of property (milk al-raqabah).
5
Examine the reduction of diya
The diya for a slave's life is less than 10,000 dirhams (the free diya), because the slave lacks one of the two types of ownership: ownership of disposition and possession (milk al-tasarruf wa al-qabd) is present, but ownership of the property itself (milk al-raqabah) is absent.
This distinction in ownership is the talil (legal cause) for the reduction.

شرح اردو المنجم الحسامي
ترجمہ :۔ اور رقیت غیر مال کی مالکیت کے منافی نہیں ہے، اور غیر مال نکاح ، دم ، اور حیات ہے، اور رقیت کمالِ حالت کے منافی ہے ان کرامتوں کے اہل ہونے میں جو دنیا میں انسان کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہیں ، جیسے ذمہ، ولایت اور حلت، یہانتک کہ رقیق کا ذمہ ضعیف ہے اس کے رقیق ہونے کی وجہ سے ، پس وہ ذمہ بذات خود دین کا متحمل نہیں ہوگا، اور ملا دیا جائے گا اس ذمہ کی طرف مالیت رقبہ اور کسب کو ، اور اسی طرح حلت آدھی ہو جاتی ہے رقیت کی وجہ سے، یہاں تک کہ غلام دوعورتوں سے نکاح کرے گا ، اور باندی کو دو طلاقیں دی جائیں گی ، اور آدھی ہو جائے گی عدت ، باری اور حد ، اور غلام کے نفس کی قیمت گھٹ جائے گی ، اس لئے کہ غلام اہل ہے مال میں تصرف کا ، اور مال پر قبضہ کے استحقاق کا نہ کہ مال کے مالک ہونے کا، پس اس کے خون کے بدل کا آزاد کی دیت سے کم ہونا واجب ہوگا ، مالکیت کی دو قسموں میں سے ایک میں نقصان کی وجہ سے، جیسا کہ دیت آدھی ہو جاتی ہے، انوقت کی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے، اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک ہے، اس لئے کہ ماذون تصرف کرتا ہے اپنے لیے ، اور تصرف کا حکم اصلی اور وہ قبضہ ہے۔ غلام ہی کے لئے ثابت ہوتا ہے، اور مولی اس کا نائب ہے اس چیز کے حکم میں جوز وائد میں سے ہے، اور وہ ملک ہے، جو مشروع ہے قبضہ تک رسائی کے لئے ،اور اسی لئے ہم نے غلام کو ملک کے حکم میں اور بقائے اذان کے حکم میں مثل وکیل کے قرار دیا آقا کے مرض الموت کے مسائل میں اور ماذون کے اکثر مسائل میں ۔
تشریح :- رقیت کا دوسرا حکم یہ ہے کہ رقیت غیر مال کی مالکیت کے منافی نہیں ہے یعنی غلام مال کے علاوہ دیگر چیزوں کا مالک ہوگا، جیسے نکاح غیر مال ہے، لہذا غلام نکاح کر سکتا ہے، کیونکہ فطری خواہش پوری کرنا شرعاً فرض ہے اور غلام کو باندی رکھنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے، لہذا نکاح کی صورت اس کے لئے متعین ہوگئی ، البتہ نکاح کا نفاذ مولی کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگا، کیونکہ نکاح سے اس پر عورت کا مہر واجب ہوگا جو غلام کے رقبہ سے متعلق ہوگا، یعنی مہر کی ادائیگی کے لئے غلام کو بیچنے کی بھی ضرورت پڑ سکتی ہے جس میں مولی کا ضرر ہے، اس لئے نکاح کا نفاذ مولی کی اجازت پر ہوگا، اسی طرح غلام اپنے خون کا مالک خود ہے کیونکہ انسان ہونے کی حیثیت سے وہ بھی زندہ رہنے کا مستحق ہے، اور خون کے تحفظ کے بغیر زندہ رہنا ممکن نہیں ہے، اسی لئے اس کا آقا بھی اس کی جان تلف کرنے کا حق نہیں رکھتا ہے، اور اگر غلام کسی کے قتل کا اقرار کرے تو اس پر قصاص آئے گا کیونکہ خون کے معاملہ میں غلام آزاد کے مشابہ ہے۔ البتہ رقیت ان کمالات کے حاصل ہونے کے منافی ہے، جن کو شرف و اعزار کی اہلیت میں دخل ہے، یعنی وہ اعزاز وشرف جو دنیا میں انسان کو حاصل ہوتا ہے ، وہ کامل شرف غلام کو نہیں ملتا اور وہ تین چیزیں ہیں (۱) ذمہ (۲) ولایت (۳) حلت ہر انسان کو ذمہ عطا کیا گیا ہے جس سے وہ اس کا اہل ہے کہ وہ دوسروں پر کوئی چیز واجب کرے اور
اس کا بھی اہل ہے کہ اس پر کوئی چیز واجب ہو، اسی ذمہ کی وجہ سے انسان حیوانات سے ممتاز ہے، یہ ذمہ غلام کا ناقص ہوتا ہے ، ولایت یعنی دوسروں پر قول نافذ کرنا ، غلام ولایت کا اہل نہیں ہے ، اسی طرح حلت نساء بھی غلام کے لئے ناقص ہے، آزاد چار عورتوں سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے، غلام صرف دو سے کر سکتا ہے، البتہ اخروی شرافت میں غلام اور آزاد برابر ہیں، کیونکہ اس کا مدار تقوی پر ہیں، ان اکرمکم عند الله اتقاكم ۔
حتى ان ذمته - مصنف مذکورہ تینوں چیزوں میں بسبب رقیت جو نقصان ہے اس کی وضاحت کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام میں انسان ہونے کے وجہ سے اصل ذمہ تو ثابت ہے، لیکن رقیت کی وجہ سے وہ ذمہ کمزور ہے، پس ذمہ ناقص ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ غلام بذات خود دین کا متحمل نہیں ہوگا ، یعنی اگر وہ غلام غیر ماذون في التجارة ہے تو اس سے فی الحال دین کا مطالبہ نہیں کیا جائے گا، بلکہ آزاد ہونے کے بعد مطالبہ کیا جائے گا، کیوں کہ غلامی کی وجہ سے ایک دوسرے کے دین کے واجب ہونے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے، لیکن چونکہ میں غلام اصل ذمہ موجود ہے، اس لئے اگر مالیت رقبہ اور کسب کو ذمہ کے ساتھ ملا دیا گیا تو ذمہ دئین کا متحمل ہو جائے گا ، مالیت رقبہ اور کسب کو ملانے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آقا اس کو تصرف کی اجازت دیدے ، اب اگر غلام نے کسی کا مال تلف کیا، یا مقروض ہو گیا تو کما کر ضمان ادا کرے گا یا پھر دین کے لئے اس کو بیچا جائے گا، تو آقا کا تصرف کی اجازت دینا، اس کے ذمہ کے ساتھ مالیت رقبہ اور کسب کو ملانا ہے، اور جب یہ ذمہ کے ساتھ مل گیا تو اب غلام دین کا متحمل ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ نفسِ ذمہ موجود ہے۔ اسی طرح رقیت کی وجہ سے حلت میں بھی تنصیف ہوگی، لہذا غلام دوعورتوں سے نکاح کرسکتا ہے ،اور باندی دو طلاق سے مغلظہ ہو جائے گی ، اس کا شوہر چاہے آزاد ہو یا غلام، اور باندی کی عدت بھی آدھی ہوگی یعنی دو حیض ، جب که آزاد عورت کی تین حیض ہے، اور اسی طرح قسم یعنی رات گزارنے کی باری یہ بھی نعمت ہے، اس میں بھی منکوحہ باندی کا حق آدھا ہوگا ، اور اسی طرح حد نا فرمانی کی سزا اور عقوبت ہے، یہ بھی غلام میں آزاد کی بہ نسبت آدھی ہوگی ، آزاد
میں اللہ کی نعمت کامل ہے تو عقوبت بھی کامل اور غلام میں اللہ کی نعمت ناقص ہے، تو عقوبت اور حد بھی ناقص ہوگی۔ وانتقصت قيمة نفسه : - رقیت کی وجہ سے غلام کی جان کی قیمت بھی آزاد سے کم ہوگی ، لہذا اگر کسی نے غلام کو خطا قتل کر دیا تو قاتل کے عاقلہ (ذمہ داروں) پر دس ہزار درہم سے کچھ کم درہم واجب ہوں گے، چاہے
غلام کی قیمت دس ہزار سے زیادہ ہو، اور اگر غلام کی قیمت دس ہزار سے کم ہے تو قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ دیت کم واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مالکیت دوقسم کی ہیں (۱) مال میں تصرف اور قبضہ کا مالک ہونا اور عین مال کا بھی مالک ہونا ، آزاد میں یہ مالکیت کامل ہے ، غلام میں ناقص ہے، کیونکہ غلام قبضہ اور تصرف کا تو مالک ہوتا ہے، عین مال کا مالک نہیں ہوتا ، (۲) غیر مال کی مالکیت جیسے نکاح سے ملک متعہ کی مالکیت ، یہ مالکیت صرف مذکر کو حاصل
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi. Commentary in Urdu on al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Translation: And riqq (slavery) does not contradict ownership of non-property. Non-property is marriage, blood, and life. And riqq contradicts the perfect state [that is required] for being worthy of those honors that are established for human beings in this world, such as dhimma (legal capacity), wilayah (guardianship), and hill (lawful things). So much so that the dhimma of a slave is weak because of his being a slave. Thus that dhimma by itself will not bear debt, and the monetary value of his person and his earnings will be attached to that dhimma. Similarly, hill becomes half because of riqq, so that a male slave will marry two women, and a female slave will be given two divorces, and her iddah, turn, and hadd punishment will be halved. And the value of the slave's own self is reduced, because the slave is capable of disposing of property and is entitled to possession of property, not of being a possessor of the property itself. Therefore, the blood-money for his life must be less than the diya of a free person, due to the deficiency in one of the two types of ownership. For example, diya becomes half due to being female, because one of the two [types of ownership] is missing. And this is according to us, because the ma'dhun (permitted slave) acts for himself, and the primary ruling of disposition is established for the slave himself, and the master is his deputy in the ruling of that which is profit, and that is ownership, which is legislated to attain possession. And for this reason we have considered the slave like a wakeel (agent) in the rulings of the master's death-illness and in most rulings of the ma'dhun. Explanation: The second ruling of riqq is that riqq does not contradict ownership of non-property, meaning the slave will be the owner of things other than property, such as marriage which is non-property. Hence the slave can marry, because fulfilling natural desire is obligatory in Shari'ah and the slave is not permitted to keep a concubine (bāndī), so the method of marriage becomes specified for him. However, the enforcement of the marriage is dependent on the master's permission, because the marriage obligates a dower (mahr) from the slave which is attached to his person, meaning that the slave may need to be sold to pay the dower, causing loss to the master. Therefore, the marriage is carried out only with the master's permission. Similarly, the slave is the owner of his own blood, because as a human being he is also entitled to live, and it is impossible to live without the protection of blood. For this reason, even his master does not have the right to kill him, and if the slave confesses to killing someone, qisas will be applicable to him because in matters of blood the slave is like a free person. However, riqq contradicts the attainment of those perfections that are involved in honor and dignity, i.e., the honor and dignity that a person obtains in this world – the complete honor is not granted to a slave. And these are three things: (1) dhimma, (2) wilayah, (3) hill. Every human is given dhimma, due to which he is capable of making something obligatory upon others and is also capable of having something obligatory upon him. Because of this dhimma, humans are distinguished from animals. This dhimma of a slave is deficient. Wilayah, i.e., making one's word effective over others – the slave is not capable of wilayah. Similarly, hill of women is also deficient for a slave; a free man can marry four women, a slave can only marry two. However, in the hereafter, slave and free are equal because its basis is taqwa: 'Verily the most noble of you in the sight of Allah is the most righteous.' Until that his dhimma – The author is explaining the loss that occurs due to riqq in these three things. He says that in the slave, due to being human, the original dhimma is established, but because of riqq, that dhimma is weak. So because the dhimma is deficient, that slave by himself will not bear debt. That is, if the slave is not permitted to trade, then debt will not be demanded from him at present; rather it will be demanded after emancipation. Because due to slavery he does not have the capacity for debt to be obligatory upon him from another. However, since the original dhimma exists in the slave, if the monetary value of his person and his earnings are attached to the dhimma, then the dhimma will bear debt. Attaching the monetary value of his person and earnings means that the master gives him permission to transact. Now if the slave destroys someone's property or becomes indebted, he will pay the guarantee by earning, or he will be sold for the debt. So the master's giving permission to transact is attaching the monetary value of his person and earnings to his dhimma. When this is attached to the dhimma, then the slave will bear debt because the dhimma itself exists. Similarly, because of riqq, hill is also halved, so a male slave can marry two women, and a female slave will become irrevocably divorced (mughtalazh) with two divorces, whether her husband is free or a slave. And the iddah of a female slave is also half, i.e., two menstrual periods, whereas the free woman's is three. Similarly, the turn (i.e., spending the night) is also a favor – in this too, the right of a married bondwoman will be half. Similarly, the hadd punishment for disobedience is a retribution – this too will be half in a slave compared to a free person. In the free person, Allah's favor is complete, so the punishment is also complete. In the slave, Allah's favor is deficient, so the punishment and hadd are also deficient. And the value of his own self is reduced: Because of riqq, the value of the slave's life is less than that of a free person. Therefore, if someone kills a slave by mistake, the killer's 'aajila (responsible ones) will owe a few dirhams less than ten thousand dirhams, even if the slave's value is more than ten thousand. And if the slave's value is less than ten thousand, then the value will be owed. The proof for the diya being less is that ownership is of two types: (1) Ownership of disposition and possession in property, and also ownership of the property itself. In a free person, this ownership is complete. In a slave, it is deficient, because the slave is capable of possession and disposition, but not of being the owner of the property itself. (2) Ownership of non-property, such as the ownership of usufruct (milk al-mut'a) through marriage. This ownership is obtained only by males.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the second ruling of riqq (slavery) according to the Hanafi school. The author clarifies that riqq does not prevent a slave from owning things that are not property (ghayr mal), such as marriage (nikah), blood (dam), and life (hayat). Thus, a slave can marry, own his blood (meaning his life is protected), and has the right to life. However, riqq does conflict with the complete state of certain honors (kamaal) that are specific to this world: dhimma (legal capacity), wilayah (guardianship), and hill (lawfulness, especially regarding marriage). The passage details how each of these is diminished due to riqq. Dhimma is weak, so a non-permitted slave cannot independently incur debt unless the master attaches the slave's monetary value and earnings to his dhimma by permitting trade. Hill is halved: a male slave can marry only two women (instead of four), a female slave's iddah is two menstrual periods (instead of three), the turn (nights spent with husband) is halved, and the hadd punishment is halved. The value of the slave's life (diya) is reduced because the slave's ownership is incomplete—he can possess and dispose of property but does not own the property itself (milk al-raqabah). Therefore, if a slave is killed by mistake, the diya is less than that of a free person (which is 10,000 dirhams), and it is adjusted based on the slave's actual value if less than that amount. The passage also notes that in matters of blood (like qisas for murder), the slave is like a free person. The Hanafi basis for these rulings is the distinction between two types of ownership: ownership of property (complete in free) and ownership of non-property (only males can own the usufruct of marriage). The author compares the permitted slave (ma'dhun) to a wakeel (agent) in some rulings. This is a clear Hanafi doctrine, differentiating from other schools in the details of diya and marriage limits.

Key Terms
رقیت (riqq): Slavery, a legal status that reduces but does not eliminate human capacity for ownership and obligations
ذمہ (dhimma): Legal capacity to incur obligations and have others incur obligations on one. In a slave, it is weak or deficient without master's permission.
حلت (hill): Lawfulness, especially regarding marriage (hill al-nisa). For a slave, it is halved: can marry only two women.
دیت (diya): Blood-money for unintended killing. For a slave, it is less than full diya of a free person (10,000 dirhams), based on the slave's property value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many wives can a male slave marry?
A) Four
B) Two
C) One
D) None

Key Takeaway
Riqq diminishes a slave's worldly honors (dhimma, wilayah, hill) and halves certain rights, but does not negate ownership of marriage, life, and blood.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Slavery as a Legal Incapacity (Ajz Hukmi) and Its Exceptions
Effects of slavery on legal capacity with exceptions and dispute on accidental homicide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that slavery is an ajz hukmi to derive rulings on jihad, spoils, aman, iqrar, and accidental jinaayah, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf in the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on jinaayah.

Core Idea
Slavery is a legal incapacity that severs wilayat but, by permission, can restore capacity for aman and iqrar.

This passage from a Hanafi usul work systematically lays out the effects of slavery (riqq) on legal capacity. It begins by affirming that slavery does not affect the sanctity of life (ismah) – a slave's life is protected like a free person's. Then it lists the consequences: slavery makes jihad non-obligatory, reduces spoils share, and cuts off all forms of wilayat. However, there is an important exception: the aman (safe conduct) of a ma'dhun (permitted) slave is valid because permission removes it from the categories of wilayat. Similarly, the ma'dhun's confession in certain crimes is valid. The passage concludes with a well-known dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the slave's accidental homicide (jinaayah bil-khata). Understanding how these rulings flow from the single 'illah of legal incapacity (ajz hukmi) is key to mastering Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational principle
Recognize that the passage treats slavery as an ajz hukmi (legal incapacity) that severs all forms of wilayat. List the rulings that directly follow from this: jihad not required, no full share of spoils, no wilayat over others.
The incapacity is 'hukmi' (legal) rather than physical; it is a construct of law.
2
Distinguish between general incapacities and exceptions
Note that for the ma'dhun (permitted) slave, certain acts like aman and iqrar are valid because the master's permission effectively removes the incapacity for those specific acts. The passage explains that aman by permission 'exits the categories of wilayat'.
Permission does not restore general capacity; it only opens specific doors, such as partnership in spoils.
3
Analyze the qiyas for accidental jinaayah
Compare the free person's accidental killing (diyah from own wealth) to the slave's. The illa is that the slave cannot guarantee what is not property (damān mā laysa bi-māl). Therefore, the slave himself becomes the compensation (jaza') unless the master ransoms.
This is qiyas khafī (hidden analogy) because the slave is not literally property but is treated as such for liability.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that if the master ransoms, the obligation returns to the original amount (the ransom) and is not nullified by insolvency. Sahibayn hold that it becomes like a hawala (transfer of debt), implying a monetary obligation that can be transferred.
The thamarah al-khilaf: whether the liability is in person (slave as object) or as a debt (master's responsibility).

وَالرِّقُ لَا يُؤْثِرَ فِي عِصْمَةِ الدَّمِ وَإِنَّمَا يُؤْثِرَ فِي قِيْمَتِهِ وَإِنَّمَا الْعِصْمَةُ بِالْإِيْمَانِ وَالدَّارِ وَالْعَبْدُ فِيهِ مِثْلُ الْحُرِ وَلِذَلِكَ يُقْتَلُ الْحُرُّ بِالْعَبْدِ قِصَاصًا وَأَوْجَبَ الرِقُ نَقْصَانًا فِي الْجِهَادِ حَتَّى لَا يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ لاَنَ اِسْتِطَاعَتَهُ فِي الْحَجَ وَالْجِهَادِ غَيْرَ مُسْتَثْنَاةٍ عَلَى الْمَوْلى وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَسْتَوْجِبْ السَّهْمَ الْكَامِلَ مِنَ الْغَنِيْمَةِ وَانْقَطَعَتْ الْوِلَايَاتُ كُلُّهَا بِالرّقِ لأَنَّهُ عَجْزٌ حُكْمِيٌّ وَإِنَّمَا صَعَ أَمَانَ الْمَأْذُوْنِ لآنَ الْآمَانَ بِالْإِذْنِ يَخْرُجُ عَنْ أَقْسَامِ الْوِلَايَةِ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنَّهُ صَارَ شَرِيكًا فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ فَلَوْزِمَهُ ثُمَّ تَعَدَّى إلى غَيْرِهِ مِثْلُ شَهَادَتِهِ بِهِلَالِ رَمَضَانَ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْاَصْلِ يَصِحُ اِقْرَارُهُ بِالْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَبِالسَرَقَةِ الْمُسْتَهْلَكَةِ وَبِالْقَائِمَةِ صَحَ مِنَ الْمَاذُوْنِ وَفِي الْمَحْجُودِ اِخْتِلَافٌ مَعْرُوفٌ وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا فِي جِنَايَةِ الْعَبْدِ خَطَاء أَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ جَزَاءً لِجِنَايَتِهِ لِاَنَّ الْعَبْدَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِ ضَمَانٍ مَا لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشَاءَ الْمَوْلَى الْفِدَاءَ فَيَصِيرُ عَائِدًا إِلَى الْأَصْلِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ اللَّهِ حَتَّى لَا يَبْطُلُ بِالْإِفْلَاسِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَصِيْرُ بِمَعْنَى الْحَوَالَةِ . ترجمہ: اور رقیت خون کی عصمت میں مؤثر نہیں ہے، البتہ غلام کی قیمت میں مؤثر ہے، اور عصمت ایمان اور دار الاسلام سے حاصل ہوتی ہے، اور غلام اس میں آزاد کے مانند ہے، اسی وجہ سے آزاد کو غلام کے بدلہ میں قصاصا قتل کیا جائے گا، اور رقیت جہاد میں نقصان پیدا کرے گی ، یہاں تک کہ غلام پر جہاد واجب نہ ہوگا، اس لئے کہ حج اور جہاد میں اس کی استطاعت کا مولی پر استثنا نہیں کیا گیا ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے غلام غنیمت کے کامل حصہ کا مستحق نہ ہوگا، اور رقیت کی وجہ سے تمام ولایات منقطع ہو جائیں گی، اس لئے کہ رقیت ایک عجز حکمی ہے، اور ماذون کا امان صحیح ہے، اس لئے کہ امان مولی کی اجازت کی وجہ سے اقسام ولایت سے خارج ہو جائے گا، اس وجہ سے کہ غلام غنیمت میں شریک ہو گیا، پس امان کا حکم غلام پر لازم ہوگا، پھر اس کے غیر کی طرف متعدی ہوگا، جیسے رمضان کے چاند کے بارے میں غلام کی شہادت ۔ اور اسی اصل پر غلام ماذون کا حدود و قصاص کا اقرار صحیح ہے ، اور اس چوری کا جس میں مال ہلاک ہو گیا ہو اور اس چوری کا جس میں مال موجود ہو، یہ اقرار مازون کی طرف سے صحیح ہے، اور غلام مجور کے اقرار میں اختلاف معروف ہے، اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا غلام کی خطاً جنایت کے بارے میں کہ غلام ہی اپنی جنایت کی جزا ہو جائے گا، اس لئے کہ غلام اس چیز کے ضمان کا اہل نہیں ہے جو مال نہ ہوں، مگر یہ کہ مولی فدیہ ادا کرنا چاہے، تو واجب لوٹ آئے گا اصل کی طرف امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک، یہاں تک کہ افلاس سے باطل نہ ہوگا، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ حوالہ کے درجہ میں ہے۔
And slavery does not affect the sanctity of blood, but only affects its value. Sanctity is through faith and abode (Dar al-Islam), and the slave is like the free in this. Therefore, a free person is killed in qisas for a slave, and slavery necessitates a deficiency in jihad such that it is not obligatory upon him, because his capacity for Hajj and jihad is not exempted by the master. For this reason, he is not entitled to the full share of the spoils. All forms of legal authority (wilayah) are cut off by slavery, because it is a legal incapacity. And the aman (safe conduct) of the ma'dhun is valid, because the aman by permission exits from the categories of wilayah, due to the fact that he becomes a partner in the spoils. So it becomes binding on him, then it extends to others, like his testimony regarding the crescent of Ramadan. On this basis, his confession (iqrar) regarding hudud, qisas, and theft where the goods are consumed or still extant is valid from the ma'dhun. Regarding the mahjur (interdicted slave), there is a well-known difference. On this basis, we say regarding the slave's jinaayah by mistake that he becomes the compensation for his crime, because the slave is not of the people who guarantee what is not property, unless the master chooses ranson, then it returns to the origin according to Abu Hanifa, so that it is not nullified by insolvency, and according to them (Sahibayn) it becomes in the meaning of hawala (transfer of debt). Translation: And slavery does not affect the sanctity of blood, only the value of the slave. Sanctity is attained through faith and Dar al-Islam, and the slave is like the free in this. For this reason, a free person is killed in qisas for a slave. Slavery creates a deficiency in jihad, such that it is not obligatory on the slave, because his capacity for Hajj and jihad is not exempted by the master. For this reason, the slave is not entitled to the full share of spoils. All forms of authority are cut off by slavery, because slavery is a legal incapacity. The aman of the ma'dhun is valid, because aman by permission exits from the categories of wilayah, because the slave becomes a partner in the spoils. Then the ruling of aman becomes binding on him, and then extends to others, like his testimony about the crescent of Ramadan. On this basis, the confession of the ma'dhun slave regarding hudud, qisas, and theft where the goods are consumed or still extant is valid. Regarding the confession of the mahjur (interdicted) slave, there is a well-known difference. And on this basis we said regarding the slave's accidental jinaayah that he becomes the compensation for his crime, because the slave is not fit to guarantee what is not property, unless the master wishes to pay ransom, then it returns to the origin according to Imam Abu Hanifa, such that it is not nullified by insolvency, and according to them (Sahibayn) it becomes in the category of hawala (transfer of debt).
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings derived from the principle that slavery (riqq) is a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi). It opens by stating that slavery does not affect the sanctity of blood (ismah), which is based on faith and dar al-Islam; thus, a free person is executed in qisas for killing a slave. The passage then lists effects: jihad is not obligatory on a slave because his capacity (istita'ah) is not exempted for the master (mawla) in Hajj and jihad; slaves do not receive full shares of spoils; all forms of guardianship (wilayah) are severed by slavery. An exception is the aman (safe conduct) of a ma'dhun (permitted) slave, which is valid because albeit by permission, the condition that he benefits in spoils makes it binding and extendable to others, akin to his testimony on the hilal of Ramadan. Similarly, the confession (iqrar) of a ma'dhun slave is valid in hudud, qisas, and theft (both consumed and extant property). For an interdicted slave (mahjur), there is a known dispute (presumably between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn). Finally, the passage addresses a slave's jinaayah bil khata' (accidental homicide): according to Abu Hanifa, the slave himself becomes the compensation (i.e., handed over) but the master may ransom him; if he ransoms, the obligation returns to the original (i.e., the ransom amount) and is not invalidated by insolvency; according to Sahibayn, it becomes like hawala (transfer of debt). Throughout, the reasoning is based on the slave's legal incapacity and limited liability.

Key Terms
رقیت (riqqiyyah): Slavery; a legal status that creates a legal impediment (ajz hukmi)
عصمت (‘ismah): Sanctity or inviolability of life; derived from faith and dar al-Islam
امان (amān): Safe conduct granted to a non-Muslim enemy; valid from a ma'dhun slave if master permits
جنایت خطاء (jināyah bil-khaṭā): Accidental homicide or bodily harm

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the aman (safe conduct) of a ma'dhun slave valid, unlike other forms of wilayat?
A) Because the slave is a free agent
B) Because aman by permission exits the categories of wilayat and the slave is a partner in spoils
C) Because the master is always liable
D) Because all slaves have full capacity

Key Takeaway
Slavery is a legal incapacity that severs wilayat, but permission can exempt specific acts like aman and iqrar from that incapacity, and accidental homicide liability follows the illah of the slave's inability to guarantee non-property, leading to a intra-madhhab dispute.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Legal Effects of Slavery (Riqq) on Capacity and Guardianship
Exposition of how slavery impacts 'ismah, jihad, hajj, wilayah, and other rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the effects of riqq on 'ismah, devotional obligations, and guardianship, and apply the Hanafi principle of legal incapacity to derive rulings for authorized and restricted slaves.

Core Idea
Riqq is a legal incapacity that leaves inviolability intact but restricts bodily benefit and cuts off guardianship, with exceptions for authorized slaves.

This passage from Al-Husami explores how the underlying cause of riqq as a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi) generates rulings across multiple fiqh chapters. We see why a slave's blood is as protected as a free person's, why he cannot perform hajj or jihad without permission, and why his guardianship is severed. The author also explains the special capacity of the authorized slave to grant aman, testify, and confess, and addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute on a slave's accidental injury.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of 'ismah
Understand that 'ismah has two aspects: sin-based (faith) and liability-based (abode). Slaves and free persons are equal in both, so riqq does not affect inviolability of blood. The only difference is in monetary value (diyah).
This explains why a free person is killed in retaliation for a slave.
2
Analyze riqq's effect on devotional obligations
Since a slave does not own his bodily benefits except as exempted by shariah (prayer, fasting), he lacks the ability for hajj and jihad without the master's permission. Consequently, he does not receive a full share of spoils.
Exception: general mobilization (nafir amm) allows jihad without permission.
3
Explain the severance of all guardianships
Riqq is a legal incapacity that prevents a slave from exercising any guardianship (wilayah) over himself or others. This is analogous to the incapacity of a minor or insane person.
The slave cannot even manage his own affairs, thus all guardianships are cut off.
4
Examine the exception for the authorized slave's aman
The authorized slave's grant of aman is valid because it is by the master's permission and falls outside the categories of guardianship. The slave becomes a partner in spoils, so the aman binds him and extends to others.
This is based on the principle that the authorized slave has limited capacity in certain matters.
5
Compare authorized vs. restricted slave regarding confessions
The authorized slave's confession of hadd, qisas, and theft (both consumed and extant) is valid. For the restricted slave, there is a known difference of opinion among Hanafis.
The difference stems from whether the restricted slave has any capacity to bear liability.
6
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on accidental injury
Regarding a slave's accidental injury (jinayah khata), the slave himself becomes the substitute for the injury because he is not capable of guaranteeing non-property claims. Abu Hanifa holds that if the master pays ransom, the obligation revives and is not voided by insolvency; the two companions say it becomes like hawala and can be voided.
The disagreement revolves around the nature of the obligation: is it a debt or a guarantee?

Source Text
