نَقْصَانًا فِي الْجِهَادِ حَتَّى لَا يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ لاَنَ اِسْتِطَاعَتَهُ فِي الْحَجَ وَالْجِهَادِ غَيْرَ مُسْتَثْنَاةٍ عَلَى الْمَوْلى وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَسْتَوْجِبْ السَّهْمَ الْكَامِلَ مِنَ الْغَنِيْمَةِ وَانْقَطَعَتْ الْوِلَايَاتُ كُلُّهَا بِالرّقَ لأَنَّهُ عَجْزٌ حُكْمِيُّ وَإِنَّمَا صَحَّ أَمَانَ الْمَأْذُوْنِ لآنَ الْآمَانَ بِالْإِذْنِ يَخْرُجُ عَنْ أَقْسَامِ الْوَلَايَةِ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنَّهُ صَارَ شَرِيكًا فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ فَلَزِمَهُ ثُمَّ تَعَدَّى إلى غَيْرِهِ مِثْلُ شَهَادَتِهِ بِهِلَالِ رَمَضَانَ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْاَصْلِ يَصِحُ اِقْرَارُهُ بِالْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَبِالسَرَقَةِ الْمُسْتَهْلَكَةِ وَبِالْقَائِمَةِ صَحَ مِنَ الْمَاذُوْنِ وَفِي الْمَحْجُوْرِ اِخْتِلَافٌ مَعْرُوفٌ وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا فِي جِنَايَةِ الْعَبْدِ خَطَاء أَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ جَزَاءً لِجِنَايَتِهِ لِاَنَّ الْعَبْدَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِ ضَمَانٍ مَا لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشَاءَ الْمَوْلَى الْفِدَاءَ فَيَصِيرُ عَائِدًا إِلَى الْأَصْلِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ حَتَّى لَا يَبْطُلُ بِالْإِفْلَاسِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَصِيْرُ بِمَعْنَى الْحَوَالَةِ .
ترجمہ: اور رقیت خون کی عصمت میں مؤثر نہیں ہے، البتہ غلام کی قیمت میں مؤثر ہے، اور عصمت ایمان اور دار الاسلام سے حاصل ہوتی ہے، اور غلام اس میں آزاد کے مانند ہے، اسی وجہ سے آزاد کو غلام کے بدلہ میں قصاصا قتل کیا جائے گا، اور رقیت جہاد میں نقصان پیدا کرے گی ، یہاں تک کہ غلام پر جہاد واجب نہ ہوگا، اس لئے کہ حج اور جہاد میں اس کی استطاعت کا مولی پر استثنا نہیں کیا گیا ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے غلام غنیمت کے کامل حصہ کا مستحق نہ ہوگا، اور رقیت کی وجہ سے تمام ولایات منقطع ہو جائیں گی، اس لئے کہ رقیت ایک عجز حکمی ہے، اور ماذون کا امان صحیح ہے، اس لئے کہ امان مولی کی اجازت کی وجہ سے اقسام ولایت سے خارج ہو جائے گا، اس وجہ سے کہ غلام غنیمت میں شریک ہو گیا، پس امان کا حکم غلام پر لازم ہوگا، پھر اس کے غیر کی طرف متعدی ہوگا، جیسے رمضان کے چاند کے بارے میں غلام کی شہادت ۔ اور اسی اصل پر غلام ماذون کا حدود و قصاص کا اقرار صحیح ہے ، اور اس چوری کا جس میں مال ہلاک ہو گیا ہو اور اس چوری کا جس میں مال موجود ہو، یہ اقرار مازون کی طرف سے صحیح ہے، اور غلام مجور کے اقرار میں اختلاف معروف ہے، اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا غلام کی خطاً جنایت کے بارے میں کہ غلام ہی اپنی جنایت کی جزا ہو جائے گا، اس لئے کہ غلام اس چیز کے ضمان کا اہل نہیں ہے جو مال نہ ہوں، مگر یہ کہ مولی فدیہ ادا کرنا چاہے، تو واجب لوٹ آئے گا اصل کی طرف امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک، یہاں تک کہ افلاس سے باطل نہ ہوگا، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ حوالہ کے درجہ میں ہے۔
تشریح:- رقیت خون کی عصمت میں موثر نہیں ہے، لہذا غلام کا خون بھی ایسا ہی معصوم ہے جیسے آزاد کا خون معصوم ہے، اس لئے کہ جس عصمت سے تعرض کرنے پر گناہ لازم ہوتا ہے، وہ عصمت ایمان کی وجہ سے پیدا ہوتی ہے، اور جس عصمت سے تعرض کرنے پر ضمان یعنی دیت لازم ہوتی ہے وہ دار الاسلام میں ہونے سے لازم ہوتی ہے، اگر کسی میں دونوں عصمتیں ہوں یعنی مومن بھی ہو اور دار الاسلام میں بھی ہو تو اس کے قتل سے دیت یا قصاص، اور کفارہ دونوں لازم ہوں گے، اور اگر مومن دار الحرب میں ہو تو اس کے قتل سے صرف کفارہ واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ ایک عصمت ہے جو موجب ضمان ہے۔ الغرض موجب گناہ عصمت ایمان سے حاصل ہوتی ہے اور موجب ضمان عصمت دار الاسلام سے، اور ایمان اور دار الاسلام کا باشندہ ہونے میں غلام آزاد کے مثل ہے، لہذا رقیت کی وجہ سے اس کی عصمت میں کوئی فرق نہ پڑے گا، البتہ رقیت کا اثر مقدار قیمت میں ظاہر ہو گا یعنی غلام کی قیمت آزاد سے تھوڑی کم ہوگی، جیسے پہلے گذرا کہ غلام مقتول کی قیمت اگر دس ہزار درہم یا اس سے زیادہ ہے، تو دس ہزار میں دس درہم کم دیت واجب ہوگی یعنی ۹۹۹۰ ، تا کہ آزاد سے اس کا درجہ کم رہے، اور اگر اس کی قیمت دس ہزار سے کم ہے تو قیمت واجب ہوگی۔
جب غلام عصمت میں آزاد کے مثل ہے تو غلام کو عمدا قتل کرنے کی صورت میں آزاد کو قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا، جیسے عورت کو قتل کرنے کے بدلہ میں مرد کو قتل کیا جاتا ہے، کیونکہ عصمت میں عورت بھی مرد کے مثل ہے۔ بہر حال رقیت عصمت میں مؤثر نہیں ہے، لیکن غلام اپنے بدنی منافع کا مالک نہیں ہے ، صرف ان عبادات میں شریعت نے غلام کو مالک بنایا ہے جن کا شریعت نے استثناء کیا ہے، جیسے نماز ، روزہ ،لہذا حج اور جہاد میں غلام منافع بدنیہ کا مالک نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس کا شریعت نے استثناء نہیں کیا ہے، لہذا غلام بغیر اجازت مولی نہ حج کر سکتا ہے اور نہ جہاد کر سکتا ہے ، ہاں اگر نفیر عام ہو جائے یعنی اچانک حملہ کی صورت میں امیر المومنین کی طرف سے عام جہاد کا حکم ہو جائے تو غلام کو مولی کی اجازت کی ضرورت نہ ہوگی۔ بہر حال جب رقیت اہلیت جہاد میں نقصان پیدا کرتی ہے تو غلام مالِ غنیمت میں کامل حصہ کا مستحق نہ ہوگا، چاہے مولی کی اجازت سے جہاد کرے یا بغیر اجازت کے، البتہ امام بطور عطیہ کے تھوڑا بہت دے سکتا ہے جس کو رضخ کہتے ہیں، جیسے خبیر میں رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے غلاموں کو عطیہ کے طور پر دیا تھا، یہاں تک ذمہ اور حلت کا بیان پورا ہوا ، امور ثلثہ میں تیسری چیز ولایت تھی ، اب اس کو بیان کر رہے ہیں۔
وانقطعت الولايات كلها : - غلام سے بوجہ رقیت کے ہر طرح کی ولایت منقطع ہے، کیونکہ رقیت ایک عجز حکمی ہے، یعنی شریعت کے حکم سے غلام تمام تصرفات سے عاجز ہے، لہذا غلام کو خود اپنے پر ولایت نہیں ہے تو
A deficiency in jihad such that it is not obligatory upon him because his ability in hajj and jihad is not excepted from the master, and therefore he does not deserve the full share of the spoils, and all guardianships are cut off by slavery because it is a legal incapacity. However, the security (aman) of the authorized slave is valid because security by permission exits from the categories of guardianship, since he becomes a partner in the spoils, so it binds him, then it extends to others, like his testimony about the crescent of Ramadan. On this principle, his confession of hadd punishments and retaliation and of theft where the property is consumed or existing is valid from the authorized slave. Regarding the restricted slave, there is a known difference. On this we said concerning the slave's accidental injury that he becomes the substitute for his injury because the slave is not qualified to guarantee what is not property, unless the master chooses ransom, then it returns to the original according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, such that it is not invalidated by insolvency, whereas according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it becomes like a transfer (hawala).
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage from Al-Husami explains the legal effects of slavery (riqq) across various areas. The author establishes first that riqq does not affect the inviolability of blood (ismah); a slave's blood is as protected as a free person's in terms of sin and liability, though the monetary value (diyah) is reduced. Then it addresses jihad and hajj: since a slave does not own his bodily benefits except as exempted by shariah (prayer, fasting), he cannot perform hajj or jihad without the master's permission, except in a general mobilization (nafir amm). Consequently, he does not receive a full share of spoils, only a token (radhkh). Next, all forms of guardianship (wilayah) are cut off due to slavery as a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi). However, the authorized slave's (ma'dhun) grant of aman is valid because it is by the master's permission and falls outside wilayah; it binds him and extends to others, like his testimony on the crescent. On the same principle, his confession of hadd and qisas is valid, as well as confession of theft (both consumed and extant property). For the restricted slave (mahjur), there is known disagreement. Finally, regarding a slave's accidental injury (jinayah khata): the slave himself becomes the substitute (jaza') for the injury because he is not capable of guaranteeing non-property claims; but if the master chooses to ransom him, the liability reverts to the original (i.e., the master's responsibility for the slave's value) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this does not become void by insolvency. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it becomes like a hawala (transfer of debt) which can be invalidated by insolvency. This passage demonstrates how the Hanafi school systematically derives rulings from the underlying cause (illah) of riqq as a legal incapacity, applying istihsan in some cases.

Key Terms
الرق (ar-riqq): Slavery; a legal status of ownership over a human being that creates a legal incapacity (عجز حكمي) affecting various rights and obligations.
العصمة (al-‘ismah): Inviolability; protection of blood and life from being taken unlawfully, which has two aspects: عصمة الإيمان (sin-based) and عصمة دار الإسلام (liability-based).
المأذون (al-ma’dhūn): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade; such a slave has limited capacity to conduct transactions and legal actions.
المحجور (al-maḥjūr): A slave who is restricted from financial transactions; a slave not given permission by his master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of riqq on a slave's inviolability ('ismah)?
A) Riqq completely removes 'ismah.
B) Riqq reduces 'ismah such that the slave's blood is less protected.
C) Riqq does not affect 'ismah; the slave's blood is as protected as a free person's.
D) Riqq only affects 'ismah based on abode, not faith.

Key Takeaway
Riqq, as a legal incapacity, does not affect inviolability but restricts bodily benefit, severs guardianship, and creates specific rules for authorized slaves, with intra-Hanafi variation on accidental injury.

Deathbed Illness and Legal Restrictions (Hajr)
Explains the usul rule of hajr during deathbed illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the effect of deathbed illness (marad al-mawt) on a person's legal transactions and state the Hanafi rule regarding hajr (restriction) on such transactions.

Core Idea
Deathbed illness triggers a partial restriction (hajr) on transactions to protect heirs and creditors, not a loss of legal capacity.

This passage explores the Hanafi usul principle that deathbed illness does not remove a person's foundational legal capacity (ahliyyat al-hukm) or capacity to express legal intent (ahliyyat al-'ibarah). However, because death is imminent, the rights of heirs and creditors become attached to the sick person's property. This attachment creates a legal restriction (hajr) on certain transactions, balancing the sick person's desire to dispose of property with the need to protect others' rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the unaffected capacities
The text states that illness does not affect ahliyyat al-hukm (capacity to be subject to rulings) nor ahliyyat al-'ibarah (capacity to express legally). Recognize that these remain intact during deathbed illness.
These are fundamental capacities that every accountable person possesses.
2
Recognize the reason for restriction
Illness is a cause of death; death triggers inheritance rights. Thus, the rights of heirs and creditors become attached to the sick person's property. This necessitates hajr when the illness is connected to death.
The restriction is for the protection of others, not a punishment or loss of capacity.
3
Distinguish transactions by rescindability
Transactions that admit rescission (e.g., sales) are valid immediately but can be annulled if they prejudice rights. Transactions that do not admit rescission (e.g., emancipation) are treated as suspended upon death (mu'allaq bi al-mawt) and are invalid if they harm heirs/creditors.
This distinction is key to understanding the Hanafi approach.
4
Apply the exception for one-third
By analogy, a sick person should not be able to make gifts or pay financial obligations, but the Law permits these from one-third of the estate out of consideration for the sick person.
The one-third rule overrides the general prohibition to allow some disposition.
5
Note the special rule for bequests to heirs
Bequests to heirs are void completely. According to Abu Hanifa, even a sale to an heir is invalid, because it would be a disguised bequest.
This prevents circumventing the rule that heirs cannot receive bequests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْمَرَضُ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يُنَا فِي أَهْلِيَةَ الْحُكْمِ وَلَا اَهْلِيَةَ الْعِبَارَةِ لَكِنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ سَبَبَ الْمَوْتِ وَالْمَوْتُ عِلَّةُ الْخِلَافَةِ كَانَ مِنْ أَسْبَابٍ تَعَلُّقِ حَقَّ الْوَارِثِ وَالْغَرِيم بِمَالِهِ فَيَثْبُتُ بِهِ الْحَجَرُ إِذَا اِتَّصَلَ بِالْمَوْتِ مُسْتَنِدًا لى اَوَلِهِ بِقَدَرٍ مَايَقَعُ بِه صِيَانَةُ الْحَقَّ فَقِيلَ كُلُّ تَصَرُّفٍ وَاقِع مِنْهُ يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَسْخَ فَإِنَّ الْقَوْلَ بِصِحَتِهِ وَاجِبْ فِي الْحَالِ ثُمَّ التَّدَارَكِ بِالنَّقْضِ إِذَا أُخْتِبْجَ إِلَيْهِ وَكُلَّ تَصَرُّفٍ وَاقِعِ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَسْخَ جُعِلَ كَالْمُعَلَق بِالْمَوْتِ كَالْاِعْتِاقِ إِذَا وَقَعَ عَلَى حَقَّ غَرِيْمٍ أَوْ وَارِثِ بِخِلَافِ اِعْتَاقِ الرَّاهِنِ حَيْثُ يَنْفُذُ لانَ حَقَّ الْمُرْتَهنِ فِي مِلْكِ الْيَدِدُونَ مِلْكِ الرَّقَبَةِ وَكَانَ الْقِيَاسُ أَنْ لَا يَمْلِكُ الْمَرِيضُ الصِلَةَ وَأَدَاءَ الْحُقُوق الْمَالِيَةِ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَالوَصِيَّةَ بِذَلِكَ إِلَّا انْ الشَّرْعَ جَوَزَذْلِكَ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ نَظْرَالَهُ وَلَمَّا تَوَلَّى الشَّرْعُ الْأَيْصَاءَ لِلْوَرَثَةِ وَأَبْطَلَ إِيْصَاءَ هُ لَهُمْ بَطَلَ ذَلِكَ صُورَةً وَمَعْنِّى وَحَقِيْقَةً وَشُبْهَةً حَتَّى لَمْ يَصِحَ بِيْعَهُ مَنَ الْوَارِثِ أَصْلًا عِنْدَ أَبِي
As for illness, it does not diminish [؟] in the capacity for rulings nor the capacity for expression, but since it is a cause of death and death is the cause of inheritance, it is among the causes of attachment of the right of the heir and creditor to his property. Thus restriction (hajr) is established when it is connected to death, based on its beginning to the extent that preserves the right. So it is said: every transaction occurring from him that admits of rescission, then the ruling of its validity is obligatory immediately, then rectification by annulment when [؟] to it. And every transaction that does not admit of rescission is made like suspended upon death, like emancipation if it occurs against the right of a creditor or heir, unlike the emancipation of the pledgor where it is effective because the right of the pledgee is over the possession, not the ownership. And the analogy is that the sick person should not have the power to gift or discharge financial obligations to Allah or bequest thereof, except that the Law permitted that from the one-third out of consideration for him. And when the Law undertook the bequest for the heirs and invalidated his bequest to them, that became void in form, meaning, reality and suspicion, so that his sale from the heir is not valid at all according to Abu [Hanifa].
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This Arabic passage from the sharh deals with the legal effect of deathbed illness (marad al-mawt) on a person's legal capacity. It begins by affirming that illness does not negate the fundamental capacity for legal rulings (ahliyyat al-hukm) or the capacity for expression (ahliyyat al-'ibarah). However, because illness is a cause of death, and death triggers inheritance rights, the rights of heirs and creditors become attached to the sick person's property. This triggers a restriction (hajr) on the sick person's transactions to protect those rights, provided the illness is connected to death. The passage then distinguishes between two types of transactions: those that can be rescinded (like sales) are considered valid immediately but can be annulled later if they prejudice rights; those that cannot be rescinded (like emancipation) are treated as suspended upon death. For example, if a sick person frees a slave, and this harms creditors or heirs, the emancipation is invalid from the start. Exception: a pledgor's emancipation is effective because the pledgee's right is only over possession (yad), not ownership (raqabah). The passage then notes that by analogy, a sick person should not be able to make gifts (hibah), pay financial obligations to Allah (like zakat), or make bequests, but the Law permits these from one-third of the estate out of consideration for the sick person. Finally, the passage states that since the Law has prescribed bequests for heirs and invalidated bequests to them (i.e., a person cannot bequeath to an heir), any such bequest is void completely, to the extent that even a sale to an heir from a sick person is not valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. This passage illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that marad al-mawt creates a partial restriction on the sick person's transactions, balancing the need to allow the sick person some disposition with the protection of heirs' and creditors' rights.

Key Terms
أهلية الحكم (ahliyyat al-hukm): The capacity to be subject to legal rulings (obligations, rights) – this remains intact during illness.
أهلية العبارة (ahliyyat al-'ibarah): Capacity to express oneself legally (e.g., contract, will) – not removed by illness.
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal restriction on a person's capacity to freely dispose of property, imposed to protect rights of others.
المعلق بالموت (al-mu'allaq bi al-mawt): A transaction that is suspended upon death, meaning it is treated as a bequest and is subject to the one-third rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a person on their deathbed frees a slave, and this harms the rights of a creditor, what is the ruling on that emancipation?
A) It is valid immediately because the sick person has full capacity.
B) It is treated as suspended upon death and invalid if it harms the creditor.
C) It is valid only if the creditor agrees.
D) It is valid because emancipation cannot be rescinded.

Key Takeaway
Deathbed illness creates a partial restriction on transactions to protect heirs and creditors, with rescindable transactions valid but voidable, and irrevocable ones suspended upon death.

Liability of a Slave for Accidental Homicide: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explaining the ruling on a slave's accidental killing and the master's option to ransom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on a slave's liability for accidental homicide and derive the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the effect of the master's ransom.

Core Idea
A slave's accidental killing yields his person as substitute; the master's ransom either revives diyah (Abu Hanifa) or transfers debt (Sahibayn).

This passage from a Hanafi usul text examines a dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the legal effect when a master ransoms his slave after the slave commits accidental homicide. The disagreement hinges on the nature of the original obligation: is it diyah (blood money) or the slave's person? The answer determines whether the master's insolvency returns liability to the slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Both sides agree that for a slave's accidental homicide, the slave's person (raqabah) is surrendered because the slave lacks ownership capacity. Understand this common starting point.
The slave is not financially liable; his person is the substitute.
2
Distinguish Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the original wajib is diyah; the person is a temporary substitute. When the master ransoms, the obligation reverts to diyah on the master. Even if the master becomes insolvent, the obligation remains on the master and the slave goes free.
The master's ransom is not a transfer but a revival of the original diyah.
3
Distinguish the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn view the ransom as a hawalah (transfer of debt). The original obligation is on the slave; the master's payment is a transfer. If the master fails to pay (e.g., insolvency), the obligation returns to the slave, and his person is surrendered again.
Hawalah rules: if the transferee fails, the original debtor remains liable.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in the scenario where the master ransoms but becomes insolvent, Abu Hanifa says the slave is free; the Sahibayn say the slave becomes liable again and his person is surrendered. Identify this real-world difference.
This is the core practical test of the dispute.
5
Identify the underlying usul principle
The dispute is rooted in the classification of the original obligation: Abu Hanifa prioritizes the diyah as the fixed liability, while the Sahibayn treat the person as the original substitute. This illustrates how different conceptions of 'wajib' affect legal consequences.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the slave's legal capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لوٹانا واجب ہوگا ، البتہ اس کے آزاد ہونے کے بعد اس پر مال کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ وعلى هذا قلنا فى جناية العبد - چونکہ رقیت مالکیت مال کے منافی ہے، اس بنیاد پر یہ کی ہے کہ اگر غلام نے خطا کوئی جنایت کی جیسے خطا کسی کوقتل کردیا تو چونکہ غلام کے پاس نہ مال ہے، نہ اس میں مالکیت کی اہلیت ہے، تو بجائے اس پر مال واجب کرنے کے اسی کی گردن کو جنایت کا عوض قرار دیا جائے گا، اور اس کو مقتول کے حوالہ کیا جائے گا ، ہاں اگر مولی اس کا فدیہ دینا منظور کرلے تو اب غلام جنایت کا عوض نہ ہوگا، بلکہ بقول امام ابوحنیفہ واجب اصلی کی طرف حکم لوٹ آئے گا، کیونکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک واجب اصلی فدیہ دینا ہے یعنی دیت، مگر چونکہ غلام قادر نہیں ہوتا ، اس لئے اس کے رقبہ کو عوض قرار دیا گیا، اب جب مولی فدیہ دینے پر راضی ہو گیا، تو حکم اصل کی طرف لوٹ آئے گا، حتی کہ اگر مولی مفلس بھی ہو گیا تو اس کے افلاس کی وجہ سے فدیہ اور دیت کا وجوب باطل نہ ہوگا ، اور حکم اس کے رقبہ کی طرف عود نہ کرے گا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک فدیہ دینا حوالہ کے درجہ میں ہے یعنی اصل وجوب غلام پر ہے، اس نے مولی کے حوالہ کر دیا، اور حوالہ میں یہ بات ہے کہ اگر محتال علیہ اداء حق سے عاجز ہو جائے تو محیل اور اصیل بری نہیں ہوتا ہے، لہذا مولی اگر مفلس ہو گیا، تو دیت غلام کے ذمہ میں ہوگی اور اس کے لئے غلام کا رقبہ حوالہ کیا جائے گا۔
It will be wajib to return; however, after he is freed, guarantee of wealth is wajib upon him. And upon this we said regarding the slave's janiyah - because servitude is contrary to ownership of wealth, on this basis it is that if a slave committed a wrong by mistake, such as mistakenly killing someone, then since the slave has neither wealth nor capacity for ownership, instead of making wealth wajib upon him, his neck itself will be made the substitute for the crime, and he will be handed over to the slain. Yes, if the master agrees to pay ransom for him, then the slave will not be the substitute for the crime; rather, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the ruling returns to the original obligation because near Imam Abu Hanifa the original obligation is to pay ransom, i.e., blood money; but since the slave is not capable, his person (raqabah) is made the substitute. Now when the master consented to pay ransom, the ruling returns to the original, even if the master becomes insolvent, due to his insolvency the obligation of ransom and blood money does not become void, and the ruling will not return to his person. And according to the Sahibayn, paying ransom is in the category of hawalah (transfer), meaning the original obligation is upon the slave; he transferred it to the master. And in hawalah, the matter is that if the transferee becomes unable to pay the right, the transferor and original debtor are not absolved. Hence, if the master becomes insolvent, the blood money will be in the slave's liability and for that his person (raqabah) will be handed over.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the liability of a slave who commits accidental homicide. The author explains the Hanafi position: because a slave lacks ownership (milk) and capacity for ownership, he cannot be held financially liable. Therefore, the default ruling is that the slave's person (raqabah) is surrendered to the victim's heirs as compensation. However, if the master (mawla) chooses to pay the ransom (fidya), i.e., the blood money (diya), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the original obligation (diyah) revives, and the slave is freed from liability. Even if the master becomes insolvent, the obligation remains on the master and does not revert to the slave. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ: they view the master's ransom as a hawalah (transfer of debt). In hawalah, if the transferee (master) fails to pay, the obligation returns to the transferor (slave). Thus, if the master becomes insolvent, the slave's liability revives and his person is surrendered. This ikhtilaf is based on whether the original wajib is the diyah (Abu Hanifa) or the slave's person (Sahibayn). The passage follows the author's order, first stating the ruling, then providing the reasoning of both sides.

Key Terms
جناية (janiyah): Crime or tort, specifically homicide or injury inflicted by a slave.
رقبہ (raqabah): The person or physical entity of the slave, used as a substitute for financial liability.
فدیہ (fidya): Ransom paid by the master to redeem the slave from being surrendered.
حوالہ (hawalah): Transfer of debt from one party to another; the master's ransom is analogized to a hawalah by the Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a master ransoms his slave for accidental homicide and then becomes insolvent, what is the status of the slave's liability?
A) The slave's liability revives and his person is surrendered.
B) The master remains liable for the diyah and the slave is free.
C) The slave is freed but must pay the diyah later.
D) The liability is voided entirely.

Key Takeaway
The dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of the master's ransom illustrates how the classification of the original obligation (diyah vs. raqabah) leads to different consequences when the master becomes insolvent.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

12 min
Hajr in Marad al-Mawt: Usul Analysis of Interdiction and Manumission
Commentary on hajr, i'taq, and wasiyya during death-illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of distinguishing between rescindable and non-rescindable transactions to determine the validity of a sick person's acts, and identify the qiyas and istihsan involved.

Core Idea
Transactions of a sick person are effective if rescindable; otherwise, they are suspended like tadbir.

This passage from a commentary on Usul al-Karkhi explains the rationale behind imposing legal interdiction (hajr) on a person during death-illness (marad al-mawt). The author derives a general rule (dabt) that distinguishes between transactions that can be rescinded and those that cannot, then applies it to manumission and compares it to the case of a mortgaged slave. The underlying legal reasoning involves qiyas and istihsan, which we will unpack.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of hajr and its scope
Understand why hajr is imposed: to protect creditors and heirs. The hajr is retroactive only if the patient dies from that illness. Determine the amount: full debt plus two-thirds of the remainder for heirs.
The hajr is designed to balance the rights of the sick person and others.
2
Distinguish rescindable from non-rescindable transactions
The passage gives a general rule: if the transaction can be rescinded (like a gift or undervalue sale), it is immediately effective, because if the patient dies, the transaction can be reversed to pay debts and heirs. If not rescindable (like manumission), it is suspended like a mudabbar.
This distinction is key to understanding the Hanafi position.
3
Apply the rule to manumission and compare to tadbir
Manumission in marad al-mawt, if it affects others' rights, is treated like tadbir: the slave becomes free only after death and works to pay his value. The qiyas (analogy) is based on the common 'illa: both are non-rescindable and affect creditors/heirs.
The text presents this as a clear qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Recognize the exception for charitable dispositions up to one-third
The text notes that qiyas would prevent all charitable acts, but the Shari'ah granted a concession (istihsan) allowing the sick person to dispose of up to one-third for charity. This is an exception to the hajr rule.
This istihsan is based on the principle of kindness (shafaqa).
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on sūra wasiyya
The passage ends with an example: a sale to an heir at fair price. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it invalid as a disguised will (sura wasiyya), while the two disciples (Sahibayn) allow it if the price is similar. This shows the practical impact of the rule.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the validity of such sales differs according to which view is followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک سوال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ جب مریض میں اہلیت باقی ہے تو مرض الموت میں بعض صورتوں میں اس پر حجر کیوں عائد ہوتا ہے، یعنی اس کے تصرف پر روک کیوں لگ جاتی ہے؟
اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ مرض موت کا سبب ہے، اور موت علت ہے، خلافت کی یعنی آدمی کے مرنے سے اس کی اہلیت ختم ہو جاتی ہے، اب اس کے مال میں اس کے ورثار خلیفہ ہوں گے، اور چونکہ اس پر قرض بھی ہے تو اس کے مال کے ساتھ قرض خواہ کا حق بھی متعلق ہے، لہذا اس کے مال میں قرض خواہ بھی خلیفہ ہوگا ، اب جب اس کے مال کے ساتھ ورثاء اور قرض خواہ کا حق متعلق ہو گا ، تو ان دونوں کے حق کی حفاظت کی خاطر مریض پر حجر عائد کیا کہ اب مریض کا تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگا ، تا کہ ان دونوں کا حق ضائع نہ ہو، لیکن یہ حجر اتنی مقدار میں ہوگا جس سے حق کی حفاظت ہو جائے ، پس قرض خواہ کے قرض کی جتنی مقدار ہے اس میں مریض کا تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگا ، اور قرض کے بعد بقیہ مال کے دو تہائی میں ورثاء کا حق ہے، اس میں بھی مریض کا تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگا، یہ حجر مرض الموت میں ہوتا ہے، اور مرض الموت ہونا اس وقت معلوم ہو گا جب وہ اسی مرض میں مرجائے ، ورنہ مرض الموت نہ ہوگا، جب یہ مر گیا تو حجر ابتدائے مرض کی طرف منسوب ہوگا یعنی موت کے وقت یہ فیصلہ دیا جائے گا کہ یہ جب سے بیمار ہوا ہے اس وقت سے اس کا تصرف نافذ نہیں ہے۔
بہر حال اس کا مرض الموت ہونا موت سے اتصال پر موقوف ہے اور موت میں احتمال ہے، ہوسکتا ہے اس بیماری میں مرے یا نہ مرے تو ابھی جو یہ تصرف کر رہا ہے اس کا کیا ؟ تو مصنف ضابطہ بتا رہے ہیں کہ اس تصرف میں ہم دیکھیں گے کہ فسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے یا نہیں ، اگر فسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے جیسے ہبہ کرنا ، بہت کم قیمت پر سامان بیچنا وغیرہ تو نافذ ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ اس تصرف میں کسی کا ضر ر نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ اگر یہ مر بھی گیا اور اس نے قرضہ چھوڑا ہے تو اس تصرف کو فسخ کر کے قرض ادا کیا جائے گا اور وارث کو دیا جائے گا، اور اگر وہ تصرف فتح کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے، جیسے غلام کو آزاد کرنا جب کہ یہ وارث یا غیریم کے حق پر واقع ہو ، تو اس تصرف کو موت پر معلق تصرف کی طرح قرار دیا جائے گا، جیسے آقا نے غلام سے کہا کہ میرے مرنے کے بعد تو آزاد ہے، جس کو مد بر بنانا کہتے ہیں، بہر حال مریض کا اعتاق جب کہ وہ وارث یا قرض خواہ کے حق پر واقع ہو ، یعنی مریض نے غلام آزاد کیا اور غلام کی قیمت ثلث مال سے زائد ہے، یا مریض پر قرضہ ہے جو اس کے پورے مال کو گھیرے ہوئے ہے، تو مریض کا یہ اعتناق وارث اور قرض خواہ کے حق پر واقع ہورہا ہے، لہذا اس کا حکم مد بر جیسا ہوگا ، جیسے مدبر آقا کی موت پر آزاد ہوتا ہے اور مد برآزاد ہونے کے بعد اپنی قیمت کے بقدر ورثاء اور قرض خواہوں کے حق کی ادائیگی کے لئے کمائی کرتا ہے، اسی طرح مرض الموت میں آزاد کردہ غلام بھی آقا کے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہوگا، ورثاء اور قرض خواہوں کے حق کی ادائیگی کے لئے اپنی قیمت کے بقدر کمائی کر کے دیگا۔
اور اگر اعتاق وارث اور قرضخواہ کے حق پر واقع نہ ہو یعنی آقا کے پاس غلام کے علاوہ مال ہے جس سے قرضہ ادا کرے یا اس غلام کی قیمت تہائی مال سے کم ہے تو عشق فوراً نافذ ہو جائے گا، موت پر متعلق نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف اعتاق الراهن : - ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے، جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ را ہن اگر غلام مرہون کو آزاد کرے تو عتق نافذ ہو جاتا ہے حالانکہ اس کے ساتھ مرتہن کا حق متعلق ہے، جب کہ اوپر ضابطہ یہ بتایا کہ غلام کے ساتھ وارث یا قرضخواہ کا حق متعلق ہو تو عتق فی الحال نافذ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔
اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مرتہن کا حق صرف قبضہ میں ہے، غلام کے رقبہ اور مالیت کے ساتھ اس کا حق متعلق نہیں ہے، بلکہ اس کے ساتھ راہن کا حق متعلق ہے، اور عشق ملک رقبہ سے ہوتا ہے، ملک ید یعنی قبضہ سے نہیں ہوتا ہے وہ قبضہ نہ بھی ہو تو بھی ملک رقبہ کی وجہ سے عتق نافذ ہو جائے گا، اسی لیے آقا مفرور غلام کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے، حالانکہ اس پر آقا کا قبضہ نہیں ہے ، مگر چونکہ ملک رقبہ ہے اس لیے عشق نافذ ہو جائے گا، برخلاف غریم اور وارث کے ان کا حق ملک رقبہ سے ہوتا ہے اس لیے مریض پر حجر لگ جاتا ہے، لہذا اعتاق راہن کو اعتناق مریض پر قیاس نہیں کر سکتے۔
مصنف یا اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ مریض کو ثلث مال میں بھی صلات یعنی احسان و تبرع کا اختیار نہ ہو جیسے ہبہ کرنا ، وغیرہ اسی طرح اللہ تعالیٰ کے مالی حقوق مثل زکوۃ ، صدقہ، کفارہ وغیرہ کا اختیار نہ ہومگر شریعت نے بطور شفقت کے ثلث مال میں اختیار دیدیا۔
ولما تولى الشرع :- سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے کہ جب ثلث مال میں شریعت نے اختیار دیا ہے، تو مریض ثلث مال میں اپنے وارث کے لئے وصیت کر سکتا ہے، کیونکہ ثلث اس کا اپنا حق ہے، حالانکہ وصیت وارث کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ وارث کے لئے جب اللہ تعالیٰ نے خود وصیت کردی ، سب کے حقوق متعین کردئے تو اس مریض کی وارث کے لئے وصیت باطل قرار دی جائے گی، وصیت کی چار صورتیں ہیں (۱) صورةُ (۲) معنی (۳) حقیقہ (۴) اور شبہہ ، وصیت کی چاروں صورتیں باطل ہیں ،سب کی مثالیں دیکھیں۔ صورۃ وصیت کی مثال: یہ ہے کہ مریض اپنے وارث کو کوئی معین چیز من مثل کے عوض یا ثمن غیر مثل کے عوض نیچے تو اگر چہ اس کی قیمت لے لی ہے مگر صورۃ وصیت ہے کہ وہ مخصوص چیز وارث کو دیدی تقسیم میراث میں وہ معین چیز اس وارث کے حصہ میں آ بھی سکتی تھی اور نہیں بھی آسکتی تھی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ بیج جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ صورۃ وصیت ہے، صاحبین کے نزدیک ثمن مثل سے یہ بیج جائز ہے کیونکہ اس سے ورثاء کا حق باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔
A question arises: when the sick person still has capacity, why is he placed under interdiction (hajr) in some cases during death-illness, i.e., why is his transaction blocked? The answer is given: death-illness is a cause (sabab), and death is the effective cause ('illa) of succession, i.e., upon a person's death his capacity ends. Now his heirs will be successors to his property, and since he also has debt, the creditor's right is also attached to his property. Therefore the creditor will also be a successor to his property. When the rights of heirs and creditors become attached to his property, then to protect the rights of both, hajr is imposed on the sick person so that his transaction will not be effective, lest the rights of both be lost. But this hajr will be to the extent that protects the right. So to the amount of the creditor's debt, the patient's transaction will not be effective, and in the remaining two-thirds of the property after debt, the heirs have a right; in that too the patient's transaction will not be effective. This hajr occurs in death-illness, and death-illness will be known when he dies from that illness, otherwise it is not death-illness. When he dies, the hajr will be attributed to the beginning of the illness, meaning at the time of death it will be decided that his transaction has been void since he became ill. In any case, his death-illness is dependent on connection with death, and death is uncertain; maybe he will die from this illness or not. So what about the transaction he is doing now? The author is giving a rule: we will see whether this transaction can be rescinded or not. If it can be rescinded, like giving a gift, selling goods at a very low price, etc., it will be effective, because there is no harm in this transaction, since if he dies and leaves debt, that transaction can be rescinded and the debt paid and given to the heirs. And if the transaction cannot be rescinded, like freeing a slave when it affects the right of an heir or creditor, then that transaction will be treated like a transaction suspended on death, e.g., the master tells the slave, 'You are free after my death,' which is called tadbir. In any case, the sick person's manumission, when it affects the right of an heir or creditor, i.e., the sick person freed a slave and the slave's value exceeds one-third of the estate, or the sick person has debt that covers all his property, then this manumission is affecting the right of heirs and creditors, so its ruling is like that of a mudabbar. Just as a mudabbar becomes free upon the master's death and after being free he works to pay off the amount of his value to the right of heirs and creditors, similarly a slave freed during death-illness will become free after the master's death and will work to pay off his value for the right of heirs and creditors. And if the manumission does not affect the right of heirs and creditors, i.e., the master has property other than the slave to pay the debt, or the slave's value is less than one-third of the estate, then the manumission is immediately effective, not suspended on death. Contrary to freeing a mortgaged slave: this is an answer to an objection, the summary of which is that if a mortgagor frees a mortgaged slave, the manumission is effective even though the mortgagee's right is attached to it, whereas the rule above stated that if the right of an heir or creditor is attached to the slave, manumission is not immediately effective. The answer is that the mortgagee's right is only in custody (qabd), not in the slave's corpus (raqaba) and value; rather, the mortgagor's right is attached, and manumission occurs from ownership of the corpus, not from ownership of possession. So even if there is no possession, manumission is effective due to ownership of the corpus. For this reason, a master can free an absconding slave even though he has no possession over him, but since he owns the corpus, manumission is effective. Contrary to a creditor and an heir: their right is from ownership of the corpus, so hajr is imposed on the sick person. Therefore, freeing a mortgaged slave cannot be analogized to freeing by a sick person. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, says: analogy would require that the sick person not have the option in one-third of his property for charitable acts (ihsan and tabarru') like giving gifts, and similarly for the financial rights of Allah like zakat, sadaqah, kaffarah, etc. But the Shari'ah, out of kindness, gave the option in one-third of the property. 'And when the Shari'ah undertook': This is the answer to an implied question: since the Shari'ah gave the option in one-third, the sick person can make a will (wasiyya) for his heir from the one-third, because one-third is his own right, even though a will for an heir is not permissible. The answer is that when Allah Himself has made a will for the heir and determined all rights, the sick person's will for the heir is invalid. There are four types of wasiyya: (1) sura (form), (2) ma'na (meaning), (3) haqiqa (reality), (4) shubha (semblance). All four types of wasiyya are invalid. See examples: Example of sura wasiyya: The sick person gives a specific item to his heir in exchange for a similar price or a price that is not similar, even though he took its price, but it is sura wasiyya because that specific item could have and could not have come into that heir's share in the division of inheritance. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this sale is not valid because it is sura wasiyya; according to the two disciples (Sahibayn), if the price is similar, the sale is valid because it does not invalidate the right of the heirs.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings concerning the juristic incapacity (hajr) imposed on a person during death-illness (marad al-mawt) and the specific rules for transactions and manumission. The text explains that hajr is imposed to protect the rights of creditors and heirs, as their rights become attached to the patient's property upon death. The hajr is retroactive to the onset of the illness only if the patient actually dies from that illness. The ruling distinguishes between transactions that can be rescinded (like gifts or sales at undervalue) and those that cannot (like freeing a slave). For non-rescindable acts, the transaction is treated like a tadbir (suspension on death), requiring the freed slave to work after the master's death to pay off his value for the benefit of creditors and heirs, unless the slave's value is within the one-third portion or there is other property to cover debts. The commentary then addresses an objection about freeing a mortgaged slave, clarifying that the mortgagee's right is only in possession (yad), not in the corpus (raqaba), so manumission is valid immediately, unlike the rights of heirs and creditors which are attached to the corpus. The text further explains that the Shari'ah has given the sick person the right to dispose of up to one-third of his estate in charity as a concession, but a will for an heir is invalid because Allah has already prescribed the shares of inheritance. The author mentions four types of invalid wills (sura, ma'na, haqiqa, shubha) and gives an example of sura wasiyya where a sale to an heir at fair value is considered a disguised will; Imam Abu Hanifa invalidates it while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it if the price is fair.

Key Terms
حجر (hajr): Legal interdiction preventing the sick person from effective transactions beyond the one-third portion.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): An illness that most often leads to death, determined by the outcome (death from that illness).
اعتناق (i'taq / i'tiq): Manumission of a slave; in this context, the ruling depends on whether it affects heirs/creditors.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death.
وصية (wasiyya): A will or bequest; for an heir, it is invalid because Allah has already assigned shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on manumission by a sick person during death-illness if the slave's value is less than one-third of the estate and there is no debt?
A) The manumission is invalid because all transactions of a sick person are void.
B) The manumission is effective immediately because it does not affect rights of creditors or heirs.
C) The manumission is suspended until death, similar to a mudabbar.
D) The manumission is valid only if the heirs consent.

Key Takeaway
A sick person's transactions are not universally invalid; the key is whether the transaction is rescindable and whether it affects the rights of creditors and heirs, with non-rescindable acts being suspended like tadbir.

Why Menstruation Drops Salah but Not Sawm: A Usul al-Fiqh Analysis
Explaining why hayd/nifas drop salah but not sawm due to hardship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle that hardship in making up multiplied prayers leads to dropping the obligation of salah, but not sawm.

Core Idea
Hardship in qada drops the asl; no hardship in sawm qada preserves it.

The passage explains why menstruation and postpartum bleeding prevent the performance of salah and sawm, but only the obligation of salah is completely dropped. The key reasoning revolves around the condition of purity and the concept of hardship (haraj) in making up missed acts. Understanding this distinction reveals how the Hanafi school applies the principle that obligations are lifted when their fulfillment causes undue difficulty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition that blocks performance
Purity (tahara) is a condition for the validity of both salah and sawm. During hayd/nifas, this condition is absent, so performance (ada') is not possible.
The condition does not affect the original obligation (asl) itself.
2
Recognize that only performance is missed
The asl (original obligation) remains in principle, but ada' is impossible. The ruling then considers whether qada (making up) is required.
Qada is the default when ada’ is missed without excuse.
3
Analyze the hardship in qada for salah vs sawm
For salah, missing multiple days means making up many prayers (e.g., 5 per day), causing multiplication. For sawm, only one day is missed per month, so no multiplication. The hardship (haraj) for salah is significant.
The Hanafi principle of al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir applies.
4
Apply the principle of hardship to drop the asl
Because qada of salah would cause undue hardship, the asl of salah is dropped entirely to avoid that hardship. For sawm, no such hardship exists, so the asl remains.
This is a specific application of the maxim that hardship brings ease.
5
Conclude the ruling
The final ruling: a menstruating woman need not make up missed salahs, but she must make up missed fasts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْحَيْضُ وَالنَّفَاسُ فَإِنَّهُمَا لَا يَعْدَمَانِ أَهْلِيَةً بِوَجْهِ مَالْكِنَّ الطَّهَارَةَ عَنْهُمَا شَرْ لِجَوَاز أَدَاءِ الصَّوْمِ وَالصَّلوةِ فَيَفُوتُ الْآدَاءُ بِهِمَا وَفِي قَضَاءِ الصَّلوةِ حَرَجٌ لِتَضَاعْفِهَا فَسَقَطَ بِهِمَا أَصْلُ الصَّلوةِ وَلَا حَرَجَ فَى قَضَاءِ الصَّوْمِ فَلَمْ يَسْقُطُ اَصْلُهُ وَاَمَّا الْمَوْتُ فَإِنَّهُ عَجْزٌ خَالِصْ يَسْقُطُ بِهِ مَاهُوَ مِنْ بَابِ التَّكْلِيفِ لِفَوَاتِ غَرَضِهِ وَهُوَ الْاَدَاء عَنْ اِخْتِيَارِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا إِنَّهُ يَبْطُلُ عَنْهُ الزَّكُوةُ وَسَائِرُ وُجُوهِ الْقُرَبِ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْقَى عَلَيْهِ الْمَاثِمَ وَمَا شُرِعَ عَلَيْهِ لِحَاجَةِ غَيْرِهِ اِنْ كَانَ حَقًّا مُتَعَلَّقًا بِالْعَيْنِ يَبْقَى بِبَقَاءِهِ لِاَنَّ فِعْلَهُ فِيْهِ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ دَيْنًا لَمْ يَبْقَ بِمُجَرَّدِ الدِّمَةِ حَتَّى يَنْضَمَ إِلَيْهِ مَالٌ اَوْ مَا يُؤكَدَ بِهِ الدِّمَمُ وَهُوَ ذِمَةُ الْكَفِيْلِ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ الله اِنَّ الْكَفَالَةَ بِالدَّيْنِ عَنِ الْمَيِّتِ لَا تَصِحُ إِذَا لَمْ يُخَلِّفُ مَالًا أَوْ كَفِيْلًا كَانَ الدَّيْنَ عَنْهُ سَاقِطْ بِخِلَافِ الْعَبْدِ الْمَحْجُورِ يَقِرُّ بِالدَّيْنِ فَتَكْفُل عَنْهُ رَجُلٌ تَصِحُ لِاَنَّ ذِمَتَهُ فِي حَقِّهِ كَامِلَةٌ وَإِنَّمَا ضُمَتْ إِلَيْهِ الْمَالِيَهُ فِي حَقَّ الْمَوْلَى
As for menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas): they do not nullify legal capacity (ahliyyah) in any way, but purification from them is a condition for the permissibility of performing fasting and prayer. So performance (ada') is missed due to them. And in making up (qada) for prayer there is hardship because it would multiply, so the origin (asl) of prayer is dropped due to them. And there is no hardship in making up for fasting, so its origin is not dropped. As for death: it is pure incapacity, so whatever is in the category of obligation (taklif) is dropped because its purpose is lost, and that is performance with choice. For this reason we say that zakat and all other acts of worship are nullified for the deceased. However, what remains upon him is the liability for monetary obligations (al-mathim) and what was legislated for the need of others. If it is a right attached to a specific asset (haqq muta'alliq bi al-'ayn), it remains with the survival of that asset, because his action in it is not intended. And if it is a debt (dayn), it does not remain by mere liability (dhimma) until property is added to it or something that strengthens the liability, which is the guarantee of a surety (kafil). For this reason, Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said that surety (kafala) for the debt of a deceased person is not valid if he did not leave property, and if there is no surety, the debt is dropped from him. In contrast, for a restricted slave (al-'abd al-mahjur) who acknowledges a debt, if a man becomes surety for him, it is valid because his liability (dhimma) is complete regarding his own rights; only financial capacity is restricted regarding the master's rights.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the effects of menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and death on religious obligations. The text explains that these conditions do not negate legal capacity itself, but they affect performance. For hayd and nifas: purification is a condition for both salah and sawm. Since salah must be performed in purity and its qada would be multiplied (each missed salah would need to be made up), the obligation of salah is dropped altogether to avoid hardship. For fasting, qada is not multiplied because only one day is missed each month, so the obligation is not dropped; it must be made up. For death: it is complete incapacity, so all acts of worship that require voluntary performance are dropped because the purpose (ada' 'an ikhtiyar) is impossible. However, financial obligations like zakat that were due are not dropped; they become a debt on the estate. Also, obligations that are rights of others, like a specific item held as trust or collateral, remain as charges on the estate. A debt does not remain merely on the dhimma after death unless there is property or a surety. Therefore, Abu Hanifa rules that kafala (suretyship) for a deceased person's debt is invalid if he left no property, because the dhimma alone cannot sustain the debt. But for a slave who is restricted (mahjur) but has a complete dhimma regarding his own obligations, surety is valid because his dhimma is full; only his financial capacity is limited vis-à-vis his master.

Key Terms
أصل الصلاة (asl al-salah): The original obligation of salah itself, as opposed to the actual performance or qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the obligation of salah dropped but not sawm for a menstruating woman according to the Hanafi view?
A) Because salah requires purity on every occurrence while sawm does not.
B) Because making up salah would multiply due to frequency, causing hardship.
C) Because sawm is a physical worship while salah is spiritual.
D) Because menstruation only prevents salah, not sawm.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school drops the obligation of salah during hayd/nifas due to hardship in making up multiplied prayers, but preserves the obligation of fasting because making up a few days does not cause similar hardship.

Why Death Ends Performative Obligations but Not Financial Liabilities: A Usul al-Fiqh Analysis
Explaining why death drops performative obligations but not financial liabilities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle that death, as pure incapacity, drops all performative obligations but leaves financial liabilities intact.

Core Idea
Pure incapacity removes performance stakes, but rights of creditors and specific assets survive.

The passage moves from the effects of temporary impediments (hayd/nifas) to the permanent cessation of death. It explains that death is 'pure incapacity' (ajz khalis), so any obligation that requires voluntary performance is dropped. However, financial obligations that do not require the deceased's personal action, such as debts and rights attached to specific assets, remain enforceable against the estate. This distinction is crucial for understanding inheritance and surety laws.

Guided Path
1
Define death as pure incapacity (ajz khalis)
Death is a complete and permanent inability to act. Therefore, any obligation that requires voluntary performance cannot be fulfilled.
This is different from temporary incapacities like hayd.
2
Identify the obligations that are dropped
All acts of worship that fall under taklif (duty to perform) are dropped, including salah, sawm, and the act of paying zakat. Their purpose (ada' 'an ikhtiyar) is unattainable.
These are obligations of personal performance.
3
Identify obligations that survive death
Rights attached to specific assets (haqq muta'alliq bi al-'ayn) remain because they do not require the deceased's action. Also, monetary obligations (al-mathim) like unpaid zakat or debts survive as charges on the estate.
These are rights of others, not personal worship.
4
Understand the condition for debt survival
A debt does not automatically remain on the dhimma after death. It continues only if there is property from which it can be paid or a surety (kafil) who guarantees it. Without either, the debt is dropped.
This is a specific Hanafi rule to prevent indefinite liability.
5
Apply to the ruling on kafala (suretyship)
Abu Hanifa rules that kafala for a deceased's debt is invalid if he left no property, because the debt itself is dropped. In contrast, for a restricted slave, kafala is valid because his dhimma is complete regarding his own obligations.
This shows the importance of dhimma completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Applying the Principle of Haraj: Menstruation and Makeup Obligations
Explaining why prayers are not made up but fasts are, using haraj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of haraj (hardship) to derive that a menstruating woman must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers.

Core Idea
Hardship (haraj) determines if an obligation is dropped or deferred: prayers multiply, so dropped; fasts are few, so deferred.

This passage from Al-Husami illustrates how the Hanafi school uses the principle of haraj to reach a ruling that balances legal capacity with practical ease. The author shows that while menstruation and postpartum bleeding prevent performance of both prayer and fasting, the obligation to make them up differs. Understanding this reasoning is crucial for deriving similar rulings in other cases where hardship is a factor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impediments and their effect on legal capacity
The passage states that hayd and nifas do not destroy legal capacity (ahliyyah). The woman remains a legal subject, so obligations can still apply.
If capacity were removed, she would not be obligated at all.
2
Identify what these impediments affect
They affect the condition (shart) of purification (tahara) for the validity of prayer and fasting. Without purification, the acts cannot be performed.
A condition is external to the act itself; its absence prevents performance but does not invalidate the underlying obligation.
3
Determine the consequence for performance
Since the condition is absent during the state, performance (ada') is missed. The question is whether missed acts must be made up (qada').
4
Analyze the hardship factor for each act
The author reasons that making up prayers would involve hardship (haraj) because they are many (multiple daily prayers). In contrast, fasting is only a few days per month, so no such hardship arises.
The concept of multiplicity (tada'uf) is key – prayers accumulate quickly, fasts do not.
5
Derive the ruling based on the presence or absence of hardship
Since hardship exists for prayer, the original obligation (asl al-wujub) is dropped entirely. For fasting, no hardship means the obligation remains but performance is postponed until after purification.
This illustrates the usul principle: 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْحَيْضُ وَالنَّفَاسُ فَإِنَّهُمَا لَا يَعْدَمَانِ أَهْلِيَةً بِوَجْهِ مَالْكِنَّ الطَّهَارَةَ عَنْهُمَا شَرْ لِجَوَاز أَدَاءِ الصَّوْمِ وَالصَّلوةِ فَيَفُوتُ الْآدَاءُ بِهِمَا وَفِي قَضَاءِ الصَّلوةِ حَرَجٌ لِتَضَاعْفِهَا فَسَقَطَ بِهِمَا أَصْلُ الصَّلوةِ وَلَا حَرَجَ فَى قَضَاءِ الصَّوْمِ فَلَمْ يَسْقُطُ اَصْلُهُ

ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال حیض اور نفاس پس یہ دونوں کسی بھی طرح اہلیت کو معدوم نہیں کرتے ہیں لیکن ان دونوں سے طہارت شرط ہے روزہ اور نماز کی ادا کے جواز کے لیے، پس ان دونوں کی وجہ سے ادا فوت ہو جائے گی ، اور نماز کی قضا میں حرج ہے ، نماز کے تضاعف (بڑھ جانے ) کی وجہ سے ، تو ان دونوں کی وجہ سے نماز کا اصل وجوب ساقط ہو جائے گا ، اور روزہ کی قضا میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے تو روزہ کا اصل وجوب ساقط نہ ہو گا۔

تشریح:- نواں عارض حیض اور دسواں عارض نفاس ہے، حیض و نفاس کسی بھی طرح اہلیت کو تو ختم نہیں کرتے لیکن نماز اور روزہ کی ادائیگی کے لئے حیض و نفاس سے طہارت شرط ہے، لہذا حیض و نفاس کے ساتھ نماز اور روزہ کی ادا ئیگی نہیں ہوسکتی ، پس حیض و نفاس والی عورت نہ نماز پڑھے گی ، نہ روزہ رکھے گی۔ پھر اس کی قضا ہوگی یا نہیں؟ تو فرمایا کہ روزوں کی قضا ہے اور نماز کی قضا نہیں ہے ، کیونکہ نمازیں بہت زیادہ ہو جائے گی اس کی قضا دشوار ہے، تو شریعت نے نماز کا اصل وجوب ہی ساقط کر دیا، اور روزوں کی قضا دشوار نہیں اس لئے روزہ کا اصل وجوب باقی رکھا، البتہ ادائیگی سے منع کر دیا، پاک ہونے کے بعد پھر اس کی قضا کر لے۔
As for menstruation and postpartum bleeding, they do not destroy legal capacity in any way, but purification from them is a condition for the validity of performing fasting and prayer. So performance is missed due to them. And in making up prayers there is hardship because of their multiplication, so the original obligation of prayer is dropped by them. And there is no hardship in making up fasting, so its original obligation is not dropped.

Translation: And in any case, menstruation and postpartum bleeding: these two do not destroy capacity in any way, but purification from them is a condition for the validity of performing fasting and prayer. So due to these two, performance will be missed. And in making up prayer there is hardship, because of the multiplication of prayers, so due to these two, the original obligation of prayer will drop. And in making up fasting there is no hardship, so the original obligation of fasting will not drop.

Explanation: The ninth impediment is menstruation and the tenth is post-partum bleeding. Menstruation and postpartum bleeding do not destroy capacity in any way, but purification from menstruation and postpartum bleeding is a condition for performing prayer and fasting. Therefore, with menstruation and postpartum bleeding, prayer and fasting cannot be performed. So a woman with menstruation or postpartum bleeding will neither pray nor fast. Then will she make up for it or not? So it is said that there is making up for fasts and no making up for prayers, because prayers will become very many, making them up is difficult. So Shariah dropped the original obligation of prayer, but left the original obligation of fasting, only prohibiting performance; after becoming pure, she should make them up.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage addresses two impediments (awarij) to legal capacity: menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The author clarifies that these do not remove the capacity (ahliyyah) itself; the woman remains a legal subject. However, the requirement of purification (tahara) as a condition for validity (shart sihha) prevents performance of prayer and fasting during these states. The key point is the distinction in obligation to make up missed acts. For prayer, due to the large number of prayers that would accumulate (each day has multiple prayers), requiring make-up would cause hardship (haraj). Therefore, Shariah completely drops the obligation (asl al-wujub) for prayer. For fasting, only a few days are missed per month, so making them up is not burdensome; hence the obligation remains, but performance is deferred until after purification. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that rulings are based on ease and removal of hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Key Terms
حیض (hayd): Menstruation, a natural biological state that prevents the validity of prayer and fasting during its occurrence.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding, treated similarly to hayd in terms of its effect on prayer and fasting.
حرج (haraj): Hardship; the criterion used to determine whether an obligation is dropped or merely postponed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason prayers are not made up by a menstruating woman?
A) Because fasting is less important than prayer.
B) Because making up many prayers would cause hardship.
C) Because prayers can only be performed in congregation.
D) Because fasting does not require purification.

Key Takeaway
Hardship (haraj) due to multiplicity leads to dropping the obligation to make up prayers for a menstruating woman, while no such hardship exists for fasting, so fasts must be made up.

Death as Pure Incapacity: Which Obligations Remain?
Explaining which obligations remain and which drop upon death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of obligations drop upon death according to the Hanafi usul principle of pure incapacity (ajz khalis) and explain why certain rights (property rights and debts) persist when supported by property or a guarantor.

Core Idea
Death removes all obligations requiring choice, but property-linked rights and debts survive if backed by assets or a guarantor.

Death is not merely the end of life but a legal event that reshapes which obligations remain. The Hanafi school classifies death as pure incapacity (ajz khalis). This lesson unpacks the reasoning: worship obligations drop because their purpose — conscious performance — is impossible, while rights tied to property persist because they don't rely on the deceased's action. Debts are more nuanced: they require either existing property or a guarantor to continue. Understanding this principle is essential for issues like inheritance, kafala, and estate planning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause (sabab) of the ruling
Recognize that death is categorized as 'ajz khalis' (pure incapacity) in Hanafi usul. This characterization drives the entire analysis of what obligations remain.
Contrast with other forms of incapacity like insanity or unconsciousness, which may be partial.
2
Separate obligations into two categories
Distinguish between obligations that are 'min bab al-taklif' (requiring conscious action and choice) and those that are not. The former drop entirely; the latter may persist.
Examples of taklif: prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj.
3
Analyze the persistence of rights: property vs. debt
Rights attached to specific property (haqq muta'allaq bi al-'ayn) survive because they depend on the property itself, not on the deceased's action. Debts (dayn) require either property left behind or a guarantor (kafil) to strengthen the liability.
The passage uses the term 'dhimma' (legal liability) which does not persist after death without support.
4
Test the principle with a counterexample
Compare with the case of a restricted slave (abd mahjur): his dhimma is complete, so a guarantee is valid even though his financial capacity is restricted. This highlights that for a deceased, the dhimma is considered 'broken' and cannot sustain a debt alone.
This counterexample refines our understanding: it's not just incapacity, but the absence of both property and a guarantor that drops the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْمَوْتُ فَإِنَّهُ عَجْزٌ خَالِصْ يَسْقُطُ بِهِ مَاهُوَ مِنْ بَابِ التَّكْلِيفِ لِفَوَاتِ غَرَضِهِ وَهُوَ الْاَدَاء عَنْ اِخْتِيَارِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا إِنَّهُ يَبْطُلُ عَنْهُ الزَّكُوةُ وَسَائِرُ وُجُوهِ الْقُرَبِ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْقَى عَلَيْهِ الْمَاثِمَ وَمَا شُرِعَ عَلَيْهِ لِحَاجَةِ غَيْرِهِ اِنْ كَانَ حَقًّا مُتَعَلَّقًا بِالْعَيْنِ يَبْقَى بِبَقَاءِهِ لِاَنَّ فِعْلَهُ فِيْهِ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ دَيْنًا لَمْ يَبْقَ بِمُجَرَّدِ الدِّمَةِ حَتَّى يَنْضَمَ إِلَيْهِ مَالٌ اَوْ مَا يُؤكَدَ بِهِ الدِّمَمُ وَهُوَ ذِمَةُ الْكَفِيْلِ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ الله اِنَّ الْكَفَالَةَ بِالدَّيْنِ عَنِ الْمَيِّتِ لَا تَصِحُ إِذَا لَمْ يُخَلِّفُ مَالًا أَوْ كَفِيْلًا كَانَ الدَّيْنَ عَنْهُ سَاقِطْ بِخِلَافِ الْعَبْدِ الْمَحْجُورِيقِرُ بالدَيْنِ فَتَكْفُل عَنْهُ رَجُلٌ تَصِحُ لِاَنَّ ذِمَتَهُ فِي حَقِهِ كَامِلَةٌ وَإِنَّمَا ضُمَتْ إِلَيْهِ الْمَالِيَهُ فِي حَقَّ الْمَوْلَى وَإِنْ كَانَ شُرِعَ عَلَيْهِ بِطَرِيْقِ الصَّلَةِ بَطَلَ إِلَّا أَنْ يُؤْصِيَ بِهِ فَيَصِحُ مِنَ الثلث

ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال موت پس وہ خالص عجز ہے، اس کی وجہ سے تمام احکام ساقط ہو جائیں گے جو تکلیف کے قبیل سے ہیں، تکلیف کی غرض کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے، اور وہ غرض اختیار سے ادا کرنا ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ میت سے زکوۃ اور عبادات کی تمام صورتیں باطل ہو جائیں گی ، اور اس پر گناہ باقی رہے گا۔ اور وہ حکم جو میت پر مشروع ہوتا ہے دوسرے کی حاجت کی وجہ سے، اگر وہ ایسا حق ہے جو عین کے ساتھ متعلق ہے، تو وہ حق باقی رہے گا عین کی بقاء کے ساتھ ، اس لئے کہ اس میں میت کا فعل مقصود نہیں ہے اور اگر وہ دین ہے تو وہ محض ذمہ کی وجہ سے باقی نہیں رہے گا، یہانتک کہ مل جائے ذمہ کے ساتھ مال یا وہ چیز جس سے ذمے مؤکد ہو جاتے ہیں، اور وہ کفیل کا ذمہ ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے امام ابوحنیفہ عالیہ نے فرمایا کہ میت کی طرف سے دین کا کفیل ہونا صحیح نہیں ہے جب کہ میت نے مال یا کفیل نہ چھوڑا ہو، گویا کہ دین اس سے ساقط ہے، برخلاف عبد مجور کے جو دین کا اقرار کرے ، پھر اس کی طرف سے کوئی شخص کفیل ہو جائے تو صحیح ہے، اس لئے کہ کفیل کا ذمہ اس کے حق میں کامل ہے، اور اس کے ذمہ کے ساتھ مولی کے حق میں مالیت ملادی جاتی ہے، اور اگر وہ حکم میت پر صلہ کے طور پر مشروع ہو تو باطل ہو جائے گا مگر یہ کہ اس کی وصیت کر دی جائے تو وہ ثلث مال سے صحیح ہو گا۔
As for death, it is pure incapacity, by which drops whatever is of the category of obligation (taklif) because its purpose is lost — and that purpose is performance by choice. For this reason we said that from him, zakah and all forms of acts of worship are void, but sin remains upon him. And whatever ruling is legislated for him due to the need of another: if it is a right attached to a specific property, it remains with the survival of that property, because his action concerning it is not intended. And if it is a debt, it does not remain by mere liability (dhimma) until there is joined to it property or something that strengthens the liability — and that is the liability of a guarantor. For this reason, Abu Hanifa said: Guarantee of a debt for the deceased is not valid if he left no property or guarantor; the debt is considered dropped from him. Contrary to a restricted slave who acknowledges a debt, then a man guarantees for him: it is valid, because his liability is complete with respect to him, and only the financial capacity is added to him with respect to the master. And if it was legislated for him by way of a gift (sila), it becomes void unless he makes a will for it, then it is valid from one-third.

Translation: And in any case death: it is pure incapacity; due to it all rulings that are of the category of obligation drop, because the purpose of obligation is lost — and that purpose is performance with choice. For this reason we said that from a deceased, zakah and all forms of worship become void, and sin remains upon him. And the ruling that is legislated for a deceased due to the need of another: if it is a right attached to a specific property, then that right will remain with the survival of the property, because his action is not intended in it. And if it is a debt, then it does not remain merely by liability until property or something that strengthens liabilities — and that is the liability of a guarantor — is joined to it. And for this reason Imam Abu Hanifa said that guarantee of a debt on behalf of a deceased is not valid when the deceased did not leave property or a guarantor; as if the debt is dropped from him. Contrary to a restricted slave who acknowledges a debt, then a person becomes a guarantor for him: it is valid because the liability of the guarantor is complete with respect to him, and financial capacity is added to it with respect to the master. And if the ruling was legislated for him as a gift, it becomes void unless he makes a will for it, then it is valid from one-third.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage explains the effects of death on various legal obligations. Death is considered absolute incapacity (ajz khalis), which removes all obligations that require choice and conscious action (taklif). Therefore, acts of worship like prayer, fasting, and zakat become void upon death; however, if they were missed intentionally, sin may remain. Rights that are tied to specific property (e.g., a pledge or specific legacy) survive because they do not depend on the deceased's action. Debts, however, do not automatically persist; they require either property left by the deceased or a guarantor who assumes liability. Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on guarantee (kafala) for a deceased person is explained: if the deceased left no assets and no prior guarantor, a post-death guarantee is invalid because the debt is considered dropped. In contrast, for a restricted slave (abd mahjur) who acknowledges a debt, a guarantee is valid because the slave's personal liability (dhimma) is intact, though his financial capacity is restricted by the master. Finally, any gift-like obligation (e.g., a voluntary bequest) is void unless explicitly willed, in which case it is executable from one-third of the estate.

Key Terms
عجز خالص (ajz khalis): Pure incapacity; death is characterized as absolute inability to perform any actions.
تکلیف (taklif): Legal obligation requiring a conscious, willing act.
ذمہ (dhimma): Legal liability or capacity, which survives death only when supported by property or a guarantor.
کفالت (kafala): Guarantee; valid only if the principal has a complete dhimma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa (as cited in the passage), why is a guarantee (kafala) for a deceased person's debt invalid if the deceased left no property or guarantor?
A) Because the deceased's sin is too great.
B) Because the debt is considered dropped from the deceased's liability.
C) Because a guarantor cannot be appointed after death.
D) Because the deceased's heirs must pay the debt first.

Key Takeaway
Death as pure incapacity voids obligations requiring conscious action, but property-linked rights and debts persist only when supported by property or a guarantor.

Effects of Hayd, Nifas, and Death on Legal Obligations
Explaining the effects of impediments on ritual obligations and debts after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule regarding the effect of temporary and permanent impediments (āriḍ) on ritual obligations and debts.

Core Idea
Hayd and nifas suspend performance but not obligation; death terminates all taklifi obligations.

This lesson explores how specific impediments (āriḍ) affect the legal capacity (ahliyya) and obligations of a mukallaf. Using the examples of hayd/nifas and death, the text demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing ease and necessity (rafʿ al-ḥaraj) in deriving rulings. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for properly applying the Sharīʿa to real-life situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impediment and its nature
Classify the impediment (āriḍ) as temporary (e.g., hayd, nifas) or permanent (e.g., death). Determine whether it nullifies legal capacity or merely suspends performance.
Hayd and nifas do not nullify capacity; death is pure incapacity.
2
Determine the category of affected rulings
Identify whether the rulings are of the category of taklīf (obligations requiring choice) or non-taklīf (e.g., rights of people attached to objects).
Taklīfi rulings are dropped by death; other rulings may persist.
3
Apply the principle of ease (rafʿ al-ḥaraj)
For temporary impediments, assess whether making up the obligation would cause undue hardship. The Lawgiver drops the obligation if hardship is severe.
Prayer is dropped due to multiplicity; fasting is not because it is manageable.
4
Distinguish rights attached to objects vs. debts
If a right is attached to a specific object (e.g., mortgaged property), it remains after death because the object itself is owed. Debts (dhimma) require property or a surety to persist in this world.
Pure dhimma without property or surety renders the debt worldly extinguished.
5
Derive practical consequences
Based on the above, state whether the obligation must be made up (qaḍā), whether sin remains, and whether debts can be collected from the estate or surety.
Example: Hayd → no qaḍā for prayer, qaḍā for fasting. Death → no worldly obligation but sin remains for missed taklīf.

Source Text
